“FEAR is the tool of a man-made devil. Self-confident faith in one’s self is both the man-made weapon which defeats this devil and the man-made tool which builds a triumphant life. And it is more than that. It is a link to the irresistible forces of the universe which stand behind a man who does not believe in failure and defeat as being anything but temporary experiences.”

“恐惧是人造恶魔的工具。一个人对自己的自信，既是击败这个魔鬼的人造武器，也是建立一个胜利生活的人造工具。不仅如此。它与宇宙不可抗拒的力量相连，这种力量支撑着一个不相信失败和失败只是暂时经历的人。”

—NAPOLEON HILL

NOTE TO READERS

读者须知

by
SHARON LECHTER

作者: sharon LECHTER

OUTWITTING THE DEVIL is the most profound book I have ever read.

战胜心魔是我读过的最深刻的书。

First, I was incredibly honored when Don Green, CEO of the Napoleon Hill Foundation, trusted me enough to ask me to become involved in this project. And then I read the manuscript! I couldn’t sleep for a week.

首先，当拿破仑山基金会的首席执行官唐 · 格林非常信任我，邀请我参与这个项目时，我感到非常荣幸。然后我读了手稿！我一个星期都睡不着觉。

Written on a manual typewriter in 1938 by the Master himself, Napoleon Hill, this manuscript had been locked away and hidden by Hill’s family for seventy-two years. Why? Because they were frightened by the response it would invoke. Hill’s courage in revealing the Devil’s work around each of us every day, in our churches, our schools, and our politics, threatened the very core of society as it was known at the time.

1938年，大师拿破仑 · 希尔亲自在一台手动打字机上写下了这份手稿，这份手稿被希尔的家人锁藏了72年。为什么？因为他们害怕它会引起的反应。希尔每天都在揭露我们周围的魔鬼的工作，在我们的教堂，我们的学校，我们的政治，这种勇气威胁到了当时社会的核心。

When asked why the family had hidden the manuscript, Don Green recites the following inside story:

当被问及为什么这家人要把手稿藏起来时，唐 · 格林说出了以下内幕:

It was the objections of Hill’s wife, Annie Lou. She was secretary to Dr. William Plumer Jacobs, president of Presbyterian College in Clinton, South Carolina. Jacobs was also owner of Jacobs Press and a public counselor to a group of South Carolina textile firms. Jacobs hired Hill to come to Clinton to work for him, and Annie Lou did not want the book published because of the role of the Devil. She feared the response from organized religion (and maybe for Hill’s job). Even though Hill died in 1970, Annie Lou did not die until 1984. Upon Annie Lou’s death, the manuscript came into the possession of Dr. Charlie Johnson, then the president of the Napoleon Hill Foundation. Charlie was the nephew of Annie Lou Hill. Charlie’s wife, Frankie, knew and shared Annie Lou’s feelings. Frankie told Charlie that she did not want the article published while she was alive either. Charlie’s wife passed away a couple of years ago and Charlie finally gave me the manuscript, bound in red leather and embossed with the letters Outwitting the Devil in gold on the cover. The Foundation believes the manuscript has a powerful message that needs to be shared.

而是希尔的妻子安妮 · 卢的反对。她是 William Plumer Jacobs 博士的秘书，William Plumer Jacobs 博士是南卡罗来纳州克林顿市长老会学院研究中心的主席。雅各布斯还是雅各布斯出版社的所有者，也是南卡罗来纳州一些纺织公司的公共顾问。雅各布斯雇希尔来克林顿为他工作，安妮卢不希望这本书出版，因为魔鬼的作用。她害怕来自有组织的宗教组织的回应(也许还有希尔的工作)。尽管希尔于1970年去世，安妮 · 卢直到1984年才去世。安妮 · 卢去世后，手稿被当时的拿破仑 · 希尔基金会主席查理 · 约翰逊博士所有。查理是安妮 · 卢 · 希尔的侄子。查理的妻子弗兰基知道并分享了安妮 · 卢的感受。弗兰基告诉查理，她也不希望这篇文章在她活着的时候发表。查理的妻子几年前去世了，查理最终把手稿给了我，手稿用红色皮革装订，封面上浮雕着金色的战胜心魔。基金会认为这份手稿有一个强有力的信息需要分享。

After speaking with Don, I was overcome with a powerful realization. This book, even though written in 1938, was actually meant to be published today . . . meant to rock our society today! It was intended to provide answers during this uncertain economic and spiritual time. It provides the keys for each of us to outwit the Devil in our own lives. It shows us how to chart a course for success and to add value to the world around us through the process.

和唐谈过之后，我有了一种强烈的领悟。这本书，虽然写于1938年，实际上是打算今天出版的... ... 意味着震撼我们今天的社会！它的目的是在这个不确定的经济和精神时期提供答案。它为我们每个人在自己的生活中智胜魔鬼提供了钥匙。它向我们展示了如何制定通往成功的道路，以及如何通过这一过程为我们周围的世界增添价值。

Just as Think and Grow Rich helped us recover and succeed after the Great Depression, Outwitting the Devil was written to help each of us recover and succeed today!

正如《思考与致富》帮助我们在大萧条后恢复并取得成功一样，《战胜心魔写的就是要帮助我们每个人在今天恢复并取得成功！

You may ask if Hill believes his conversation with the Devil was real, or was it merely imaginary? The choice is yours. But I also asked Don Green about Hill’s thoughts in his other writings to see if we could get another look inside Hill’s head. Don’s response was as follows:

你可能会问，希尔是否相信他与魔鬼的对话是真实的，还是仅仅是想象的？选择权在你。但是我也问了唐 · 格林关于希尔在其他作品中的想法，看看我们是否可以从另一个角度看希尔的大脑。唐的回答如下:

The use of imaginary conversations was not new to Hill. In 1953, Hill published How to Raise Your Own Salary, which was written as a conversation between Hill and Carnegie. Hill had actually interviewed Carnegie in 1908 and Carnegie died in 1919, well before its publication.

对希尔来说，使用想象中的谈话并不是什么新鲜事。1953年，希尔出版了《如何提高自己的薪水》 ，这本书是希尔和卡内基之间的对话。事实上，希尔在1908年曾采访过卡内基，而卡内基在1919年去世，那时候《纽约时报》还没有出版。

This was not the first time Hill used imaginary meetings to convey what he was writing about. In Think and Grow Rich, Hill, writing about the sixth sense, wrote about his imaginary council meeting with the nine men whose lifeworks had been the most impressive to Hill. These nine imaginary council members were Emerson, Paine, Edison, Darwin, Lincoln, Burbank, Napoleon, Ford, and Carnegie.

这并不是希尔第一次用虚构的会议来表达他所写的内容。在《思考与致富》一书中，希尔写到了他的第六感，描述了他想象中的与九个人的会议，这九个人的一生给希尔留下了最深刻的印象。这九个虚构的委员会成员是爱默生、潘恩、爱迪生、达尔文、林肯、伯班克、拿破仑、福特和卡内基。

Hill wrote in Think and Grow Rich that during his meetings with his “Invisible Counselors” he found his mind most receptive to ideas, thoughts, and knowledge that reached him during these times when his sixth sense was activated.

希尔在《思考致富》一书中写道，在与“看不见的顾问”会面期间，他发现自己的大脑最容易接受各种想法、思想和知识，这些都是在他的第六感被激活的那段时间里接触到的。

Outwitting the Devil was by no means his first time to write about religion. In fact, after he published Law of Success in 1928, he received letters of criticism about his stance on schools and religion. In Think and Grow Rich, in the chapter titled “The Six Ghosts of Fear,” Hill wrote that fear of death, in the majority of cases, could be charged to religious fanaticism. Hill had much to say about religious leaders in this section of his classic best seller.

战胜心魔绝不是他第一次写关于宗教的东西。事实上，在1928年他出版了《成功法则》之后，他收到了批评信，批评他在学校和宗教问题上的立场。在《思考致富》(Think and Grow Rich)一书中，希尔在题为《恐惧的六个幽灵》(The Six Ghosts of Fear)的章节中写道，在大多数情况下，对死亡的恐惧可能被归咎于宗教狂热。希尔在他的经典畅销书的这一部分对宗教领袖有很多话要说。

Hill had much to say about religion even in his Hill’s Golden Rule Magazine. He wrote an article, “A Suggestion to Ministers of the Gospel,” in which he admonished church leaders to teach their followers to practice harmony among each other.

希尔甚至在他的希尔的黄金法则杂志上也谈到了很多关于宗教的话题。他写了一篇文章，“给传福音的牧师的建议” ，在这篇文章中，他告诫教会领袖要教导他们的信徒彼此和谐相处。

So the choice is yours. Did Hill actually talk to the Devil or is this a parable created to reach and touch your heart? Hill’s unique style will pull you in and move you in ways you never thought possible. The words in this book are Hill’s own. Since the original manuscript was quite lengthy, I edited with careful precision to preserve the profound impact of his message. I have kept his original language in place even when modern grammar may have dictated adjustments.

所以选择权在你。希尔真的和魔鬼说话了吗? 或者这只是一个能触动你心灵的寓言？希尔的独特风格会吸引你，以你从未想过的方式打动你。这本书里的话是希尔自己写的。由于原稿相当长，我小心地精确地编辑，以保存他的信息的深远影响。即使在现代语法可能已经规定了调整的时候，我仍然保留了他的原始语言。

In an effort to highlight certain issues, bring clarity to his words, and show how his predictions have become realities, I have added my thoughts throughout the manuscript in a different type style. This allows you to choose to read the book either with my comments or without.

为了突出某些问题，使他的话清晰，并显示他的预测如何成为现实，我在整个手稿添加了我的想法在一个不同类型的风格。这样你就可以选择是否有我的评论来阅读这本书。

Please enjoy this powerful book and share it with your friends and family. The power in Hill’s words can and will change your life.

请享受这本强大的书，并与您的朋友和家人分享它。希尔话语中的力量可以而且将会改变你的生活。

FOREWORD

前言

DR. NAPOLEON HILL is arguably the most famous self-help action writer, thinker, évocateur, and best-selling author of all time. We ask that you refer quickly to the actual interview with the Devil. You will thus get the impact in your life of who the Devil really is and what he does to 98 percent of living beings, according to the Devil himself.

拿破仑 · 希尔博士可以说是有史以来最著名的自助动作作家、思想家、演说家和畅销书作家。我们要求你们尽快参考与魔鬼的实际面谈。因此，你将在你的生活中得到影响，魔鬼到底是谁，他对百分之九十八的生命做了什么，根据魔鬼自己。

As a thought stimulator, Hill quickly starts the book’s journey, taking us through his life and what was meaningful and life-changing to him. Hill learned the greatest and most useful and instantly helpful success principles on the planet, but he did not know how to use and easily apply them. We predict that this is true for many people still today. It is easy to say the words and sometimes even think the thoughts. It takes a profound and lasting decision to actually live by the principles daily in every way. Sharon Lechter illuminates what Hill’s words mean when transported into today’s dollars, thinking, and understanding.

作为一个思想的刺激，希尔迅速开始了书的旅程，带领我们通过他的生活和什么是有意义的，生活改变了他。希尔学到了这个星球上最伟大、最有用、立竿见影的成功法则，但他不知道如何使用它们，也不知道如何轻松应用它们。我们预测，这对今天的许多人来说仍然是正确的。说出这些话很容易，有时甚至想出这些想法。这需要一个深刻和持久的决定，以实际生活的原则，每天在各种方式。莎伦 · 莱切特阐明了希尔的话在今天的美元、思想和理解中的意义。

Dr. Hill’s goal was to communicate clearly a philosophy and practice of individual achievement that would stimulate lasting happiness. His inner knower guided him to find his own life’s rainbow.

希尔博士的目标是清楚地传达个人成就的哲学和实践，这将刺激持久的幸福。他内心的知觉引导他找到了自己生命中的彩虹。

You are being tested now in the toughest times imaginable, just as Hill was during the Depression. He felt, acted, and became depressed and despondent, an attitude that was deleterious to his very beingness, just as it is to you and your wellness. Reading this inspiring book can help you snap out of your lethargy and negative-mindedness and get you on a new and more glorious path to an ever brighter, better, and more rewarding future.

你们现在正面临着可以想象的最艰难时期的考验，就像希尔在大萧条时期一样。他感觉、行动、变得沮丧和沮丧，这种态度对他的存在是有害的，就像对你和你的健康一样。读这本鼓舞人心的书可以帮助你从你的昏昏欲睡和消极心态中振作起来，让你走上一条崭新的、更加光荣的道路，通向一个更加光明、更加美好、更加有意义的未来。

Like Hill, you are here to master your fears and not let them master you, to live passionately and with purpose, to decide what you want to be, do, and have, and to make it so.

像希尔一样，你在这里是为了控制你的恐惧，而不是让它们控制你，是为了充满激情和目标地生活，是为了决定你想要成为什么，做什么，拥有什么，并使它成为现实。

As you rediscover the marvelous and magical discoveries of Dr. Hill, you will know and believe that you can match them and surpass them if you want to, because you are unlimited. Hill correctly says, “Your only limitations are self-imposed.” This book will help you be aware that you can achieve your breakthroughs using all that he learned by interviewing the five hundred greatest living achievers.

当你重新发现希尔博士的奇妙和神奇的发现时，你会知道并相信如果你愿意，你可以赶上并超越他们，因为你是无限的。希尔正确地说: “你唯一的局限是自我强加的。”这本书将帮助你意识到，你可以实现你的突破，利用他所学到的一切，通过采访500个最伟大的成功者。

You will discover whether the Devil he interviews is real or imaginary, much like the Devil that you may personally be dealing with in your life and experience.

你会发现他采访的魔鬼是真实的还是虚构的，就像你在生活和经历中亲自面对的魔鬼一样。

—MARK VICTOR HANSEN




ー马克 · 维克多 · 汉森

MARK VICTOR HANSEN is co-creator of the #1 New York Times best-selling series Chicken Soup for The Soul® and co-author of Cracking the Millionaire Code, The One Minute Millionaire, and Cash in a Flash.

马克 · 维克多 · 汉森是《纽约时报》畅销系列书《心灵鸡汤》的联合创作者，也是《破解百万富翁密码》、《一分钟的百万富翁》和《瞬间现金》的联合作者。





Chapter One

MY FIRST MEETING WITH ANDREW CARNEGIE

第一章我与安德鲁 · 卡内基的第一次会面

FOR MORE THAN A QUARTER OF A CENTURY my major purpose has been that of isolating and organizing into a philosophy of achievement the causes of both failure and success, with the object of being helpful to others who have neither the inclination nor the opportunity to engage in this form of research.

四分之一个多世纪以来，我的主要目的一直是把失败和成功的原因孤立起来，组织成一种成就哲学，目的是帮助那些既没有兴趣也没有机会从事这种形式的研究的人。

My labor began in 1908, as the result of an interview that I had with the late Andrew Carnegie. I frankly told Mr. Carnegie that I wished to enter law school and that I had conceived the idea of paying my way through school by interviewing successful men and women, finding out how they came by their success, and writing stories of my discoveries for magazines. At the end of our first visit Mr. Carnegie asked whether or not I possessed enough courage to carry out a suggestion he wished to offer me. I replied that courage was about all I did have and that I was prepared to do my best to carry out any suggestion he cared to offer.

我的劳动始于1908年，那是我和已故的安德鲁 · 卡内基的一次面谈的结果。我坦率地告诉卡内基先生，我希望进入法学院学习，而且我构想过通过采访成功的男男女女来支付我的学费，找出他们是如何获得成功的，并为杂志撰写我的发现故事。在我们第一次访问结束时，卡内基先生问我是否有足够的勇气去执行他想给我的建议。我回答说，勇气是我所拥有的一切，我准备尽我最大的努力去执行他提出的任何建议。

He then said, “Your idea of writing stories about men and women who are successful is commendable, as far as it goes, and I have no intention of trying to discourage you from carrying out your purpose, but I must tell you that if you wish to be of enduring service, not only to those now living, but to posterity as well, you can do so if you will take the time to organize all of the causes of failure as well as all of the causes of success.

他接着说: “就目前而言，你关于写成功男女的故事的想法是值得称赞的，我无意阻止你实现你的目标，但我必须告诉你，如果你希望不仅为现在活着的人，而且也为子孙后代服务，你可以这样做，如果你愿意花时间组织失败的所有原因以及成功的所有原因。

“There are millions of people in the world who have not the slightest conception of the causes of success and failure. The schools and colleges teach practically everything except the principles of individual achievement. They require young men and women to spend from four to eight years acquiring abstract knowledge, but do not teach them what to do with this knowledge after they get it.

“世界上有数以百万计的人对成功和失败的原因毫无概念。除了个人成就原则之外，学校和大学几乎教授所有的东西。他们要求青年男女花四到八年时间学习抽象知识，但不教他们在学会之后如何处理这些知识。

“The world is in need of a practical, understandable philosophy of achievement, organized from the factual knowledge gained from the experience of men and women in the great university of life. In the entire field of philosophy I find nothing which even remotely resembles the sort of philosophy which I have in mind. We have few philosophers who are capable of teaching men and women the art of living.

”这个世界需要一种切合实际、易于理解的成就哲学，这种哲学是根据从伟大的大学生活中的男女经验中获得的实际知识组织起来的。在整个哲学领域中，我找不到任何与我心目中的哲学类似的东西。我们很少有哲学家能够教会男人和女人生活的艺术。

“It seems to me that here is an opportunity which should challenge an ambitious young man of your type; but ambition alone is not enough for this task which I have suggested. The one who undertakes it must have courage and tenacity.

”“在我看来，这是一个挑战你这种有抱负的年轻人的机会，但是单凭抱负是不足以完成我所建议的任务的。承担这一任务的人必须有勇气和毅力。

“The job will require at least twenty years of continuous effort, during which the one who undertakes it will have to earn his living from some other source, because this sort of research is never profitable at the outset, and generally those who have contributed to civilization through work of this nature have had to wait a hundred years or so after their own funerals to receive recognition for their labor.”

“这项工作至少需要20年的持续努力，在此期间，从事这项工作的人将不得不从其他来源谋生，因为这种研究从一开始就没有利润可言，通常那些通过这种性质的工作对文明作出贡献的人，不得不在他们自己的葬礼之后等待大约100年，才能获得对他们劳动的认可。”

NOTE to READERS: Sharon Lechter adds her comments in special sections like this.

读者注意: Sharon Lechter 在这样的特殊章节中添加了她的评论。

Twenty years of labor with no pay and possibly no recognition! How would you respond to this “offer”? As he discusses below, Hill accepted Carnegie’s challenge and, with a letter of introduction from Carnegie, set about interviewing the giants of that time, including Theodore Roosevelt, Thomas Edison, John D. Rockefeller, Henry Ford, Alexander Graham Bell, King Gillette (founder of the Gillette Safety Razor Company), and many others. His effort ultimately culminated in the publication of several books, including the eight-volume Law of Success and Think and Grow Rich after more than twenty-five years of research. Think and Grow Rich is widely recognized as the seminal work in self-development, introducing essentially all the principles that continue to serve as the foundation for the teachings of the personal development gurus of today. As reflected in Hill’s own description, the process of developing and publishing Think and Grow Rich was itself a study in the principles he revealed. It may be telling that the manuscript of Outwitting the Devil was written the year after Think and Grow Rich was published, since this work may reveal the frustration and revelation of Hill’s “other self” and how he conquered his frustrations and succeeded in using the very principles he described in Think and Grow Rich. Outwitting the Devil will reveal Hill’s spiritual awakening and how each of us can learn from his encounter with the Devil.

二十年的劳动，没有报酬，可能没有认可！你会如何回应这个“提议” ？希尔接受了卡内基的挑战，写了一封卡内基的介绍信，开始采访那个时代的巨人，包括西奥多·罗斯福，爱迪生，约翰·戴维森·洛克菲勒，亨利福特，亚历山大·格拉汉姆·贝尔，吉列特(吉列安全剃须刀公司的创始人) ，以及许多其他人。他的努力最终导致了几本书的出版，其中包括八卷本的《成功法则》和《思考和致富》 ，这两本书经过了25年多的研究。思考和致富被广泛认为是自我发展的开创性工作，介绍了基本上所有的原则，继续作为今天个人发展大师的教义的基础。正如希尔自己的描述所反映的那样，开发和出版《思考致富》的过程本身就是对他所揭示的原则的研究。也许可以说，战胜心魔的手稿是在《思考与致富》出版后一年写的，因为这部作品可能揭示了希尔“另一个自我”的挫折和启示，以及他如何克服挫折并成功运用他在《思考与致富》中描述的原则。战胜心魔将揭示希尔的精神觉醒，以及我们每个人如何从他与魔鬼的遭遇中学习。

“If you undertake this job, you should interview not only the few who have succeeded, but the many who have failed. You should carefully analyze many thousands of people who have been classed as ‘failures,’ and I mean by the term ‘failures,’ men and women who come to the closing chapter of life disappointed because they did not attain the goal which they had set their hearts upon achieving. As inconsistent as it may seem, you will learn more about how to succeed from the failures than you will from the so-called successes. They will teach you what not to do.

“如果你担任这份工作，你不仅应该面试少数成功者，还应该面试多数失败者。你应该仔细分析成千上万被归类为失败的人，我指的是失败这个词---- 那些走到人生最后一章的男人和女人们失望了，因为他们没有达到他们心中想要达到的目标。尽管看起来前后不一致，但相比所谓的成功，你会从失败中学到更多关于如何成功的知识。他们会教你什么是不该做的。

“Along toward the end of your labor, if you carry it through successfully, you will make a discovery which may be a great surprise to you. You will discover that the cause of success is not something separate and apart from the man; that it is a force so intangible in nature that the majority of men never recognize it; a force which might be properly called the ‘other self.’ Noteworthy is the fact that this ‘other self’ seldom exerts its influence or makes itself known excepting at times of unusual emergency, when men are forced, through adversity and temporary defeat, to change their habits and to think their way out of difficulty.

“在你的劳动即将结束的时候，如果你成功地完成了它，你将会有一个发现，这可能会给你带来巨大的惊喜。你会发现成功的原因并不是某种独立于人的东西; 它是一种无形的力量，大多数人从来不承认它; 一种可以恰当地称之为‘另一个自我’的力量值得注意的是，这个“他者自我”很少发挥其影响力，或者在非常紧急的时刻，当人们被迫，通过逆境和暂时的失败，改变他们的习惯和思考他们摆脱困境的方法时，这个“他者自我”很少显露出来。

“My experience has taught me that a man is never quite so near success as when that which he calls ‘failure’ has overtaken him, for it is on occasions of this sort that he is forced to think. If he thinks accurately, and with persistence, he discovers that so-called failure usually is nothing more than a signal to re-arm himself with a new plan or purpose. Most real failures are due to limitations which men set up in their own minds. If they had the courage to go one step further, they would discover their error.”

“我的经验告诉我，一个人最接近成功的时候，就是他所谓的‘失败’占据他的时候，因为在这种情况下，他不得不思考。如果他思维准确，坚持不懈，他就会发现，所谓的失败通常只不过是一个信号，让他重新武装自己，制定新的计划或目标。大多数真正的失败是由于人们在自己的头脑中设置的限制。如果他们有勇气更进一步，他们就会发现自己的错误。”

“Most real failures are due to limitations which men set up in their own minds.”

“大多数真正的失败都是由于人们在自己的头脑中设置的局限性。”

A negative mind-set and self-doubt can be the primary obstacle to success. With the current economic downturn, far too many people who have, all their life, done everything right are now, for the first time, facing severe economic adversity. The greatest barrier to their recovery is their own fear and self-doubt instilled by their recent experience. Have you allowed the current economic downturn to overtake you? Have self-doubt and self-sabotage held you back from reaching your dreams? Are you your own worst enemy? In Think and Grow Rich, Hill told the story of R.U. Darby, a gold prospector. Frustrated when a rich vein of gold apparently ran out, Darby sold his gold claim for a pittance to the town junkman. The junkman brought in the right expert advisers and found that Darby would have rediscovered the vein—had he moved his digging by a mere three feet. Had Darby persevered he would have made his fortune, but he gave up and abandoned his dreams—when he was only three feet from gold. Rather than being crushed by his error, Darby learned from his experience and went on to build an insurance empire. Will you abandon your quest just before reaching great success, when you are only three feet from gold? (You can read how many of today’s icons persevered through difficult situations in the book Three Feet from Gold.)

消极的心态和自我怀疑可能是成功的主要障碍。在当前经济低迷的情况下，太多人一生中所做的一切都是正确的，但现在却第一次面临严重的经济困境。他们康复的最大障碍是他们最近的经历灌输给他们的恐惧和自我怀疑。你是否听任当前的经济衰退超过你？是否自我怀疑和自我毁灭阻碍了你实现梦想？你是你自己最大的敌人吗？在《思考致富》一书中，希尔讲述了一位淘金者 r.u. 达比的故事。当一个金矿显然已经枯竭时，达比非常沮丧，他把自己的金矿卖给了城里的一个破烂工人。收废品的人找来了合适的专家顾问，发现如果达比把挖掘地点移动三英尺的话，他可能会重新发现矿脉。如果达比坚持下去，他会发财的，但他放弃了，放弃了自己的梦想——当时他离金子只有三英尺远。达比没有被自己的错误击垮，而是从自己的经历中吸取教训，继续建立了一个保险帝国。当你离金子只有三英尺的时候，你会在即将获得巨大成功的时候放弃你的追求吗？(你可以在《距离金子三英尺》一书中读到，今天有多少偶像人物在困境中坚持不懈。)

Begin Life Anew

重新开始生活

Mr. Carnegie’s speech reshaped my entire life and planted in my mind a burning purpose, which has driven me ceaselessly, and this despite the fact that I had but a vague idea as to what he meant by the term “other self.”

卡内基先生的演讲重塑了我的整个人生，在我的脑海中植入了一个燃烧的目标，这个目标不停地驱使着我，尽管我对他所说的“他者自我”只有一个模糊的概念

During my labor of research into the causes of failure and success I have had the privilege of analyzing more than 25,000 men and women who were rated as “failures,” and over 500 who were classed as “successful.” Many years ago I caught my first glimpse of that “other self” Mr. Carnegie had mentioned. The discovery came, as he said it would, as the result of two major turning-points of my life, which constituted emergencies that forced me to think my way out of difficulties such as I had never before experienced.

在我研究成功和失败的原因的过程中，我有幸分析了超过25000名被评为“失败者”的男女，以及超过500名被评为“成功者”的男女许多年前，我第一次瞥见了卡内基先生提到的“另一个自我”。正如他所说，这个发现是我人生中两个重大转折点的结果，这两个转折点构成了迫使我思考如何摆脱以前从未经历过的困难的紧急情况。

I wish it were possible to describe this discovery without the use of the personal pronoun, but this is impossible because it came through personal experiences from which it cannot be separated. To give you the complete picture I shall have to go back to the first of these two major turning-points and bring you up to the discovery step by step.

我希望没有人称代词的帮助也能描述这个发现，但这是不可能的，因为它来自于个人经历，无法与之分离。为了给你们一个完整的画面，我必须回到这两个主要转折点中的第一个，一步一步地带你们进入这个发现。

The research necessary for the accumulation of the data, from which the seventeen principles of achievement and the thirty major causes of failure were organized, required years of labor.

为了积累必要的研究数据，从这些数据中组织出成就的十七个原则和失败的三十个主要原因，需要多年的劳动。

I had reached the false conclusion that my task of organizing a complete philosophy of personal achievement had been completed. Far from having been completed, my work had merely begun. I had erected the skeleton of a philosophy by organizing the seventeen principles of achievement and the thirty major causes of failure, but that skeleton had to be covered with the flesh of application and experience. Moreover, it had to be given a soul through which it might inspire men and women to meet obstacles without going down under them.

我得出了一个错误的结论，认为我组织一个完整的个人成就哲学的任务已经完成了。我的工作远远没有完成，只是刚刚开始。我已经通过组织成就的十七个原则和失败的三十个主要原因，树立了一个哲学的框架，但是这个框架必须被应用和经验的肉体所覆盖。此外，还必须赋予它一个灵魂，通过这个灵魂，它可以激励男人和女人遇到障碍，而不是倒在障碍之下。

The “soul,” which had yet to be added, as I discovered later, became available only after my “other self” made its appearance, through two major turning-points of my life.

我后来发现，“灵魂”还没有加进去，只有在我的“另一个自我”出现之后，通过我生命中的两个主要转折点，它才变得可用。

Resolving to turn my attention, and whatever talents I might possess, into monetary returns through business and professional channels, I decided to go into the profession of advertising, and I became the advertising manager of the LaSalle Extension University of Chicago. Everything went along beautifully for one year, at the end of which I was seized by a violent dislike for my job and resigned.

我决心通过商业和专业渠道，将我的注意力和才能转化为金钱回报，我决定进入广告行业，我成为了芝加哥拉萨尔扩展大学的广告经理。整整一年，一切都进行得很顺利，最后我对自己的工作产生了强烈的厌恶感，辞职了。

I then entered the chain store business, with the former president of the LaSalle Extension University, and became the president of the Betsy Ross Candy Company. Unfortunate—or what seemed to me at the time to be unfortunate—disagreements with business associates disengaged me from that undertaking.

后来，我和拉塞尔扩展大学的前任校长一起进入了连锁店行业，并成为了贝琪 · 罗斯糖果公司的总裁。不幸的是——或者在当时看来是不幸的——与生意伙伴的分歧使我无法从事这项工作。

The lure of advertising still was in my blood, and I tried again to give expression to it by organizing a school of advertising and salesmanship, as a part of Bryant & Stratton Business College.

广告的诱惑仍然在我的血液里，我再次试图通过组织一个广告和推销学校来表达它，作为 Bryant & Stratton 商学院的一部分。

The enterprise was sailing smoothly and we were making money rapidly when the United States entered World War I. In response to an inner urge which no words can describe, I walked away from the school and entered the service of the United States government, under President Woodrow Wilson’s personal direction, leaving a perfectly sound business to disintegrate.

当美国参加第一次世界大战时，我们的事业进展顺利，而且赚钱很快。为了回应一种无法用语言来形容的内心冲动，我离开了学校，在伍德罗 · 威尔逊总统的亲自指导下为美国政府服务，留下了一个完全健全的企业等待瓦解。

On Armistice Day 1918, I began the publication of The Golden Rule magazine. Despite the fact that I did not have a penny of capital, the magazine grew rapidly and soon gained a nation-wide circulation of nearly half a million, ending its first year’s business with a profit of $3,156.

在1918年的停战纪念日，我开始出版《黄金法则》杂志。尽管我没有一分钱的资金，但这份杂志发展迅速，很快在全国范围内发行了近50万份，第一年的利润为3156美元。

For a proper perspective, $3,156 in 1918 would represent $45,000 today based on the Consumer Price Index average for each year compiled by the U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics and $202,000 using the nominal GDP per capita tables. Not a bad profit for a first year in the magazine business . . . when 80 to 90 percent of new titles fail and even the successful ones take three to five years to become profitable

根据美国劳工统计局编制的每年消费者价格指数平均值计算，1918年的3156美元相当于今天的45000美元，按照人均名义 GDP 表计算，相当于202000美元。对于杂志业的第一年来说，这是一个不错的利润... ... 当80% 到90% 的新杂志倒闭，即使是成功的杂志也需要3到5年才能盈利

(http://www.magazinepublisher.com/startup.html).

( http://www.magazinepublisher.com/startup.html ).

Some years later I learned, from an experienced publisher, that no man experienced in the publication and distribution of national magazines would think of starting such a magazine with less than half a million dollars of capital.

几年后，我从一位经验丰富的出版商那里了解到，在出版和发行全国性杂志方面经验丰富的人都不会想到用不到50万美元的资金创办这样的杂志。

The Golden Rule magazine and I were destined to part company. The more we succeeded the more discontented I became, until finally, due to an accumulation of petty annoyances caused by business associates, I made them a present of the magazine and stepped out. Through that move perhaps I tossed a small fortune over my shoulder.

黄金法则》杂志和我注定要分道扬镳。我们越是成功，我就越是不满，直到最后，由于生意伙伴带来的琐碎烦恼，我把他们作为杂志的礼物，走了出去。通过这一步，也许我把一小笔财富抛在了肩膀上。

This was only the beginning of Hill’s love for magazines. The Golden Rule was followed by his publication of The Napoleon Hill Magazine. Later in life he became the editor of SUCCESS, a magazine that is still published today.

这仅仅是希尔喜欢杂志的开始。金科玉律之后，他出版了《拿破仑 · 希尔杂志》。后来，他成为了《成功》杂志的编辑，这本杂志至今仍在出版。

Next I organized a training school for salesmen. My first assignment was to train a sales army of 3,000 people for a chain store company, for which I received $10 for each salesman who went through my classes. Within six months my work had netted me a little over $30,000. Success, as far as money was concerned, was crowning my efforts with abundance. Again I became “fidgety” inside. I was not happy. It became more obvious every day that no amount of money would ever make me happy.

接下来我组织了一个销售人员培训学校。我的第一项任务是为一家连锁店公司培训一支3000人的销售大军，每个上过我课的销售员可以得到10美元。不到六个月，我的工作就为我带来了3万多美元的收入。就金钱而言，成功是我努力的最高点。我的内心再一次变得“烦躁不安”。我并不快乐。越来越明显的是，再多的钱也不能让我快乐。

Without the slightest reasonable excuse for my actions, I stepped out and gave up a business from which I might easily have earned a healthy salary. My friends and business associates thought I was crazy, and they were not backward about saying so.

没有任何合理的理由来为我的行为辩解，我走出去，放弃了一个我本来可以轻松赚到一份健康薪水的生意。我的朋友和生意伙伴们都认为我疯了，他们并不回避这样说。

Frankly, I was inclined to agree with them, but there seemed nothing I could do about it. I was seeking happiness and I had not found it. At least that is the only explanation I could offer for my unusual actions. What man really knows himself?

坦白地说，我倾向于同意他们的观点，但是我似乎对此无能为力。我一直在寻找幸福，却没有找到。至少这是我对自己不寻常行为的唯一解释。什么人真正了解自己？

“Again I became ‘fidgety’ inside. I was not happy. It became more obvious every day that no amount of money would ever make me happy.”

“我的内心再一次变得‘烦躁不安’。我并不快乐。越来越明显的是，再多的钱也不能让我快乐。”

I could have written this about myself a few years ago. But when I took action by leaving a situation that, although financially rewarding, was no longer aligned with my personal mission, new doors of opportunity opened for me. It turned out to be the best decision of my professional life. Can you think of a time in your life when you made a difficult decision . . . but knew it was the right one even when others questioned you?

几年前我就可以这样写我自己了。但是，当我采取行动，离开一个虽然在经济上有回报，但不再符合我个人使命的环境时，新的机会之门为我打开了。这是我职业生涯中最好的决定。你能想起你生命中的某个时刻，当你做出一个艰难的决定时... ... 即使别人质疑你，你也知道这是正确的决定吗？

That was during the late fall of 1923. I found myself stranded in Columbus, Ohio, without funds, and worse still, without a plan by which to work my way out of my difficulty. It was the first time in my life that I had actually been stranded because of lack of funds.

那是在1923年的深秋。我发现自己被困在俄亥俄州的哥伦布市，没有资金，更糟糕的是，没有一个解决困难的计划。这是我有生以来第一次因为资金短缺而陷入困境。

Many times previously I had found money to be rather shy, but never before had I failed to get what I needed for my personal conveniences. The experience stunned me. I seemed totally at sea as to what I could or should do.

以前很多时候，我发现金钱是相当害羞的，但以前从来没有我没有得到我需要的个人便利。这一经历让我大吃一惊。我似乎完全不知道自己能做什么或应该做什么。

I thought of a dozen plans by which I might solve my problem, but dismissed them all as being either impractical or impossible of achievement. I felt like one who was lost in a jungle without a compass. Every attempt I made to work my way out brought me back to the original starting point.

我想到了一大堆可以解决问题的计划，但都被认为是不切实际或者不可能完成的。我觉得自己就像一个迷失在丛林中的人，没有指南针。每一次我试图走出困境的尝试都把我带回到了最初的起点。

For nearly two months I suffered with the worst of all human ailments: indecision. I knew the seventeen principles of personal achievement, but what I did not know was how to apply them! Without knowing it I was facing one of those emergencies of life through which, Mr. Carnegie had told me, men sometimes discover their “other selves.”

在将近两个月的时间里，我忍受着人类最严重的疾病: 优柔寡断。我知道个人成就的十七个原则，但是我不知道如何应用它们！卡耐基先生曾告诉我，在不知不觉中，我正面临着生活中的一个紧急情况，在这种情况下，人们有时会发现他们的“另一个自我”

My distress was so great that it never occurred to me to sit down and analyze its cause and seek its cure.

我的痛苦是如此之大，以至于我从来没有想过坐下来分析它的原因，寻找它的治疗方法。

“The worst of all human ailments: indecision.”

“所有人类疾病中最糟糕的是: 优柔寡断。”

Have you ever felt paralyzed by indecision? This was the first major turning point in Napoleon Hill’s life. His moving from job to job, seeking contentment and his own ideal professional life, sounds like many people today . . . people who are seeking contentment in their jobs and lives. Hill’s predicament was, by his own admission, self-inflicted. However, he found himself in very much the same circumstances as someone today who has been negatively affected by the present economic situation. Hill took advantage of his temporary defeat, using it as a spur to force himself into thought and analysis—to find his “other self.” If you have been dealt a blow by economic circumstances, you too can use it as a lever and motivation to find your “other self.”

你有没有因为犹豫不决而感到无能为力？这是拿破仑 · 希尔生命中的第一个重大转折点。他从一份工作跳到另一份工作，寻求满足感和他自己理想的职业生活，听起来像今天的许多人... 那些在工作和生活中寻求满足感的人。希尔承认，他的困境是自己造成的。然而，他发现自己与今天受到当前经济形势负面影响的人处境非常相似。希尔利用自己暂时的失败，把它作为一种刺激，强迫自己进行思考和分析，找到自己的“另一个自我”如果你受到了经济环境的打击，你也可以把它作为一个杠杆和动力去寻找你的“另一个自我”

Defeat Is Converted into Victory

失败转化为胜利

One afternoon I reached a decision through which I found the way out of my difficulty. I had a feeling that I wanted to get out into the “open spaces” of the country, where I could get a breath of fresh air and think.

一天下午，我做出了一个决定，通过这个决定，我找到了摆脱困境的办法。我有一种感觉，我想到乡下的“开放空间”去，在那里我可以呼吸到新鲜的空气，并且思考。

I began to walk, and had gone seven or eight miles when I felt myself brought suddenly to a standstill. For several minutes I stood there as if I had been glued to my tracks. Everything around me went dark. I could hear the loud sound of some form of energy which was vibrating at a very high rate.

我开始走路，走了七八英里后，突然觉得自己停住了。我在那儿站了好几分钟，好像被自己的足迹粘住了似的。我周围的一切都陷入了黑暗。我能听到某种形式的能量的巨大声响，它正在以非常高的频率振动。

Then my nerves became quiet, my muscles relaxed, and a great calmness came over me. The atmosphere began to clear, and as it did so, I received a command from within which came in the form of a thought, as near as I can describe it.

然后我的神经变得安静了，我的肌肉放松了，一种巨大的平静笼罩着我。气氛开始变得清晰起来，当它这样做的时候，我收到了来自内心的一个命令，这个命令以一种思想的形式出现，这是我所能描述的最接近它的形式。

The command was so clear and distinct that I could not misunderstand it. In substance it said, “The time has come for you to complete the philosophy of achievement which you began at Carnegie’s suggestion. Go back home at once and begin transferring the data you have gathered from your own mind to written manuscripts.” My “other self” had awakened.

这个命令非常清楚明白，我不会误解。实质上，它说: “现在是你完成你在卡内基的建议下开始的成就哲学的时候了。马上回家，开始把你从自己脑子里收集到的数据转移到书面手稿上。”我的“另一个自我”已经觉醒。

For a few minutes I was frightened. The experience was unlike any I had ever undergone before. I turned and walked rapidly until I reached home. As I approached the house, I saw my three little boys looking out of a window of our house at our neighbor’s children, who were dressing a Christmas tree in the house next door.

有那么几分钟，我感到害怕。这次经历与我以前经历过的任何一次都不同。我转身快步走回家。当我走近房子时，我看见我的三个小男孩从我们家的窗户向外看着我们邻居的孩子们，他们正在隔壁的房子里装饰圣诞树。

Then I recalled that it was Christmas Eve. Moreover, I recalled, with a feeling of deep distress such as I had never known before, that there would be no Christmas tree at our house. The look of disappointment on the faces of my children reminded me painfully of that fact.

然后我想起那天是平安夜。此外，我带着一种前所未有的极度痛苦的心情回忆说，我们家将没有圣诞树了。孩子们脸上失望的表情使我痛苦地想起了这个事实。

I went into the house, sat down at my typewriter, and began at once to reduce to writing the discoveries I had made concerning the causes of success and failure. As I placed the first sheet of paper in the typewriter I was interrupted by that same strange feeling which had come over me out in the country a few hours before, and this thought flashed into my mind:

我走进屋子，坐在打字机前，立刻开始写我所发现的成功和失败的原因。当我把第一张纸放进打字机时，我被几个小时前在乡下的那种奇怪的感觉打断了，这种想法闪现在我的脑海里:

“Your mission in life is to complete the world’s first philosophy of individual achievement. You have been trying in vain to escape your task, each effort having brought you failure. You are seeking happiness. Learn this lesson, once and forever, that you will find happiness only by helping others to find it! You have been a stubborn student. You had to be cured of your stubbornness through disappointment. Within a few years from now the whole world will start through an experience which will place millions of people in need of the philosophy which you have been directed to complete. Your big opportunity to find happiness by rendering useful service will have come. Go to work, and do not stop until you have completed and published the manuscripts which you have begun.”

“你人生的使命是完成世界上第一个个人成就的哲学。你一直徒劳地试图逃避你的任务，每一次努力都带给你失败。你在寻找幸福。学习这一课，一次并且永远，你会发现幸福只有通过帮助别人找到它！你一直是个固执的学生。你必须通过失望来治愈你的固执。从现在开始的几年内，整个世界将开始通过一个经验，这将使数以百万计的人需要的哲学，你已经被指示完成。你通过提供有用的服务来寻找幸福的大好机会将会到来。开始工作，不要停止，直到你完成并出版了你已经开始的手稿。”

I was conscious of having arrived, at last, at the end of life’s rainbow, and I was happy!

我意识到我终于到达了生命的彩虹的尽头，我很高兴！

Doubt Makes Its Appearance

怀疑出现

The “spell,” if the experience may be so called, passed away. I began to write. Shortly thereafter my “reason” suggested to me that I was embarking upon a fool’s mission. The idea of a man who was down and almost out presuming to write a philosophy of personal achievement seemed so ludicrous that I laughed hilariously, perhaps scornfully.

如果这种经历可以这样称呼的话，“咒语”已经过去了。我开始写作。此后不久，我的“理性”告诉我，我正在从事一项愚蠢的任务。一个人穷困潦倒，几乎不敢自信地写出一本关于个人成就的哲学著作，这种想法似乎是如此荒唐可笑，以至于我开怀大笑，或许还带着轻蔑的神情。

I squirmed in my chair, ran my fingers through my hair, and tried to create an alibi that would justify me in my own mind in taking the sheet of paper out of my typewriter before I had really begun to write, but the urge to continue was stronger than the desire to quit. I became reconciled to my task and went ahead.

我在椅子上扭动着身子，用手指梳理着头发，试图在我还没真正开始写作的时候，从打字机里拿出一张纸，在我自己的脑海里为自己创造一个托辞，但是继续写作的欲望比放弃的欲望更强烈。我接受了我的任务，继续前进。

“The urge to continue was stronger than the desire to quit.”

“继续的欲望比放弃的欲望更强烈。”

Remember that time when you wanted to quit, but something drove you to keep going? It may have been your “other self.”

还记得那次你想放弃，但是有什么东西驱使你继续前进吗？可能是你的“另一个自我”

Looking backward now, in the light of all that has happened, I can see that those minor experiences of adversity through which I had passed were among the most fortunate and profitable of all of my experiences. They were blessings in disguise because they forced me to continue a work which finally brought me an opportunity to make myself more useful to the world than I might have been had I succeeded in any previous plan or purpose.

现在，鉴于已经发生的一切，我可以看到，我所经历的那些微不足道的逆境经历，是我所有经历中最幸运和最有益的回顾。它们是伪装的祝福，因为它们迫使我继续一项工作，这项工作最终给了我一个机会，使我自己对世界更有用，如果我在以前的任何计划或目标中成功的话，我可能会得到这样的机会。

For almost three months I worked on those manuscripts, completing them during the early part of 1924. As soon as they had been completed, I felt myself again being lured by the desire to get back into the great American game of business.

我花了将近三个月的时间写这些手稿，并在1924年初完成了它们。他们一完成，我就觉得自己又被重新回到美国商业游戏的欲望所吸引。

Succumbing to the lure, I purchased the Metropolitan Business College in Cleveland, Ohio, and began to lay plans for increasing its capacity. By the end of 1924 we had developed and expanded, by adding new courses, until we were doing a business nearly double the best previous record the school had ever known.

在这种诱惑下，我买下了俄亥俄州克利夫兰市的大都会商学院(Metropolitan Business College) ，并开始制定增加其容量的计划。到1924年底，我们通过增加新的课程来发展和扩大，直到我们的业务几乎是学校以往最好记录的两倍。

Again the germ of discontentment began to make itself felt in my blood. Again I knew that I could not find happiness in that sort of endeavor. I turned the business over to my associates and went on the lecture platform, lecturing on the philosophy of achievement, to the organization of which I had devoted so many of my previous years.

我的血液里又开始感到不满足的萌芽。我再一次意识到，在这样的努力中我找不到幸福。我把生意交给了我的同事，走上讲台，就成就哲学进行演讲，为我前几年投入了如此多时间的组织工作。

One night I was booked to lecture in Canton, Ohio. Fate, or whatever it is that seems sometimes to shape the destiny of men, no matter how hard they may try to battle against it, again stepped into the picture and brought me face to face with a painful experience.

一天晚上，我被安排到俄亥俄州的坎顿去演讲。命运，或者不管是什么，有时似乎塑造了人类的命运，不管他们多么努力地与之抗争，再次出现在画面中，让我面对一段痛苦的经历。

In my Canton audience sat Don R. Mellett, publisher of the Canton Daily News. Mr. Mellett became so thoroughly interested in the philosophy of individual achievement on which I lectured that night that he invited me to come to see him the following day.

我在广州的听众里坐着唐 · r · 梅利特，他是《广州日报》的出版人。梅利特先生对我那天晚上演讲的个人成就哲学非常感兴趣，他邀请我第二天去看他。

That visit resulted in a partnership agreement which was to have taken place on the first of the following January when Mr. Mellett planned to resign as publisher of the Daily News, to take charge of the business and publishing of the philosophy on which I had been working.

这次访问促成了一项合伙协议，该协议原定于次年1月1日签订，当时梅利特先生计划辞去《每日新闻》出版人的职务，负责我一直致力于的商业和出版哲学。

However, in July 1926, Mr. Mellett was murdered by Pat McDermott, an underworld character, and a Canton, Ohio, policeman, both of whom were sentenced to life imprisonment. He was murdered because he was exposing in his newspaper a hook-up between the bootleggers and certain members of the Canton police force. The crime was one of the most shocking that the prohibition era produced.

然而，在1926年7月，Mellett 先生被 Pat McDermott 谋杀，一个黑社会性质，和一个坎顿，俄亥俄州，警察，他们都被判处无期徒刑。他之所以被谋杀，是因为他在报纸上揭露了走私贩和某些广州警察之间的勾结。这起犯罪是禁酒时代产生的最令人震惊的案件之一。

The July 1926 murder of crusading journalist Donald Ring Mellett, the editor of the Canton, Ohio, Daily News, was one of the most publicized crimes in the 1920s. In 1925 Mellett had discovered widespread corruption within the Canton police force and embarked on an anti-vice, anti-corruption editorial campaign, targeting, among others, the Canton police chief. Hill was reported to have asked Ohio’s governor to initiate an investigation of the corruption, a detail not reflected in Hill’s account.

1926年7月，《俄亥俄州坎顿每日新闻报》的编辑唐纳德 · 林 · 梅利特被谋杀，这是20世纪20年代最广为人知的罪行之一。1925年，梅利特发现了广州警察队伍中普遍存在的腐败现象，并开展了一场反腐败、反腐败的编辑运动，其目标包括广州警察局长。据报道，希尔已经要求俄亥俄州州长启动对腐败的调查，希尔的描述中没有反映这一细节。

Local underworld figures and at least one Canton police officer hired Patrick McDermott, an ex-con from Pennsylvania, to silence Mellett. Mellett was gunned down outside his home. As the story goes, gunmen were also lying in wait for Hill, but a fortuitous automotive breakdown kept him out of their way. On July 17, the New York Times reported in an article titled “More Death Threats Follow the Slaying of Canton Editor” that the citizens of Canton “are terror-stricken by threats of further killings by the rulers of the gamblers, bootleggers and other criminals.” As recounted by Hill, after hearing of Mellett’s murder and receiving an anonymous warning to get out of town, he fled to West Virginia. In large part due to the work of a private detective hired by the Stark County prosecutor, McDermott, two local gangsters, and a former police detective were ultimately convicted of Mellett’s murder.

当地黑社会人物和至少一名广州警察雇佣了帕特里克 · 麦克德莫特，一个来自宾夕法尼亚州的前科犯，让梅莱特闭嘴。梅利特在家门口被枪杀。随着故事的发展，持枪歹徒也在埋伏等待希尔，但一个偶然的汽车故障使他远离他们的方式。7月17日，《纽约时报》在一篇题为《广州编辑被杀之后更多的死亡威胁》的文章中报道说，广州市民“受到赌徒、走私贩和其他罪犯的统治者进一步杀人的威胁的恐怖打击。”根据希尔的叙述，在听到梅利特被谋杀的消息并接到匿名警告让他离开小镇后，他逃到了西弗吉尼亚州。在很大程度上，由于斯塔克县检察官雇佣的一名私家侦探的工作，麦克德莫特、两名当地黑帮成员和一名前警察侦探最终被判谋杀了梅莱特。

Chance (?) Saves My Life

机会救了我的命

The morning after Mr. Mellett’s death I was called on the telephone and put on notice, by some unknown person, that I had one hour in which to get out of Canton; that I could go voluntarily within the hour, but if I waited longer I probably would go in a pine box. My business association with Mr. Mellett had apparently been misunderstood. His murderers evidently believed I was directly connected with the exposé he was making in his newspapers.

梅利特先生死后的第二天早上，我接到了一个陌生人的电话，他告诉我，我有一个小时的时间离开坎顿，我可以在一个小时内自愿离开，但是如果我再等下去，我可能会被装进一个松木棺材里。我和梅利特先生的生意往来显然被误解了。他的凶手显然认为我与他在报纸上曝光的事件有直接关系。

I did not wait for the one hour time limit to expire, but immediately got into my automobile and drove down to the home of relatives in the mountains of West Virginia, where I remained until the murderers had been placed in jail.

我没有等到一个小时的时限到期，而是立刻钻进我的汽车，驱车前往位于西弗吉尼亚山区的亲戚家，在那里我一直呆到杀人犯被关进监狱。

That experience came well within the category described by Mr. Carnegie as an “emergency” that forces men to think. For the first time in my life I knew the pain of constant fear. My experience of a few years before, in Columbus, had filled my mind with doubt and temporary indecision, but this one had filled it with a fear which I seemed unable to remove. During the time that I was in hiding I seldom left the house at night, and when I did step out I kept my hand on an automatic pistol in my coat pocket, with the safety catch unlatched for immediate action. If a strange automobile stopped in front of the house where I was hiding, I went into the basement and carefully scrutinized its occupants through the basement windows.

这种经历完全符合卡内基先生所描述的那种迫使人们思考的“紧急情况”。我生平第一次体会到了持续恐惧带来的痛苦。几年前，我在哥伦布的经历使我心中充满了怀疑和暂时的优柔寡断，但这一次，我心中充满了恐惧，似乎无法消除。在我躲藏的那段时间里，我很少在晚上离开家，当我真的走出家门的时候，我总是把手放在外套口袋里的一把自动手枪上，保险栓松开以便立即采取行动。如果一辆陌生的汽车停在我藏身的房子前面，我就会走进地下室，透过地下室的窗户仔细观察车里的人。

After some months of this sort of experience, my nerves began to crack. My courage had completely left me. The ambition which had heartened me during the long years of labor in my search for the causes of failure and success also had departed.

经过几个月的这种经历后，我的神经开始崩溃。我的勇气完全消失了。在我多年的努力寻找失败和成功的原因的过程中，曾经鼓舞我的雄心壮志也已经消失了。

Slowly, step by step, I felt myself slipping into a state of lethargy from which I was afraid I should never be able to emerge. The feeling must have been closely akin to that experienced by one who suddenly steps into quicksand and realizes that every effort to extricate himself carries him just so much deeper. Fear is a self-generating morass.

慢慢地，一步一步地，我觉得自己进入了一种昏昏欲睡的状态，我害怕自己永远无法从这种状态中苏醒过来。这种感觉一定非常类似于一个人突然踏入流沙，意识到每一次想要解脱自己的努力都会把自己带得更深。恐惧是一个自我生成的沼泽。

If the seed of insanity had been in my make-up, surely it would have germinated during those months of living death. Foolish indecision, irresolute dreams, doubt and fear were my mind’s concern, day and night.

如果精神错乱的种子已经在我的化妆中，它一定会在那几个月的活死人生活中发芽。愚蠢的犹豫不决，优柔寡断的梦想，怀疑和恐惧是我日夜关心的问题。

The “emergency” I faced was disastrous in two ways. First, the very nature of it kept me in a constant state of indecision and fear. Secondly, the forced concealment kept me in idleness, with its attendant heaviness of time, which I naturally devoted to worry.

我所面临的“紧急情况”在两方面都是灾难性的。首先，它的本质使我一直处于优柔寡断和恐惧的状态。其次，强迫性的隐瞒使我无所事事，随之而来的是时间的沉重，我自然而然地专注于担忧。

My reasoning faculty had almost been paralyzed. I realized that I had to work myself out of this state of mind. But how? The resourcefulness which had helped me to meet all previous emergencies seemed to have completely taken wing, leaving me helpless.

我的推理能力几乎瘫痪了。我意识到我必须努力摆脱这种心理状态。但是怎么做呢？帮助我应付以前所有紧急情况的足智多谋似乎完全展翅高飞了，使我无能为力。

Out of my difficulties, which were burdensome enough up to this point, grew another which seemed more painful than all the others combined. It was the realization that I had spent the better portion of my past years in chasing a rainbow, searching hither and yon for the causes of success, and finding myself now more helpless than any of the 25,000 people whom I had judged as being “failures.”

我的困难到目前为止已经够麻烦的了，现在又出现了一个似乎比所有其他困难加起来还要痛苦的问题。我意识到，我过去几年的大部分时间都在追逐彩虹，四处寻找成功的原因，现在我发现自己比那25000个我认为是“失败者”中的任何一个都更加无助

This thought was almost maddening. Moreover, it was extremely humiliating, because I had been lecturing all over the country, in schools and colleges and before business organizations, presuming to tell other people how to apply the seventeen principles of success, while here I was, unable to apply them myself. I was sure that I never could again face the world with a feeling of confidence.

这种想法简直令人发狂。此外，这是极其羞辱的，因为我一直在全国各地演讲，在学校、大学和商业组织，擅自告诉别人如何应用成功的十七个原则，而在这里，我自己却无法应用它们。我确信我再也不能带着自信面对这个世界了。

Every time I looked at myself in a mirror I noticed an expression of self-contempt on my face, and not infrequently I did say things to the man in the mirror which are not printable. I had begun to place myself in the category of charlatans who offer others a remedy for failure which they themselves cannot successfully apply.

每次我对着镜子看自己的时候，我注意到自己脸上有一种自卑的表情，而且我经常对着镜子里的那个人说一些不能打印出来的话。我已经开始把自己归入江湖骗子的一类，他们为别人提供一种他们自己无法成功应用的失败补救办法。

The criminals who had murdered Mr. Mellett had been tried and sent to the penitentiary for life; therefore, it was perfectly safe, as far as they were concerned, for me to come out of hiding and again take up my work. I could not come out, however, because now I faced circumstances more frightful than the criminals who had sent me into hiding.

谋杀梅利特先生的罪犯已经受到审判，并被送进监狱终身监禁; 因此，就他们而言，我走出藏身之处，重新开始我的工作是绝对安全的。然而，我不能出来，因为我现在面临的情况比那些把我送到隐蔽处的罪犯更可怕。

The experience had destroyed whatever initiative I had possessed. I felt myself in the clutches of some depressing influence which seemed like a nightmare. I was alive; I could move around, but I could not think of a single move by which I might continue to seek the goal which I had, at Mr. Carnegie’s suggestion, set for myself. I was rapidly becoming indifferent, not only toward myself, but worse still, I was becoming grouchy and irritable toward those who had given me shelter during my “emergency.”

这次经历摧毁了我所拥有的一切积极性。我感到自己陷入了某种令人沮丧的影响之中，这就像是一场噩梦。我还活着，我可以四处走动，但是我想不出一个办法来继续寻求我在卡内基先生的建议下为自己设定的目标。我很快变得漠不关心，不仅对我自己，而且更糟糕的是，我对那些在我“紧急情况”期间给我庇护的人变得暴躁易怒

I faced the greatest emergency of my life. Unless you have gone through a similar experience, you cannot possibly know how I felt. Such experiences cannot be described. To be understood they must be felt.

我面对了人生中最大的危机。除非你有过类似的经历，否则你不可能知道我的感受。这样的经历是无法描述的。为了被理解，他们必须被感觉到。

“My reasoning faculty had almost been paralyzed.”

“我的推理能力几乎瘫痪了。”

Hill was paralyzed first by fear of physical harm and then by the shame of having been paralyzed by that fear. Have you ever been paralyzed by similar emotions? When you are faced with your own “emergency,” fear can either motivate you or paralyze you. By recognizing that you have a choice and reacting positively to your fears, you can permanently change your life for the better. Many people today may be experiencing the same feelings of anger followed by irritability and the debilitating feeling of indifference. They feel discouraged and lack self-confidence due to uncertainty in their financial situation or personal lives. They may be angry and allow that anger to paralyze them. I had a conversation with just such a young man. “I am 30 years old,” he said, “and have no marketable skills or prospects.” He had a million excuses for not taking action to change his situation. I pointed out that unless he took action nothing would change. “Unless you make an effort to change things,” I said, “in a year’s time the only difference will be that you are 31 years old with no marketable skills or prospects.” Does this pattern sound familiar to you, either for yourself or someone you care for? How do you break that paralysis? Napoleon Hill now shares how he overcame his fear and indifference and found the hope, inspiration, and motivation to recover and create success in his life.

希尔先是因为害怕身体受到伤害而瘫痪，后来又因为害怕而感到羞愧而瘫痪。你曾经被类似的情绪麻痹过吗？当你面对自己的“紧急情况”时，恐惧既可以激励你，也可以麻痹你。通过认识到你有一个选择，并积极地应对你的恐惧，你可以永久地改变你的生活向更好的方向发展。今天，许多人可能正在经历同样的感觉，愤怒之后是易怒和冷漠的衰弱感。由于财务状况和个人生活的不确定性，他们感到沮丧和缺乏自信。他们可能会生气，让这种愤怒麻痹他们。我和这样一个年轻人谈过话。“我今年30岁，”他说，“没有任何市场需要的技能或前景。”他有无数的借口不采取行动改变他的处境。我指出，除非他采取行动，否则一切都不会改变。“除非你努力改变现状，”我说，“不出一年，唯一的区别就是你已经31岁了，没有任何市场需要的技能或前途。”无论是对你自己还是对你关心的人来说，这种模式听起来熟悉吗？如何打破这种麻痹状态？拿破仑 · 希尔现在分享他是如何克服恐惧和冷漠，找到希望、鼓舞和动力，以恢复和创造成功的生活。

The Most Dramatic Moment of My Life

我生命中最激动人心的时刻

The turn came suddenly, in fall 1927, more than a year after the Canton incident. I left the house one night and walked up to the public school building, on top of a hill above the town.

一九二七年秋天，广州事变一年多以后，这个转折突然来临。一天晚上，我离开家，走到镇上一座小山顶上的公立学校大楼。

I had reached a decision to fight the matter out with myself before that night ended. I began to walk around the building, trying to force my befuddled brain to think clearly. I must have made several hundred trips around the building before anything which even remotely resembled organized thought began to take place in my mind. As I walked I repeated over and over to myself, “There is a way out and I am going to find it before I go back to the house.” I must have repeated that sentence a thousand times. Moreover, I meant exactly what I was saying. I was thoroughly disgusted with myself, but I entertained a hope of salvation.

在那天晚上结束之前，我已经决定和自己一决高下。我开始在大楼里走来走去，试图让我糊涂的大脑清晰地思考。在我的脑海中开始出现任何哪怕是很有条理的想法之前，我在这座建筑物周围走了几百次。我边走边一遍又一遍地对自己说: “有一条出路，我要在回家之前找到它。”那句话我一定重复了一千遍。而且，我说的都是真心话。我甚甚厌恶自己，却盼望得救。

Then like a flash of lightning out of a clear sky, an idea burst into my mind with such force that the impulse drove my blood up and down my veins:

然后，就像晴朗的天空中的一道闪电，一个想法以如此强大的力量冲击着我的血管:

“This is your testing time. You have been reduced to poverty and humiliated in order that you might be forced to discover your ‘other self.’”

“现在是你的测试时间。你已经沦落到贫穷和屈辱之中，为的是你可能被迫去发现你的另一个自我。”’

If today’s economic times have dealt you a blow, moving you toward poverty, embarrassing you, or damaging your self-confidence, consider it a test, just as Napoleon Hill did in the late 1920s and early 1930s. Force yourself to discover your “other self.” By working through the low points in your life and persevering, you can gain the insight needed to succeed.

如果今天的经济时代给了你一个打击，让你走向贫穷，让你难堪，或者损害你的自信，那么就把它当作一次考验，就像拿破仑 · 希尔在20世纪20年代末和30年代初所做的那样。强迫自己去发现你的“另一个自我”通过克服生活中的低谷并坚持不懈，你可以获得成功所需的洞察力。

For the first time in years I recalled what Mr. Carnegie had said about this “other self.” I recalled now that he said I would discover it toward the end of my labor of research into the causes of failure and success, and that the discovery usually came as the result of an emergency, when men are forced to change their habits and to think their way out of difficulty.

这么多年来，我第一次回想起卡耐基先生关于“另一个自我”的说法现在我回想起他说我会在我研究失败和成功原因的工作接近尾声的时候发现它，而这个发现通常是紧急情况的结果，当人们被迫改变他们的习惯和思考他们走出困境的方法时。

I continued to walk around the school house, but now I was walking on air. Subconsciously I seemed to know that I was about to be released from the self-made prison into which I had cast myself.

我继续在学校的房子里走来走去，但是现在我感到飘飘然了。潜意识里，我似乎知道自己即将从我自己投入的自我制造的监狱中解脱出来。

I realized that this great emergency had brought me an opportunity, not merely to discover my “other self,” but to test the soundness of the philosophy of achievement which I had been teaching others as being workable. Soon I would know whether it would work or not. I made up my mind that if it did not work I would burn the manuscripts I had written and never again be guilty of telling other people that they were “the masters of their fate, the captains of their souls.”

我意识到这个重大的紧急情况给我带来了一个机会，不仅仅是去发现我的“另一个自我” ，而是去检验我一直教导别人的成就哲学是否可行。很快我就会知道它是否有效。我下定决心，如果它不起作用，我会烧掉我写的手稿，再也不会因为告诉别人他们是“他们命运的主人，他们灵魂的首领”而感到内疚

Hill is paraphrasing from the poem “Invictus,”
published in 1888
by William Ernest Henley (1849–1903).

希尔是从《成事在人》这首诗中转述过来的，这首诗由威廉·欧内斯特·亨利在1888年出版(1849-1903)。

Out of the night that covers me,
Black as the Pit from pole to pole,
I thank whatever gods may be
For my unconquerable soul.

在覆盖着我的黑夜里，从一个极点到另一个极点，我感谢上帝赐予我不可征服的灵魂。

In the fell clutch of circumstance
I have not winced nor cried aloud.
Under the bludgeonings of chance
My head is bloody, but unbowed.

在一连串的外遇中，我没有退缩，也没有大声哭泣。在机会的重击下，我的头血流成河，但不低头。

Beyond this place of wrath and tears
Looms but the Horror of the shade,
And yet the menace of the years
Finds, and shall find, me unafraid.

在这愤怒和泪水的地方之外，只有恐怖的阴影，然而岁月的威胁发现并将发现，我是无所畏惧的。

It matters not how strait the gate,
How charged with punishments the scroll.
I am the master of my fate:
I am the captain of my soul.

无论大门多么狭窄，无论受到多么严厉的惩罚。我是我命运的主人，我是我灵魂的统帅。

The full moon was just rising over the mountain top. I had never seen it shine so brightly before. As I stood gazing at it, another thought flashed into my mind. It was this:

满月正从山顶升起。我以前从未见过它如此明亮地发光。当我站在那里盯着它的时候，另一个想法闪入我的脑海。是这样的:

“You have been telling other people how to master fear and how to surmount the difficulties which arise out of the emergencies of life. From now on you can speak with authority because you are about to rise above your own difficulties with courage and purpose, resolute and unafraid.”

“你一直在告诉别人如何克服恐惧，如何克服生活中的紧急情况所带来的困难。从现在开始，你可以用权威的口吻说话，因为你即将带着勇气和决心，坚定而无畏地克服自己的困难。”

With that thought came a change in the chemistry of my being which lifted me into a state of exultation I had never before known. My brain began to clear itself of the state of lethargy into which it had lapsed. My faculty of reason began to work once more.

随着这个想法而来的是我生命中的化学变化，这种变化使我进入了一种以前从未有过的兴奋状态。我的大脑开始从昏睡状态中清醒过来。我的理智又开始发挥作用了。

For a brief moment I was happy to have had the privilege of going through those long months of torment, because the experience provided an opportunity for me to test the soundness of the principles of achievement which I had so laboriously wrested from my research.

有那么一小会儿，我很高兴能有幸经历这几个月的折磨，因为这次经历让我有机会检验我从研究中辛辛苦苦获得的成就原则的正确性。

When this thought came to me, I stopped still, drew my feet closely together, saluted (I did not know what or whom), and stood rigidly at attention for several minutes. This seemed, at first, like a foolish thing to do, but while I was standing there another thought came through in the form of an “order” that was as brief and snappy as any ever given by a military commander to a subordinate.

当这个念头出现在我脑海里时，我停下来，两脚紧紧地并拢，向他们敬礼(我不知道是什么，也不知道是谁) ，僵硬地立正站了好几分钟。起初，这似乎是一件愚蠢的事情，但是当我站在那里的时候，另一个想法以一种“命令”的形式出现了，这种“命令”和任何一个军事指挥官对下属发出的命令一样简短而有力。

The order said, “Tomorrow get into your automobile and drive to Philadelphia, where you will receive aid in publishing your philosophy of achievement.”

命令上说: “明天上车，开到费城，在那里你将得到帮助，出版你的成就哲学。”

There was no further explanation and no modification of the order. As soon as I received it, I walked back to the house, went to bed, and slept with peace of mind such as I had not known for over a year.

没有进一步的解释，也没有修改命令。我一收到这封信，就走回家，上床睡觉，心情平静地睡着了，这种感觉我已经有一年多没有体会过了。

When I awoke the following morning, I got out of bed and immediately began to pack my clothes and make ready for the trip to Philadelphia. My reason told me that I was embarking upon a fool’s mission. Who did I know in Philadelphia to whom I might apply for financial aid in publishing eight volumes of books at a cost of $25,000? I asked myself.

第二天早上醒来后，我立刻起床，开始收拾衣服，准备去费城旅行。我的理智告诉我，我正在执行一个愚蠢的任务。我在费城认识的人中，有谁可以帮我申请助学金，以25000美元的价格出版八卷书？我问自己。

Instantly the answer to that question flashed into my mind, as plainly as if it had been uttered in audible words: “You are following orders now, instead of asking questions. Your ‘other self’ will be in charge during this trip.”

这个问题的答案立刻在我的脑海中闪现，仿佛是用可以听见的话说出来的: “你现在是在服从命令，而不是问问题。你的“另一个自我”将在这次旅行中负责。”

There was another condition which seemed to make my preparation to go to Philadelphia absurd. I had no money! This thought had barely occurred to me when my “other self” exploded it by giving another sharp order, saying, “Ask your brother-in-law for fifty dollars and he will lend it to you.”

还有另外一个条件似乎使我准备去费城的计划变得荒谬可笑。我没有钱！我还没有想到这一点，“另一个我”就又给了我一个尖锐的命令，说: “向你姐夫要五十块钱，他会借给你的。”

The order seemed definite and final. Without further hesitation I followed instructions. When I asked my brother-in-law for the money, he said, “Why, certainly you can have fifty dollars, but if you are going to be gone very long you had better take a hundred dollars.” I thanked him and said I thought fifty dollars would be enough. I knew it was not enough, but that was the amount my “other self” had commanded me to ask for and that is the amount I secured.

这个命令似乎是确定无疑的。我毫不犹豫地照办了。当我向我姐夫要钱时，他说: “为什么，你当然可以有五十美元，但是如果你要离开很长时间，你最好拿一百美元。”我谢过他，说我觉得五十块钱就够了。我知道这是不够的，但这是我的“另一个我”命令我要求的数额，这是我担保的数额。

I was greatly relieved when I found that my brother-in-law was not going to ask me why I was going to Philadelphia. If he had known all that had taken place in my mind during the previous night, he perhaps would have thought I should go to a psychiatric hospital for treatment instead of going to Philadelphia on a wild-goose chase.

当我发现姐夫不打算问我为什么要去费城时，我松了一口气。如果他知道前一天晚上我脑子里发生的一切，他可能会认为我应该去精神科医院接受治疗，而不是徒劳地去费城。

My “Other Self” Takes Command

我的“另一个自我”掌控一切

I left with my head telling me I was a fool and my “other self” commanding me to ignore the challenge and carry out my instructions.

我离开的时候，我的头告诉我，我是一个傻瓜，我的“另一个自我”命令我忽视这个挑战，执行我的指示。

I drove all night, arriving in Philadelphia the next morning. My first thought was to look up a modestly priced boarding house where I could rent a room for about one dollar a day.

我开了一整夜的车，第二天早上到了费城。我的第一个想法是找一家价格适中的寄宿公寓，在那里我可以以每天一美元的价格租到一个房间。

Here again my “other self” took charge and gave the command to register at the most exclusive hotel in the city. With a little more than forty dollars of my remaining capital in my pocket, it seemed like financial suicide when I marched up to the desk and asked for a room; or rather I should say I started to ask for a room when my newly discovered “other self” gave the order to ask for a suite of rooms, the cost of which would about consume my remaining capital in two days. I obeyed.

在这里，我的“另一个自我”再次掌控了局面，并下令在这个城市最高级的酒店注册。我口袋里只剩下40多美元的剩余资金，当我大步走到桌前要房间的时候，看起来就像是经济上的自杀; 或者更确切地说，当我新发现的“另一个自我”下令要一套房间的时候，我开始要房间了，这个价格将在两天内消耗掉我剩余的资金。我照做了。

The bell-boy picked up my bags, handed me my claim check for my automobile, and bowed me toward the elevator as if I were the Prince of Wales. It was the first time in more than a year that any human being had shown me such deference. My own relatives, with whom I had been living, far from having shown me deference, had (so I imagined) felt I was a burden on their hands, and I am sure that I was, because no man in the frame of mind that I had been in for the past year could be anything other than a burden to all with whom he came into contact.

服务生拿起我的行李，递给我汽车的索赔支票，像威尔士亲王一样向电梯鞠了一躬。这是一年多以来第一次有人对我表现出如此的尊重。我自己的亲戚——我一直和他们生活在一起，远没有表现出对我的尊重——(所以我想)觉得我是他们手中的负担，我确实是这样，因为在我过去一年的心境中，没有一个人能够不成为他所接触的所有人的负担。

It was becoming apparent that my “other self” was determined to wean me away from the inferiority complex which I had developed.

很明显，我的“另一个自我”决心让我摆脱我已经形成的自卑情结。

I tossed the bell-boy a dollar. I started to estimate what my hotel bill would be by the end of the week when my “other self” commanded me to get my mind entirely off of all thoughts of limitation, and to conduct myself, for the time being, just as I would if I had all the money I wanted in my pockets.

我扔给门童一美元。当我的“另一个自我”命令我把思绪从所有限制的想法中完全抽离出来时，我开始估计我的酒店账单在这个周末会是多少，并且暂时保持自己的行为，就像如果我口袋里有我想要的所有钱一样。

The experience I was passing through was both new and strange to me. I had never posed as being anything other than what I believed myself to be.

我所经历的这段经历对我来说既新鲜又陌生。我从来没有摆出过自己不相信自己的样子。

For nearly half an hour this “other self” gave orders which I followed to the letter during the subsequent period of my stay in Philadelphia. The instructions were given through the medium of thoughts which presented themselves in my mind with such force that they were readily distinguishable from my ordinary self-created thoughts.

在接下来的半个小时里，这个“另一个自我”发出了命令，我在费城逗留的这段时间里一直严格遵守。这些指示是通过在我脑海中出现的思想这种力量的媒介发出的，它们很容易与我平常的自我创造的思想区分开来。

Hill took on the persona of the wealthy man he wanted to be. We strongly agree that to be wealthy you need to think wealthy. It is also important to be in the right environment. Don Green, CEO of the Napoleon Hill Foundation, once told me, “I first bought my good suits from Sobel’s, a custom clothing store—where Eastman Kodak executives shopped. The owner had a sign behind the register that said, “If you want to be a success, you must first dress the part.”

希尔扮演了他想成为的富人的角色。我们强烈同意，要变得富有，你需要考虑富有。在正确的环境中工作也很重要。拿破仑山基金会(Napoleon Hill Foundation)的首席执行官唐•格林(Don Green)曾告诉我，“我最初是从定制服装店 Sobel’s (伊士曼柯达(Eastman Kodak)的高管们经常光顾的地方)购买上等西装的。店主在收银台后面挂了一个牌子，上面写着: “如果你想成功，你必须首先穿上这件衣服。”

However, we recommend moderation in trying to emulate Mr. Hill in spending money that he did not have.

然而，我们建议在试图模仿希尔先生的花钱节制，他没有。

I Receive Strange “Orders”
from a Strange Source

我收到奇怪的“命令”从一个奇怪的来源

My instructions began in this fashion:

我的指示是这样开始的:

“You are now completely in charge of your ‘other self.’ You are entitled to know that two entities occupy your body, as in fact two similar entities occupy the body of each living person on earth.

“你现在完全掌控着你的‘另一个自我’你有权知道两个实体占据了你的身体，因为事实上两个相似的实体占据了地球上每一个活着的人的身体。

“One of these entities is motivated by and responds to the impulse of fear. The other is motivated by and responds to the impulse of faith. For more than a year you have been driven, like a slave, by the fear entity.

”其中一个实体受到恐惧冲动的激励并作出反应。另一种是由信仰的冲动所激励和回应的。一年多以来，你像一个奴隶一样，被恐惧所驱使。

“Night before last the faith entity gained control over your physical body, and you are now motivated by that entity. For the sake of convenience you may call this faith entity your ‘other self.’ It knows no limitations, has no fears, and recognizes no such word as ‘impossible.’

“前天晚上，信仰实体获得了对你物质身体的控制，你现在被那个实体所激励。为了方便起见，你可以称这个信仰实体为你的“另一个自我”它知道没有限制，没有恐惧，没有不可能这样的字眼

“You were directed to select this environment of luxury, in a good hotel, as a means of discouraging the return to power of the fear entity. That fear-motivated ‘old self’ is not dead; it has merely been dethroned. And it will follow you around wherever you go, awaiting a favorable opportunity to step in and take charge of you again. It can gain control of you only through your thoughts. Remember this, and keep the doors to your mind tightly closed against all thoughts which seek to limit you in any manner whatsoever, and you will be safe.

“你被指示选择这种奢华的环境，在一个好的酒店，作为一种阻止恐惧实体重新掌权的手段。那个由恐惧驱动的“旧我”并没有死，它只是被废黜了。无论你走到哪里，它都会跟随着你，等待着一个有利的机会再次站出来掌控你。它只能通过你的思想来控制你。记住这一点，紧紧地关闭你的心灵之门，拒绝一切试图以任何方式限制你的思想，你就会安全。

“Do not permit yourself to worry about the money you will need for your immediate expenses. That will come to you by the time you must have it.

“不要让你自己担心你眼下的开支所需要的钱。当你必须拥有它的时候，它就会出现在你面前。

“Now, let us get down to business. First of all you should know that the faith entity now in charge of your body performs no miracles, nor does it work in opposition to any of nature’s laws. As long as it is in charge of your body it will guide you when you call on it, through impulses of thought which it will place in your mind, in carrying out your plans through the most logical and convenient natural media available.

“现在，让我们开始谈正事吧。首先，你们应该知道，现在掌管你们身体的信仰实体不会施行任何神迹，也不会违背任何自然法则。只要它控制着你的身体，当你呼唤它的时候，它就会引导你，通过它在你脑海中的思想冲动，通过最合乎逻辑和最方便的自然媒介来执行你的计划。

“Above everything else, get this fact clearly fixed in your mind, that your ‘other self’ will not do your work for you; it will only guide you intelligently in achieving for yourself the objects of your desires.

“最重要的是，把这个事实清楚地记在心里，你的‘另一个自我’不会为你做事，它只会引导你聪明地为自己实现你的愿望。

Will you be guided by faith?

你会被信仰所引导吗？

Or will you allow fear to overtake you?

或者你会让恐惧压倒你？

“This ‘other self’ will aid you in translating your plans into reality. Moreover, you should know that it begins, always, with your major, or most pronounced desire. At this time your major desire—the one which brought you here—is to publish and distribute the results of your research into the causes of success and failure. You estimate that you will need approximately $25,000.

“这个‘另一个自我’将帮助你把你的计划变成现实。此外，你应该知道，它始终开始于你的专业，或最明显的愿望。在这个时候，你的主要愿望ーー也就是把你带到这里的愿望ーー就是发表和分发你对成功和失败原因的研究成果。你估计大约需要25,000美元。

“Among your acquaintances there is a man who will supply you with this needed capital. Begin, at once, to call into your mind the names of all persons of your acquaintance whom you have reason to believe might be induced to furnish the financial aid you require.

结16:11你所认识的人中、有一个人、能给你这所需的资金。立刻开始在你的脑海中想起你认识的所有人的名字，你有理由相信他们可能会被诱导提供你所需要的经济援助。

“When the name of the logical person comes into your mind, you will recognize it immediately. Communicate with that person and the aid you seek will be given. In your approach, however, present your request in terminology such as you would use in the usual course of business transactions. Make no reference whatsoever to this introduction you have had to your ‘other self.’ If you violate these instructions, you will meet with temporary defeat.

“当逻辑人物的名字出现在你的脑海中时，你会立刻认出它。与那个人交流，你所寻求的帮助就会被给予。但是，在您的方法中，请使用术语表达您的请求，例如在通常的业务事务过程中使用的术语。不要提及任何你已经介绍给你的“另一个自我”如果你违反了这些指示，你将会遭遇暂时的失败。

“Your ‘other self’ will remain in charge and continue to direct you as long as you rely upon it. Keep doubt and fear and worry, and all thoughts of limitation, entirely out of your mind.

“只要你依赖它，你的‘他者自我’将继续掌控并继续指引你。把怀疑、恐惧、担忧，以及所有限制性的想法完全从你的脑海中抹去。

“That will be all for the present. You will now begin to move of your own free will, precisely as you did before you discovered your ‘other self.’ Physically you are the same as you have always been; therefore, no one will recognize that any change has taken place in you.”

“目前就到这里吧。你们现在将开始按照你们自己的自由意志行动，正如你们在发现你们的“另一个自我”之前所做的那样身体上你和以前一样，因此，没有人会意识到你身上发生了什么变化。”

I looked around the room, blinked my eyes, and to make sure that I was not dreaming, I got up and walked over to a mirror and looked at myself closely. The expression on my face had changed from one of doubt to one of courage and faith. There was no longer any doubt in my mind that my physical body was in charge of an influence far different from the one which had been dethroned two nights before, as I walked around that school house in West Virginia.

我环顾了一下房间，眨了眨眼睛，为了确定自己没有在做梦，我站起身来，走到一面镜子前，仔细地看着自己。我脸上的表情从怀疑变成了勇气和信念。当我在西弗吉尼亚的学校房子里走来走去的时候，我的身体对我的影响已经不再有任何的怀疑了。

Here, in editing the manuscript, I have ended the chapter at one of the great turning points in the author’s life. Have you ever undergone a life change such as the one Hill describes above? It can also be described, in religious terms, as a conversion experience. Others may simply refer to it as “a wake-up call” or “a tap on the shoulder” or more vehemently as “a slap in the face!”

在这里，在编辑手稿的过程中，我在作者生命中的一个伟大转折点上结束了这一章。你是否经历过像希尔上面描述的那样的人生转变？从宗教的角度来说，这也可以被描述为一次皈依的经历。其他人可能只是简单地称之为“一个唤醒电话”或“拍拍肩膀” ，或者更激烈地称之为“一记耳光! ”





Chapter Two

A NEW WORLD IS REVEALED TO ME

第二章一个新的世界展现在我面前

OBVIOUSLY I HAD UNDERGONE A NEW BIRTH by which I had been separated from all forms of fear. I now had courage such as I never before had experienced. Despite the fact that I had not as yet been shown how, or from what source, I would be able to secure the necessary funds which I was seeking, I had such absolute faith that the money would be forthcoming that I could see it already in my possession.

很明显，我经历了一次新的生命的诞生，通过这次生命的诞生，我从各种形式的恐惧中分离出来。我现在有了前所未有的勇气。尽管事实上我还没有被告知如何或从什么渠道获得我所寻求的必要资金，但我坚信这笔钱将会到来，我可以看到它已经在我的手中。

On but few occasions in my entire life have I experienced such faith. It was a feeling which one person cannot describe to another. There are no words in the English language suitable for such a description—a fact that all who have had similar experiences can easily verify.

在我的一生中，只有很少的几次经历过这样的信仰。这是一种一个人无法向另一个人描述的感觉。英语中没有适合这种描述的词汇ーー所有有类似经历的人都能轻易地证实这一事实。

I proceeded immediately to carry out the instructions I had received. All feeling that I had embarked upon an impossible mission had now left me. One by one I began to call into my mind the names of all my acquaintances I knew to be financially able to supply me with the $25,000 which I needed, starting with the name of Henry Ford, and going over the entire list of more than three hundred people. My “other self” plainly said, “Keep on searching.”

我立即开始执行我所接到的指示。所有那种我已经开始了一个不可能完成的任务的感觉现在都离我而去了。我开始一个接一个地在脑海里想起我所有的熟人的名字，我知道他们在经济上有能力给我提供我所需要的25,000美元，从亨利 · 福特的名字开始，一直到300多人的名单。我的“另一个自我”明确地说，“继续寻找。”

The Darkest Hour Is Just Before Dawn

至暗之时就在黎明前

But I had come to the end of my rope. My entire list of acquaintances had been exhausted, and with it my physical endurance as well. I had been at work, concentrating my mind upon that list of names, for the better part of two days and nights, having stopped only long enough to sleep for a few hours.

但是我已经走到了极限。我所有的熟人都筋疲力尽了，连同我的身体也受不了了。我一直在工作，把注意力集中在那张名单上，两天两夜的大部分时间里，我只停下来睡了几个小时。

I leaned back in my chair, shut my eyes, and went into a sort of doze for a few minutes. I was aroused by what seemed to be an explosion in the room. As I regained consciousness the name of Albert L. Pelton came into my mind . . . and with it a plan which I knew instantly to be the plan through which I would succeed in getting Mr. Pelton to publish my books. I remembered Mr. Pelton only as an advertiser in The Golden Rule magazine, which I had formerly published.

我靠在椅背上，闭上眼睛，打了几分钟的瞌睡。我被房间里的爆炸声惊醒了。当我恢复意识的时候，阿尔伯特 · l · 佩尔顿的名字出现在我的脑海里... ... 随之而来的是一个计划，我立刻就知道这个计划会成功地让佩尔顿先生出版我的书。我记得佩尔顿先生只是在我以前出版的《金科玉律》杂志上做广告的。

Hill’s subconscious mind identified an acquaintance, remembered only as an advertiser in Hill’s magazine, as a potential source of funding. You make an impression on everyone you meet, just as everyone you meet makes an impression on you. You never know when an acquaintance may become a business associate. There is great power in your network.

希尔的潜意识里认出了一个熟人，只记得他是希尔杂志上的一个广告客户，作为潜在的资金来源。你给你遇到的每个人都留下了印象，就像你遇到的每个人都给你留下了印象一样。你永远不知道一个熟人什么时候会成为生意伙伴。在你的网络中有巨大的力量。

I sent for a typewriter, addressed a letter to Mr. Pelton at Meriden, Connecticut, and described the plan just as it had been handed over to me. He answered by telegram, saying that he would be in Philadelphia to see me the following day.

我派人去请了一台打字机，写了一封信给康涅狄格州梅里登的佩尔顿先生，描述了这个计划，就像它已经交给我一样。他回了电报，说他第二天会到费城来看我。

When he came I showed him the original manuscripts of my philosophy, and briefly explained what I believed its mission to be. He turned through the pages of the manuscripts for a few minutes, then stopped suddenly and fixed his eyes on the wall for a few seconds and said, “I will publish your books for you.”

当他来的时候，我给他看了我哲学的原始手稿，并简要地解释了我认为它的使命是什么。他翻了几页手稿，然后突然停下来，眼睛盯着墙壁看了几秒钟，说: “我会为你出版你的书。”

The contract was drawn; a substantial advance payment on royalties was given me, the manuscripts were turned over to him, and he took them back to Meriden.

合同已经签订，版税的一大笔预付款已经给了我，手稿交给了他，他把它们带回了梅里登。

I did not ask him at the time what caused him to reach a decision to publish my books before he had read the manuscripts, but I do know that he supplied the necessary capital, printed the books, and assisted me in selling many thousands of sets of them to his own clientele of book buyers, who were located in practically every English-speaking country in the world.

我当时并没有问他是什么原因使他在他还没有读过我的手稿之前就决定出版我的书，但我知道他提供了必要的资金，印刷了这些书，并且帮助我向他自己的买书人客户销售了成千上万套，这些买书人几乎遍布世界上每一个讲英语的国家。

My “Other Self” Makes Good

我的“另一个自我”成就美好

Three months from the day that Mr. Pelton called on me in Philadelphia, a completed set of my books was placed on the table in front of me, and my income from the sale of the books began to run high enough for all my needs. These books are now in the hands of my students all over the world.

从佩尔顿先生在费城拜访我的那天算起，三个月后，我的一整套书就放在我面前的桌子上，我卖书的收入开始增加，足以满足我所有的需要。这些书现在在全世界我的学生手中。

My first royalty check from the sale of my books was for $850. As I opened the envelope in which it came, my “other self” said, “Your only limitation is the one which you set up in your own mind!”

我的第一张版税支票是850美元。当我打开信封的时候，我的“另一个自我”说: “你唯一的局限就是你在自己心里设定的那个局限! ”

“Your only limitation is the one which
you set up in your own mind!”

“你唯一的限制就是你自己设定的限制! ”

Does this statement ring as true for you as it does for me? So many times I have been my own worst enemy and needlessly held myself back through a lack of self-confidence. Hill wants us all to discover our “other self” so we can each reach our maximum potential.

这句话对你和对我一样真实吗？很多时候，我都是我自己最大的敌人，因为缺乏自信而毫无必要地让自己退缩。希尔希望我们所有人都能发现自己的“另一个自我” ，这样我们每个人都能发挥最大的潜力。

I am not sure that I understand just what this “other self” is, but I do know that there can be no permanent defeat for the man or the woman who discovers it and relies upon it.

我不确定自己是否真正理解了这个“另一个自我”是什么，但我确实知道，对于发现并依赖它的男人或女人来说，不可能永远失败。

The day after Mr. Pelton came to see me in Philadelphia, my “other self” presented me with an idea which solved my immediate financial problem. The idea flashed into my mind that automobile merchandising methods had to undergo a drastic change and that future salesmen in this field would have to learn to sell automobiles instead of merely serving as buyers of used car trade-ins, as most of them were doing at the time.

佩尔顿先生来费城看我的第二天，我的“另一个自我”向我提出了一个想法，解决了我眼下的财务问题。我突然想到，汽车销售的方法必须经历一个剧烈的变化，未来这个领域的销售人员必须学会销售汽车，而不是像当时的大多数人那样，仅仅充当二手车折价商品的买家。

It also occurred to me that young men who had just finished college and who, therefore, knew nothing of the old “tricks” of automobile merchandising would be the material out of which this new brand of salesmen could best be developed.

我还想到，那些刚刚大学毕业，对汽车销售的老“把戏”一无所知的年轻人，将是培养这种新型销售人员的最佳材料。

The idea was so distinct and impressive that I immediately called the sales manager of the General Motors Company on long-distance telephone and briefly explained my plan to him. He too was impressed by it and referred me to the West Philadelphia branch of the Buick Automobile Company, which was then owned and managed by Earl Powell. I went to see Mr. Powell, explained my plan to him, and he retained me at once to train fifteen carefully selected young college men through whom the plan was put into operation.

这个想法是如此独特和令人印象深刻，我立即打电话给通用汽车公司的销售经理，并简要地向他解释了我的计划。他也对此印象深刻，把我介绍到别克汽车公司在费城西部的分公司，这家公司当时由厄尔 · 鲍威尔拥有和管理。我去见了鲍威尔先生，向他解释了我的计划，他立刻请我去训练十五个经过精心挑选的年轻大学生，通过他们，计划得以实施。

My income from that retainer was more than enough to take care of all of my expenses for the following three months, until the returns from the sale of my books began to come in, including the cost of that expensive suite of rooms, over which I had at first been so concerned.

我从预付款中获得的收入足够支付我接下来三个月的所有开支，直到我的书开始有回报，包括那套昂贵的房间的费用，起初我对此非常关心。

My “other self” had not disappointed me. The money I needed was in my hands at the proper time, just as I had been assured the money would be. By this time I had been convinced that my trip to Philadelphia was by no means a fool’s mission, as my reason had indicated it would be before I left West Virginia.

我的“另一个自我”并没有让我失望。我所需要的钱在适当的时候在我的手中，就像我被保证的钱会是。这时，我已经确信，我的费城之行决不是一个愚蠢的任务，因为我的理由已经表明，在我离开西弗吉尼亚之前，它将是一个愚蠢的任务。

From that time right up to this very minute everything I have needed has come to me, and this despite the fact that the whole world has recently passed through a period of economic depression, when the bare necessities of life have not always been available to all people. Sometimes the arrival of the material things I needed has been a little late, but I can truthfully say that my “other self” has always met me at the cross-roads when I have come to them, and indicated which path I should follow.

从那时到现在，我所需要的一切都来到了我的面前，尽管最近整个世界都经历了一段经济萧条时期，生活的必需品并不总是对所有人开放。有时，我所需要的物质来得有点晚，但我可以真诚地说，当我走到十字路口时，我的“另一个自我”总是在那里迎接我，并指明我应该走哪条路。

The “other self” follows no precedents, recognizes no limitations, and always finds a way to accomplish desired ends! It may meet with temporary defeat, but not with permanent failure. I am as sure of the soundness of this statement as I am of the fact of being engaged in writing these lines.

“另一个自我”不遵循先例，不承认任何限制，并且总能找到一种方法来实现期望的目标！它可能会遭遇暂时的失败，但不会永远失败。我确信这一发言是正确的，正如我确信正在撰写这些文字一样。

The “other self” may “meet with temporary defeat, but not with permanent failure.” How many times do we allow a temporary defeat to affect us as if it were a permanent failure instead of learning from it and moving on? As Hill describes, he himself faced many setbacks along his journey, but each time he was able to find the seed of greater benefit and move on to greater successes.

“他我”可能会“遭遇暂时的失败，但不会永远失败。”有多少次我们允许一个暂时的失败影响我们，仿佛它是一个永久的失败，而不是从中学习并继续前进？正如希尔所描述的那样，他自己在旅途中也面临过许多挫折，但每一次他都能够找到更大利益的种子，并继续向更大的成功迈进。

Meanwhile, I earnestly hope that some of the millions of men and women who have been wounded by the business depression and other unpleasant experiences will discover within themselves this strange entity which I have called my “other self,” and that the discovery will lead them, as it has led me, into a closer relationship with that source of power which surmounts obstacles and masters difficulties, instead of being mastered by them. There is a great power to be discovered in your “other self”! Search sincerely and you will find it.

与此同时，我真诚地希望，数以百万计受到商业萧条和其他不愉快经历伤害的男男女女中的一些人，会在他们自己身上发现这个我称之为“另一个自我”的奇怪实体，这个发现将引导他们，正如它引导我那样，与克服障碍和主人困难的力量之源建立更密切的关系，而不是被他们所掌控。在你的“另一个自我”中有一个巨大的力量需要被发现！真诚地搜索，你就会找到它。

Hill’s work was published during the Great Depression and indeed helped millions of people find hope and courage to live in faith that they would find their own paths to success. I believe we can find many parallels between his time and our own. It is during periods of great stress that we find our will and our inner strength. With the current economic uncertainties, people are choosing—or being forced—to find new paths to provide for themselves and their families, and many will find great success. They will be the great stories of success we will be reading about a few years from now. Will you be among those success stories or still watching from the sidelines?
