希尔的著作发表于大萧条时期，的确帮助数百万人找到了希望和勇气，相信他们会找到自己通往成功的道路。我相信我们可以在他的时代和我们的时代之间找到许多相似之处。正是在巨大的压力下，我们找到了自己的意志和内心的力量。在当前经济不确定的情况下，人们正在选择或被迫寻找新的道路来养活自己和家庭，许多人将会取得巨大成功。它们将是我们几年后将要读到的成功的伟大故事。你会成为那些成功故事中的一员，还是继续袖手旁观？

“Failure”: A Blessing in Disguise

“失败” : 塞翁失马焉知非福

I have made another discovery as the result of this introduction to my “other self,” namely, that there is a solution for every legitimate problem, no matter how difficult the problem may seem.

作为对我的“另一个自我”的介绍，我有了另一个发现，那就是，每一个合理的问题都有一个解决方案，不管这个问题看起来有多么困难。

“There is a solution for every legitimate problem, no matter how difficult the problem may seem.”

“每一个合理的问题都有一个解决方案，不管这个问题看起来有多么困难。”

While this concept may be difficult to acknowledge when you are in the midst of the storm, hindsight generally proves it true.

虽然这个概念可能很难承认，当你在风暴中，后见之明通常证明它是真实的。

I have also discovered that there comes with every experience of temporary defeat, and every failure and every form of adversity, the seed of an equivalent benefit.

我还发现，每一次暂时失败的经历，每一次失败和每一种形式的逆境，都会带来同等收益的种子。

Mind you, I did not say the full-blown flower of success, but the seed from which that flower may be made to germinate and grow. I know of no exception to this rule. The seed of which I speak may not always be observed, but you may be sure it is there, in one form or another.

请注意，我说的不是成功之花的完全盛开，而是这朵花可以发芽和生长的种子。我知道这条规则没有例外。我所说的种子可能不总是被观察到，但是你可以肯定它就在那里，以这样或那样的形式。

I do not pretend to understand all about this strange force which reduced me to poverty and want, and filled me with fear, and then gave me a new birth of faith through which I have been privileged to extend help to tens of thousands who found themselves slipping. But I do know that such a force has come into my life and that I am doing all I can to place others in communication with it.

我并不假装理解这种奇怪的力量，这种力量使我陷入贫穷和匮乏，使我充满恐惧，然后又给我一种新的信仰，通过这种信仰，我有幸帮助了成千上万发现自己正在下滑的人。但是我知道，这样一种力量已经进入我的生活，我正在尽我所能地让其他人与之交流。

During my quarter-century of research into the causes of success and failure I have discovered many principles of truth which have been helpful to me and to others, but nothing I have observed has impressed me more than the discovery that every great leader of the past, whose record I have examined, was beset by difficulties and met with temporary defeat before “arriving.”

在我对成功和失败的原因进行的四分之一个世纪的研究中，我发现了许多对我和其他人都有帮助的真理原则，但我观察到的最令我印象深刻的是，我发现过去的每一位伟大领袖——我研究了他们的记录——在“到达”之前都遭遇了困难和暂时的失败

“Every great leader of the past, whose record I have examined, was beset by difficulties and met with temporary defeat before ‘arriving.’”

“过去的每一位伟大领袖，我已经研究过他们的记录，在到来之前都遭遇困难和暂时的失败。”’

Failure and temporary defeat are part of the journey to finding true success.

失败和暂时的失败是通往真正成功之路的一部分。

From Christ on down to Edison, the men who have achieved most have been those who met with the most stubborn forms of temporary defeat. This would seem to justify the conclusion that Infinite Intelligence has a plan, or a law, by which it hurdles men over many obstacles before giving them the privilege of leadership or the opportunity to render useful service in a noteworthy fashion.

从基督到爱迪生，成就最大的人是那些遭遇最顽固形式的暂时失败的人。这似乎证明了这样一个结论: 无限智慧有一个计划，或者说一条法律，它在给予男人领导特权或者以引人注目的方式提供有用服务的机会之前，先跨越许多障碍。

I would not wish to be again subjected to the experiences through which I passed during that fateful Christmas Eve in 1923, and since, on that eventful evening when I walked around the school house in West Virginia and fought that terrible battle with fear, but all the wealth in the world would not induce me to divest myself of the knowledge I have gained from those experiences.

我不希望再次经历我在1923年那个决定命运的圣诞夜所经历的事情，自从那个多事的晚上，我在西弗吉尼亚的学校里走来走去，与恐惧进行可怕的战斗，但是世界上所有的财富都不会使我放弃我从那些经历中获得的知识。

Faith Has a New Meaning to Me

信仰对我有了新的意义

I repeat that I do not know exactly what this “other self” is, but I know enough about it to lean upon it in a spirit of absolute faith in times of difficulty, when the ordinary reasoning faculty of my mind seems to be inadequate for my needs.

我再说一遍，我并不确切知道这个“另一个自我”是什么，但我对它有足够的了解，在困难时期，当我头脑中普通的推理能力似乎不足以满足我的需要时，我会以绝对信仰的精神依靠它。

The economic depression which started in 1929 brought misery to millions of people, but let us not forget that the experience also brought many blessings, not the least of these being the knowledge that there is something infinitely worse than being forced to work. It is being forced not to work. In the main, that depression was more of a blessing than it was a curse, if analyzed in the light of the changes it brought to the minds of those who were wounded by it. The same is true of every experience which changes men’s habits and forces them to turn to the great “within” for the solution of their problems.

1929年开始的经济萧条给数百万人带来了痛苦，但我们不要忘记，这一经历也带来了许多好处，尤其是认识到有些事情比被迫工作更糟糕。它被迫不工作。总的来说，抑郁更多的是一种祝福而不是一种诅咒，如果从它给那些受到它伤害的人们的思想带来的变化的角度来分析的话。每一次改变人们习惯并迫使他们求助于伟大的“内在”来解决他们的问题的经历也是如此。

“There is something infinitely worse than being forced to work. It is being forced not to work. In the main, that depression was more of a blessing than it was a curse, if analyzed in the light of the changes it brought.”

“还有比被迫工作更糟糕的事情。它被迫不工作。总的来说，如果从经济萧条带来的变化的角度来分析的话，那么它更多的是一种祝福而不是诅咒。”

Is Hill being harsh here, or is he looking beyond the immediate cause and effect of economic disaster to the underlying spiritual result that comes from a true crisis? Can our present economic travails be more of a blessing than a curse? Can economic hardship, such as the loss of a job, be a blessing in disguise? Perhaps yes, if the result is the awakening of an entrepreneurial spirit and the creation of a new business.

希尔在这里是严厉的，还是他超越了经济灾难的直接原因和后果，看到了来自真正危机的潜在精神结果？我们目前的经济困境是否更多的是一种祝福而不是诅咒？经济困难，比如失业，是因祸得福吗？也许是的，如果结果是唤醒了企业家精神，创建了一家新企业的话。

The time which I spent in seclusion in West Virginia was, by great odds, the most severe punishment of my life, but the experience brought blessings in the form of needed knowledge which more than offset the suffering which it cost me. These two results—the suffering and the knowledge gained from it—were inevitable. The law of compensation, which Emerson so clearly defined, made this result both natural and necessary.

我在西弗吉尼亚隐居的那段时间，很可能是我一生中受到的最严重的惩罚，但是这段经历带来了我所需要的知识，远远抵消了我所遭受的痛苦。这两种结果ーー苦难和从中获得的知识ーー是不可避免的。爱默生明确定义的补偿法则使得这个结果既自然又必要。

Ralph Waldo Emerson (1803–1882) explained the law of compensation in very clear terms: “For everything you have missed, you have gained something else; and for everything you gain, you lose something else.” In his journal dated January 8, 1826, he also wrote, “The whole of what we know is a system of compensations. Every defect in one manner is made up in another. Every suffering is rewarded; every sacrifice is made up; every debt is paid.”

拉尔夫·沃尔多·爱默生(1803-1882)用非常清晰的术语解释了补偿法则: “对于你错过的一切，你得到了其他的东西; 对于你得到的一切，你失去了其他的东西。”在他1826年1月8日的日记中，他还写道: “我们所知道的一切都是一个补偿系统。每一个缺陷都是用一种方式来弥补的。凡受苦的、必得报应. 凡牺牲的、必补偿. 凡债都必偿还

What the future may hold for me in the way of disappointment, through temporary defeat, I of course have no way of knowing. I do know, however, that no experience of the future can possibly wound me as deeply as have some of those of the past, because I am now on speaking terms at least with my “other self.”

在失望的道路上，通过暂时的失败，我当然没有办法知道未来会给我带来什么。然而，我确实知道，对未来的体验不可能像过去的一些体验那样深深地伤害我，因为我现在至少与我的“另一个自我”处于交谈状态

Since this “other self” took charge of me, I have come by useful knowledge which I am sure I never would have discovered while my old fear entity was on the throne. For one thing I have learned that those who meet with difficulties which seem insurmountable may, if they will do so, best overcome these difficulties by forgetting them for a time and helping others who have greater problems.

自从这个“另一个自我”控制了我，我就获得了有用的知识，我确信，当我的旧恐惧实体还在位时，我永远不会发现这些知识。我学到的一件事是，那些遇到看似不可逾越的困难的人，如果他们愿意这样做，最好克服这些困难，暂时忘记它们，帮助那些遇到更大困难的人。

The Value of Giving
Before Trying to Get

在试图获得之前先付出的价值

I am sure that no effort which we extend to those who are in distress can go without some form of adequate reward. Not always does the reward come from those to whom the service is rendered, but it will come from one source or another.

我相信，如果没有某种形式的充分回报，我们向那些处于困境的人所作的任何努力都是不可能的。奖励并不总是来自服务对象，而是来自这样或那样的渠道。

I seriously doubt that any man can avail himself of the benefits of his “other self” as long as he is steeped in greed and avarice, envy and fear, but if I am wrong in this conclusion then I still have the unusual honor of being one who has found peace of mind and happiness through a viewpoint that was not sound. I would prefer being thus wrong and happy, to being right and unhappy! But this viewpoint is not wrong!

我严重怀疑，只要一个人沉浸在贪婪、贪婪、嫉妒和恐惧之中，他就不可能从他的“另一个自我”中获益，但如果我的这个结论是错误的，那么我仍然有一种不同寻常的荣耀，那就是通过一种不合理的观点，找到了内心的平静和幸福。我宁愿这样做是错的，是快乐的，也不愿意做对的，是不快乐的！但是这个观点并没有错！

As long as I remain on good terms with my “other self” I shall be able to acquire every material thing that I need. Moreover, I shall be able to find happiness and peace of mind. What more could anyone else accomplish?

只要我与“他我”保持良好的关系，我就能够获得我所需要的一切物质。此外，我将能够找到幸福和内心的平静。其他人还能做什么呢？

The sole motive which inspired me to write this book was a sincere desire to be helpful to others by sharing with them as much as they may be prepared to accept of the stupendous fortune which became mine the moment I discovered my “other self.” This fortune, happily, is one that cannot be measured in material or financial terms alone, because it is greater than everything which such things represent.

促使我写这本书的唯一动机是一种真诚的愿望，希望通过与他人分享尽可能多的东西来帮助他人，因为他们可能已经准备好接受在我发现我的“另一个自我”的那一刻成为我的巨大财富令人高兴的是，这种财富不能仅仅用物质或金钱来衡量，因为它比这些东西所代表的一切都要伟大。

Material and financial fortunes, when reduced to their most liquid terms, are measurable in terms of bank balances. Bank balances are no stronger than banks. This other fortune of which I speak is measurable, not only in terms of peace of mind and contentment but as manifested in those adept at prayer.

物质财富和金融财富，如果减少到最具流动性的条件，就可以用银行余额来衡量。银行存款余额并不比银行存款余额多。我所说的另一种幸运是可以衡量的，不仅仅是内心的平静和满足，而且还体现在那些擅长祈祷的人身上。

My “other self” has taught me to concentrate upon my purpose and to forget about the plan by which it is to be attained when I go to prayer. I am not suggesting that material objects may be acquired without plans. What I am saying is that the power which translates one’s thoughts or desires into realities has its source in an Infinite Intelligence which knows more about plans than the one doing the praying.

我的“另一个自我”已经教导我专注于我的目标，忘记当我开始祷告时要达到的计划。我并不是说物质实体可以无计划地获得。我想说的是，将一个人的想法或愿望转化为现实的能力，来源于一种无限的智慧，这种智慧比做祷告的人更懂得计划。

Stating the case in another way, may it not be wise, when praying, to trust to the Universal Mind to hand over the plan best suited for the attainment of the object of that prayer? My experience with prayer has taught me that so often all which results from prayer is a plan (if the prayer is answered at all), a plan that is suited for the attainment of the object of the prayer through natural and material media. The plan must be transmuted, through self-effort action.

用另一种方式来说明这个问题，在祈祷时，相信宇宙意识交出最适合实现祈祷目标的计划，难道不是明智之举吗？我的祷告经验告诉我，祷告的结果往往都是一个计划(如果祷告得到回应的话) ，这个计划适合通过自然和物质的媒介来达到祷告的目的。这个计划必须通过自我努力的行动来改变。

I know nothing about any form of prayer which can be induced to work favorably in a mind that is colored, in the slightest degree, by fear.

我对任何形式的祈祷一无所知，这种祈祷可以诱使一个有一点点恐惧色彩的人产生积极的效果。

Is prayer a part of your life? Do you trust God to “hand over the plan best suited for the attainment of the object” of your prayer? Do you acknowledge that in order for your plan to be successful you must take action?

祈祷是你生活的一部分吗？你是否相信神会“交出最适合你祷告的目的的计划” ？你是否认识到，为了使你的计划成功，你必须采取行动？

A New Way to Pray

一种新的祈祷方式

Since becoming better acquainted with my “other self,” my way of praying is different from what it was before. I used to go to prayer only when facing difficulty. Now I go to prayer before difficulty overtakes me, when possible. I now pray, not for more of this world’s goods and greater blessings, but to be worthy of that which I already have. I find that this plan is better than the old one.

自从我更加了解我的“另一个自我”以后，我的祈祷方式和以前不一样了。我过去只在遇到困难时才去祷告。现在我要在困难来临之前，尽可能的祈祷。我现在祈祷，不是为了这个世界更多的财富和更多的祝福，而是为了配得上我已经拥有的。我发现这个计划比原来的计划好。

Infinite Intelligence seems not at all offended when I give thanks and show that I am grateful for the blessings which have crowned my efforts. I was astounded, when I first tried this plan of offering a prayer of thanks for what I already possessed, to discover what a vast fortune I had owned without being appreciative of it.

当我感谢并表达我对加冕我的努力的祝福的感激时，无限智慧似乎并没有被冒犯。当我第一次尝试这个为我已经拥有的东西祈祷感谢的计划时，我感到很惊讶，因为我发现自己拥有了如此巨大的财富，却没有对它充满感激。

For example, I discovered that I possessed a sound body which had never been seriously damaged by illness. I had a mind which was reasonably well balanced. I had a creative imagination through which I could render useful service to great numbers of people. I was blessed with all the freedom I desired, in both body and mind. I possessed an imperishable desire to help others who were less fortunate.

例如，我发现我拥有一个健康的身体，从来没有被疾病严重损害。我有一个相当平衡的头脑。我有一种创造性的想象力，通过这种想象力，我可以为许多人提供有用的服务。我得到了我所渴望的自由，无论是身体上还是精神上。我有一种不朽的愿望，那就是帮助那些不幸的人。

I discovered that happiness, the highest aim of mankind, was mine for the taking, business depression or no business depression.

我发现幸福，人类的最高目标，是我可以得到的，不管是经济萧条还是没有经济萧条。

Last, but by no means least, I discovered that I had the privilege of approaching Infinite Intelligence, either for the purpose of offering thanks for what I already possessed, or to ask for more, and for guidance.

最后，但绝不是最不重要的，我发现我有接近无限智慧的特权，要么是为了对我已经拥有的东西表示感谢，要么是为了要求更多的东西和指引。

It may be helpful for every reader of this book to take inventory of his or her intangible assets. Such an inventory may disclose possessions of priceless value.

这可能是有助于每一个读者的这本书，以盘点他或她的无形资产。这样的存货清单可能会显示出无价的财产。

May we all make an inventory of our blessings in life. And give thanks for every gift that we have been given. I know that when I am at a low point in my life, I force myself to think of my family and friends and the blessings they have brought to my life. It is the quickest path up and puts my temporary setbacks into perspective.

愿我们都能清点一下生命中的幸福。感谢我们所得到的一切恩赐。我知道，当我处于人生的低谷时，我会强迫自己想起我的家人和朋友，以及他们给我的生活带来的幸福。这是最快的方法，可以让我正确看待暂时的挫折。

Some Signs We Have Overlooked

我们忽视的一些迹象

The whole world is undergoing a change of such stupendous proportions that millions of people have become panic-stricken with worry, doubt, indecision, and fear! It seems to me that now is a splendid time for those who have come to the cross-roads of doubt to endeavor to become acquainted with their “other selves.”

整个世界正在经历如此巨大的变化，以至于数以百万计的人们因担忧、怀疑、优柔寡断和恐惧而惊慌失措！在我看来，现在是那些来到怀疑的十字路口，努力去熟悉他们的“其他自我”的辉煌时刻

All who wish to do so will find it helpful if they take a lesson from nature. Observation will show that the eternal stars shine nightly in their accustomed places; that the sun continues to send down its rays of warmth, causing Mother Earth to yield an over-abundance of food and clothing; that water continues to flow down hill; that the birds of the air and the wild animals of the forest receive their accustomed requirements of food; that useful day follows restful night; that busy summer follows the inactive winter; that the seasons come and go precisely as they did before the 1929 depression began; that, in reality, only men’s minds have ceased to function normally, and this, because men have filled their minds with fear. Observation of these simple facts of everyday life may be helpful as a starting point for those who wish to supplant fear by faith.

所有希望这样做的人都会发现，如果他们从大自然中吸取教训，这会很有帮助。观察将表明，永恒的星星每夜都在它们习惯的地方发光; 太阳继续发出温暖的光芒，导致地球母亲产生过多的食物和衣服; 水继续从山上流下; 空中的鸟儿和森林里的野生动物得到它们习惯的食物; 有用的白天紧随着宁静的夜晚; 繁忙的夏天紧随着冬天; 四季来来去去，正如1929年大萧条开始之前一样; 事实上，只有人类的思想停止了正常的运作，这是因为人类已经让他们的心中充满了恐惧。观察这些日常生活中的简单事实可能会对那些希望用信仰取代恐惧的人有所帮助。

I am not a prophet, but I can, with all due modesty, predict that every individual has the power to change his or her material or financial status by first changing the nature of his or her beliefs.

我不是一个预言家，但是我可以非常谦虚地预言，每个人都有能力通过改变他或她信仰的本质来改变他或她的物质或经济状况。

“Every individual has the power to change his or her material or financial status by first changing the nature of his or her beliefs.”

”每个人都有权通过首先改变其信仰的性质来改变其物质或经济状况”

It was right after publication of Think and Grow Rich in 1937 that Napoleon Hill began this manuscript for Outwitting the Devil. Through his interview with the Devil, Hill discovers and reveals how the Devil may be “having his way” with you and how you can ignite your “other self” to not only conquer the Devil in your own life but to also empower your “other self” to achieve your greatest success! Throughout his work is the recurring theme of the importance of transforming your thoughts from fear to faith.

就在1937年《思考与致富》出版后，拿破仑 · 希尔在20世纪90年代战胜心魔开始写这份手稿。通过他与魔鬼的访谈，希尔发现和揭示魔鬼可能是“有他的方式”与你和你如何可以点燃你的“其他自我” ，不仅在你自己的生活中征服魔鬼，而且授权你的“其他自我” ，以实现你最大的成功！贯穿他整个作品的是一个反复出现的主题，即把你的思想从恐惧转化为信仰的重要性。

Do not confuse the word “belief” with the word “wish.” The two are not the same. Everyone is capable of “wishing” for financial, material, or spiritual advantages, but the element of faith is the only sure power by which a wish may be translated into a belief, and a belief into reality.

不要把“信仰”和“希望”混淆这两者是不同的。每个人都能“希望”获得经济、物质或精神上的好处，但是信仰是唯一可靠的力量，通过它，一个愿望可以转化为信仰，一个信仰变成现实。

And right here is an appropriate place at which to call attention to a real benefit which anyone may experience by deliberately using faith in focusing attention upon any form of constructive desire. The mind acts upon one’s dominating, or most pronounced desires. There is no escape from this fact. It is a fact indeed. “Be careful what you set your heart upon, for it surely shall be yours.”

这里是一个合适的地方，可以让人们注意到一个真正的好处，任何人都可以通过故意使用信念，将注意力集中在任何形式的建设性欲望上，从而体验到这个好处。头脑对一个人的支配欲或最明显的欲望采取行动。这是无法逃避的事实。这确实是一个事实。你要谨慎自己所倚靠的，因为这必是你的

Faith Is the Beginning
of All Great Achievement

信仰是一切伟大成就的开端

If Edison had stopped by merely wishing for the secret with which electric energy might be harnessed and made to serve through the incandescent lamp, that convenience to civilization would have remained among nature’s multifarious secrets. He met with temporary defeat more than 10,000 times before wresting this secret from nature. It was finally yielded up to him because he believed it would be, and he kept on trying until he had the answer.

如果爱迪生停下来仅仅是希望找到利用电能的秘密，并通过电灯泡为人类服务，那么对人类文明的便利将仍然是大自然多种多样的秘密之一。在从大自然中获得这个秘密之前，他遭遇了一万多次暂时的失败。他最终屈服于他，因为他相信这是可能的，他不断地尝试，直到他得到了答案。

Edison uncovered more of nature’s secrets (they might have been called “miracles” at an earlier period) in the realm of physics than did any other man who ever lived, and this because he became acquainted with his “other self.” I have his own word for this, but even if I did not have it, his achievements of themselves have disclosed the secret in their unfoldment.

爱迪生在物理领域发现了比任何其他人都多的大自然的秘密(它们在早期可能被称为“奇迹”) ，这是因为他开始了解他的“另一个自我”关于这一点，我有他自己的话，但即使我没有，他自己的成就已经在他们的展示中揭示了秘密。

Nothing within reason is impossible to the man who knows and relies upon his “other self.” Whatever man believes to be true has a way of becoming true.

对于一个知道并依赖于他的“他者自我”的人来说，在理性之中没有什么是不可能的无论人们相信什么是真理，总有一种方式会变成真理。

A prayer is a released thought, sometimes expressed in audible words and at other times expressed silently. I have observed by experience that a silent prayer is as efficacious as the one which is expressed in words. I have observed also that one’s state of mind is the determining factor when prayer works, as well as when it does not.

祈祷是一种释放的思想，有时以可听见的语言表达，有时以无声的方式表达。根据我的经验，我观察到一个无声的祷告和一个用语言表达的祷告一样有效。我也注意到，一个人的心态是决定祷告成功与否的因素。

My conception of the “other self” which I have tried to describe is that it merely symbolizes a newly discovered approach to Infinite Intelligence, an approach which one may control and direct through the simple process of mixing faith with one’s thoughts. This is only another way of saying that I now have greater faith in the power of prayer.

我对“另一个自我”的概念，我试图描述的是，它仅仅象征着一种新发现的通向无限智慧的方法，一种人们可以通过把信仰和思想混合在一起的简单过程来控制和引导的方法。这只是另一种说法，我现在更加相信祈祷的力量。

The state of mind known as faith apparently opens to one the medium of a sixth sense through which one may communicate with sources of power and information far surpassing any available through the five physical senses. There comes to your aid, and to do your bidding, with the development of the sixth sense, a strange power which, let us assume, is a guardian angel who can open to you at all times the door to the Temple of Wisdom. The “sixth sense” comes as near to being a miracle as anything I have ever experienced, and it appears so perhaps because I do not understand the method by which this principle is operated.

被称为信仰的精神状态显然打开了一种第六感的媒介，通过这种媒介，一个人可以与力量和信息的来源进行交流，远远超过任何通过五种物理感官所能获得的。随着第六感的发展，一种奇怪的力量，我们假设，它是一个守护天使，可以随时为你打开通往智慧圣殿的大门。“第六感”几乎是我经历过的任何事情中的一个奇迹，它之所以出现，也许是因为我不明白这个原理是如何运作的。

This much I do know—that there is a power or a first cause, or an Intelligence which permeates every atom of matter, and embraces every unit of energy perceptible to man; that this Infinite Intelligence converts acorns into oak trees, causes water to flow downhill in response to the law of gravity, follows night with day, and winter with summer, each maintaining its proper place and relationship to the other. This Intelligence may aid in transmuting one’s desires into concrete or material form. I have this knowledge because I have experimented with it and have experienced it.

我只知道这么多: 有一种力量或第一原因，或者说是一种智慧，它渗透在物质的每一个原子里，包括人类可以感知到的每一个能量单位; 这种无限的智慧把橡子变成橡树，根据万有引力定律，使水顺着山坡流下去，白天跟着黑夜，夏天跟着冬天，每一个都保持着适当的位置和相互之间的关系。这种智慧可能有助于将你的欲望转化为具体的或物质的形式。我有这方面的知识，因为我与它有实验和经验。

I have for many years followed the habit of taking personal inventory of myself once a year, for the purpose of determining how many of my weaknesses I have bridged or eliminated, and to ascertain what progress, if any, I had made during the year.

多年来，我一直遵循每年对自己进行一次个人盘点的习惯，目的是确定自己弥补或消除了多少缺点，并确定自己在这一年中取得了哪些进步，如果有的话。

This section on faith is worth rereading a few times because it contains Hill’s core teachings on prayer. Faith, in his view, is a “sixth sense” or spiritual power that enables one to succeed if one is in step with the first cause of all things—one of his descriptions of God. His is a practical or “scientific” faith that emphasizes tangible results.

这部分关于信仰的内容值得重读几遍，因为它包含了希尔关于祈祷的核心教义。在他看来，信仰是一种“第六感”或精神力量，如果一个人与万物的第一原因——他对上帝的描述之一——步调一致，他就能够成功。他的信仰是一种实际的或“科学的”信仰，强调有形的结果。

In the book Three Feet from Gold my co-author and I discuss the Personal Success Equation that clearly reveals the importance of faith:

在《距离金子三英尺》一书中，我和合著者讨论了个人成功等式，它清楚地揭示了信仰的重要性:

((P + T) x A x A) + F = Your Personal Success Equation

(p + t) x a x a) + f = 你的个人成功等式

Combining your Passion with your Talent and then seeking the right Association and taking the right Action are very important components for Success . . . but it is when you combine all those components with a strong Faith in yourself and your mission that you truly have Your Personal Success Equation.

把你的激情和你的天赋结合起来，然后寻找正确的联系，采取正确的行动是成功的重要组成部分... ... 但是当你把所有这些组成部分与对自己和你的使命的强烈信念结合起来，你才真正拥有了你的个人成功方程式。





Chapter Three

A STRANGE INTERVIEW WITH THE DEVIL

第三章与魔鬼的奇怪会面

WHILE YOU ARE READING THE INTERVIEW with the Devil, you will recognize from the brief description I have given you of the history of my life what a desperate effort the Devil made to muzzle me before I gained public recognition. You will understand also, after reading the interview with the Devil, why the interview had to be preceded by this personal history of my background.

当你在阅读《与魔鬼的交谈》的时候，你会从我给你的关于我生命历史的简短描述中认识到，在我获得公众认可之前，魔鬼做出了多么绝望的努力来堵住我的嘴。你也会理解，在阅读了魔鬼的采访之后，为什么采访之前必须有这个我的背景的个人历史。

Before you begin to read the interview, I want you to have a clear picture of the final fling the Devil had at me, and be it remembered with profit that it was this final fling which gave mercy a chance to turn and twist the Devil’s tail until he squealed out his confession.

在你开始读这篇采访之前，我要你清楚地了解一下魔鬼对我最后的一次抛掷，并且要记住，正是这最后一次抛掷给了仁慈一个机会转动并扭曲魔鬼的尾巴，直到他尖叫出他的忏悔。

The Devil’s undoing began with the depression in 1929. Through that fortunate turn of the Wheel of Life, I lost my 600-acre estate in the Catskill Mountains; my income was entirely cut off; the Harriman National Bank, in which all my funds were deposited, folded up and was wiped out. Before I realized what was happening, I found myself caught up in a spiritual and economic hurricane which evolved into a worldwide catastrophe of such force that no individual or group of individuals could withstand it.

魔鬼的毁灭始于1929年的大萧条。在那次生命之轮的幸运转折中，我失去了卡兹奇山600英亩的庄园; 我的收入全部被切断; 哈里曼国家银行，我所有的资金都存在那里，折叠起来，然后一笔勾销。在我意识到发生了什么之前，我发现自己陷入了一场精神和经济上的飓风，这场飓风演变成了一场世界性的灾难，其力量之大，任何个人或团体都无法承受。

While waiting for the storm to cease and the stampede of human fear to stop, I moved to Washington, D.C., the city from which I made my start after my first meeting with Andrew Carnegie, nearly a quarter of a century previously.

在等待风暴停止和人类恐惧的惊慌失措停止时，我搬到了华盛顿特区。

There seemed nothing for me to do except sit down and wait. All I had was time. After three years of waiting without tangible results, my restless soul began to push me back into service.

除了坐下来等待，我似乎什么也做不了。我只有时间。经过三年的等待，没有实际的结果，我不安的灵魂开始推动我回到服务。

There was little opportunity for me to teach a philosophy of success when the world around me was in the midst of abject failure, and men’s minds were filled with the fear of poverty.

我几乎没有机会教授成功哲学，当时我周围的世界正处于一团糟的失败之中，人们的心中充满了对贫穷的恐惧。

This thought came to me one evening while I was sitting in my automobile, in front of the Lincoln Memorial on the Potomac River, within the shadow of the Capitol. With it came another thought: The world had staged an unprecedented depression over which no human being had control. With that depression had come to me an opportunity to test the philosophy of self-determination, to the organization of which I had devoted the better portion of my adult life. Once more I had the opportunity to learn whether my philosophy was practical or mere theory.

一天晚上，当我坐在我的汽车里，在 Potomac River 的林肯纪念堂前，在国会大厦的阴影下，我突然产生了这个想法。随之而来的是另一种想法: 世界已经上演了一场前所未有的萧条，没有人能够控制它。伴随着这种沮丧，我有机会来检验自决的哲学，我把我成年生活中更好的一部分奉献给了这个组织。我又一次有机会学习我的哲学是实用的还是纯粹的理论。

I realized too the opportunity had come to test a claim I had made hundreds of times that “every adversity brings with it the seed of an equivalent advantage.” What, if any, I asked myself, were the advantages to me of a world depression?

我也意识到，这个机会来检验我曾数百次说过的一句话: “每一次逆境都会带来同等优势的种子。”我问自己，如果有的话，对我来说世界萧条有什么好处？

When I began to look for a direction in which I might move to test my philosophy, I made the most shocking discovery of my life. I discovered that through some strange power which I did not understand, I had lost my courage; my initiative had been demoralized; my enthusiasm had been weakened. Worst of all, I was sorely ashamed to acknowledge that I was the author of a philosophy of self-determination, because down deep in my heart I knew, or thought I knew, that I could not make my philosophy pull me out of the hole of despair in which I found myself.

当我开始寻找一个可以检验我的人生哲学的方向时，我有了人生中最令人震惊的发现。我发现，由于某种我无法理解的奇异力量，我失去了勇气; 我的积极性受挫; 我的热情被削弱了。最糟糕的是，我羞于承认自己是自决哲学的作者，因为在我的内心深处，我知道，或者说我认为我知道，我不能让我的哲学把我从绝望的深渊中拉出来。

While I floundered in a state of mental bewilderment, the Devil must have been dancing a jig of rejoicing. At last he had “the author of the world’s first philosophy of individual achievement” pinned under his thumb and paralyzed with indecision.

当我在精神困惑的状态中挣扎时，魔鬼一定在欢快地跳着舞。最后，他终于把“世界上第一个个人成就哲学的作者”压在了自己的脚下，犹豫不决，不知所措。

But the Devil’s opposition must have been at work too!

但是魔鬼的反对一定也在起作用！

As I sat there in front of the Lincoln Memorial, reviewing in retrospect the circumstances which had so many times previously lifted me to great heights of achievement, only to let me drop to equal depths of despair, a happy thought was handed over to me in the form of a definite plan of action by which I believed I could throw off that hypnotic feeling of indifference with which I had been bound.

当我坐在林肯纪念堂前，回想起过去多次把我提升到成就高峰的情形，只是让我陷入同样深的绝望时，一个快乐的想法以一个明确的行动计划的形式交给了我，我相信我可以摆脱那种被束缚在我身上的麻木不仁的催眠感觉。

In the interview with the Devil, the exact nature of the power by which I had been deprived of my initiative and courage has been described. It is the same power with which millions of others were bound during the Great Depression. It is the chief weapon with which the Devil ensnares and controls human beings.

在与魔鬼的会谈中，我被剥夺了主动权和勇气的力量的确切性质被描述了。在大萧条时期，数以百万计的其他国家也与这种力量紧密相连。它是魔鬼诱捕和控制人类的主要武器。

The sum and substance of this thought which came to me was this: Despite the fact that I had learned from Andrew Carnegie and more than five hundred others of equal business and professional achievements that noteworthy achievements in all walks of life come through the application of the Master Mind (the harmonious coordination of two or more minds working to a definite end), I had failed to make such an alliance for the purpose of carrying out my plan to take the philosophy of individual achievement to the world.

这个想法的总和和实质是这样的: 尽管我从安德鲁 · 卡内基和其他500多位具有同等商业和专业成就的人那里学到，各行各业中值得注意的成就都是通过运用大师的思想(两个或两个以上的头脑为了一个明确的目标而和谐地协调)而取得的，但我没有达成这样一个联盟，以便实现我的计划，把个人成就的哲学带到世界上去。

Despite the fact I had understood the power of the Master Mind, I had neglected to appropriate and use this power. I had been laboring as a “lone wolf” instead of allying myself with other and superior minds.

尽管事实上我已经理解了大师思想的力量，我却忽略了合理使用这种力量。我一直在努力作为一个“独狼” ，而不是与其他和优越的头脑结盟自己。

The interview with the Devil may have occurred as Hill sat at the foot of the Lincoln Memorial. Was it real? It was real to Hill and created the framework for how he lived his life and shared his revelations with us: his students. To reiterate Hill’s earlier words, he had discovered that “every great leader of the past, whose record I have examined, was beset by difficulties and met with temporary defeat before ‘arriving.’” Hill also describes in his works how these great leaders surrounded themselves with Master Minds. They conquered their inner struggles with adversity and then used the power of the Master Mind to propel their successes. Consider how you could form a Master Mind group—a team—to help you overcome adversity and propel you to success.

对魔鬼的采访可能发生在希尔坐在林肯纪念堂脚下的时候。是真的吗？这对希尔来说是真实的，并为他如何生活创造了框架，并与我们分享了他的启示: 他的学生。为了重申希尔早些时候的话，他发现“过去的每一位伟大领袖——我研究过他们的记录——在‘到达’之前都曾遭遇困难和暂时的失败。希尔还在他的作品中描述了这些伟大的领袖们是如何被大师级的思想包围着的。他们在逆境中战胜了内心的挣扎，然后运用大师的力量来推动他们的成功。考虑一下如何组建一个智囊团ーー一个团队ーー来帮助你克服逆境，推动你走向成功。

An Analysis

分析

Let us now briefly analyze the strange interview you are about to begin. Some who read will want to ask, after they finish it, “Did you really interview the Devil, or did you merely interview an imaginary Devil?” Some may wish the answer to this question before they begin the interview.

现在让我们简要地分析一下你即将开始的这次奇怪的采访。有些读者读完之后会问: “你真的采访了魔鬼，还是仅仅采访了一个想象中的魔鬼? ”有些人可能希望在开始面试之前得到这个问题的答案。

I will answer in the only truthful way I could answer . . . by saying that the Devil I interviewed may have been real, just as he claimed to be, or he may have been the creation of my own imagination. Whichever he was, whether real or imaginary, is of little importance compared with the nature of the information conveyed through the interview.

我会用我能回答的唯一真实的方式来回答... ... 我会说，我采访的魔鬼可能是真实的，就像他声称的那样，或者他可能是我自己想象出来的。无论他是真实的还是想象的，与通过采访传达的信息的性质相比，都是微不足道的。

The important question is this: Does the interview convey dependable information which may be helpful to people who are trying to find their places in the world? If it conveys that sort of information, no matter whether it is conveyed in the form of fact or fiction, then it is worthy of serious analysis through careful reading. I am not concerned in the least as to the real source of the information or as to the real nature of the Devil whose astounding story you are about to read. I am concerned only with the fact that the Devil’s confession squares perfectly with what I have seen of life.

重要的问题是: 面试是否传达了可靠的信息，这些信息可能对那些试图在世界上找到自己位置的人有帮助？如果它传达了这种信息，不管它是以事实还是虚构的形式传达的，那么通过仔细阅读，它就值得认真分析。我一点也不关心信息的真正来源，也不关心你们将要读到的那个令人震惊的故事中的魔鬼的真实本性。我只关心这样一个事实: 魔鬼的忏悔与我所看到的生活完全吻合。

I believe the interview does convey information of practical benefit to all who have not found life to be friendly, and the reason I believe so is the fact that I have made the central theme of this book yield to me all the happiness I need, in the form best suited to my nature.

我相信这次采访的确向那些没有发现生活是友好的人传达了实际利益的信息，我之所以这样认为，是因为我已经使这本书的中心主题以最适合我本性的形式给了我所需要的所有幸福。

I have had experience with enough of the principles mentioned by the Devil to assure me that they will do exactly what he says they will. That is enough for me. So I pass the story of the interview on to you for whatever you may be able to make it pay in useful dividends.

我有足够的经验与魔鬼提到的原则向我保证，他们将完全按照他说他们会。这对我来说足够了。所以我把这个面试的故事告诉你们，无论你们能从中得到什么有用的回报。

Perhaps you will get the greatest values if you accept the Devil as being what he claims himself to be, relying upon his message for whatever it may bring you that you can use, and not worrying as to who the Devil is or whether he exists.

也许你会得到最大的价值，如果你接受魔鬼是什么，他声称自己是，依靠他的信息，无论它可能带给你什么，你可以使用，而不是担心谁是魔鬼或是否存在。

If you want my honest personal opinion, I believe the Devil is exactly who he claims to be. Now let us analyze his strange confession.

如果你想要我诚实的个人意见，我相信魔鬼就是他声称的那个人。现在让我们来分析一下他那奇怪的供词。

After forcing his way into the consciousness of the Devil, “Mr. Earthbound” began the unwilling interview with questions which could not be evaded . . .

在强行进入魔鬼的意识之后，“地缚先生”开始了不情愿的采访，提出了一些无法回避的问题..。

Hill, “Mr. Earthbound,” interrogates the Devil in an almost courtroom atmosphere. Somehow, the Devil is obligated to give complete and accurate answers. How was this done? Perhaps Hill forced the Devil’s confession by forming a Master Mind, possibly with his wife, “the harmonious coordination of two or more minds working to a definite end” to exert the power of God—“the great storehouse of Infinite Intelligence wherein is stored all that is, all that ever was, and all that can ever be.” Perhaps Hill won the right to accurate responses by being a thinker in control of his own mind, who mastered all his fears. Thanks to this mastery and control, Hill could demand true and accurate responses from the Devil. In any event, Hill forces the Devil to expose his tricks and wiles—so that we may counter them and avoid the pitfalls in our lives.

希尔，“地缚先生，”在几乎法庭的气氛中审问魔鬼。不知何故，魔鬼有义务给出完整和准确的答案。这是怎么做到的？也许希尔迫使魔鬼认罪，是因为他形成了一个“两个或两个以上的头脑为了一个明确的目的而协调工作”的头脑，以便发挥上帝的力量——“无限智慧的巨大宝库，里面储存着所有的现在，所有的过去，所有的将来。”也许希尔是通过控制自己的思想，控制自己的所有恐惧，从而赢得了准确回答问题的权利。由于这种掌握和控制，希尔可以要求魔鬼做出真实和准确的反应。无论如何，希尔迫使魔鬼揭露他的诡计和诡计ーー这样我们就可以反击它们，避开我们生活中的陷阱。

Here Begins the
Interview with the Devil

以下是对魔鬼的采访

Q I have uncovered the secret code by which I can pick up your thoughts. I have come to ask you some very plain questions. I demand that you give me direct and truthful answers. Are you ready for the interview, Mr. Devil?

问: 我已经发现了一个秘密密码，我可以通过这个密码了解你的想法。我是来问你一些非常简单的问题的。我要求你给我直接和真实的答案。你准备好面试了吗，恶魔先生？

A Yes, I am ready, but you must address me with more respect. During this interview you will address me as “Your Majesty.”

A 是的，我准备好了，但是你必须对我更加尊重。在这次采访中，你要称呼我为“陛下”

Q By what right do you demand such royal respect?

你有什么权利要求这样的皇家尊重？

A You should know I control 98 percent of the people of your world. Do you not think that entitles me to rate as royalty?

A 你应该知道我控制着你们世界98% 的人。难道你不认为这样我就有资格成为皇室成员了吗？

I had an extremely adverse reaction to hearing the Devil referred to as “Your Majesty” when I first read this interview. Then I realized that Hill probably intended to create just that reaction . . . and I read on. And, of course, the text does not reflect whether Hill might have used an ironic or sarcastic tone when so addressing the Devil.

当我第一次读到这篇采访时，听到魔鬼被称为“陛下” ，我有一个极其不利的反应。然后我意识到希尔可能只是想创造这种反应... ... 我继续读下去。当然，文本并没有反映出希尔在这样称呼魔鬼时是否使用了讽刺或讽刺的语气。

Q Have you proof of your claim?

问: 你有证据证明你的索赔吗？

A Yes, plenty of it.

A 是的，很多。

Q Of what does your proof consist?

你的证明是什么？

A Of many things. If you want answers, you will address me as “Your Majesty.” Some things you will understand; some you will not. In order that you may get my viewpoint, I shall describe myself and correct the false notions people have of me and my place of abode.

A 许多事情。如果你想知道答案，你可以叫我“陛下”有些事你会明白，有些你不会。为了让你了解我的观点，我将描述我自己，并纠正人们对我和我的住所的错误观念。

Q That is a fine idea, Your Majesty. Start by telling me where you live. Then describe your physical appearance.

问: 这是个好主意，陛下。先告诉我你住在哪里，然后描述一下你的外表。

A My physical appearance? Why, my dear Mr. Earthbound, I have no physical body. I would be handicapped by such an encumbrance as those in which you earthbound creatures live. I consist of negative energy, and I live in the minds of people who fear me. I also occupy one-half of every atom of physical matter and every unit of mental and physical energy. Perhaps you will better understand my nature if I tell you I am the negative portion of the atom.

A 我的外貌？哎呀，我亲爱的地缚先生，我没有肉体。我会被你们这些地球上的生物所生活的这种累赘所阻碍。我包含着消极的能量，我生活在那些害怕我的人的心中。我还占据了身体物质的每一个原子和精神和身体能量的每一个单位的一半。如果我告诉你我是原子的负面部分，也许你会更好地理解我的本性。

Q Oh, I see what you are preparing to claim. You are laying the foundation to say that if it were not for you, there would be no world, no stars, no electrons, no atoms, no human beings, nothing. Is that correct?

哦，我知道你准备要求什么了。你正在奠定基础，说如果没有你，就不会有世界，没有星星，没有电子，没有原子，没有人类，什么都没有。是这样吗？

A True! Absolutely true.

A 是真的! 绝对是真的。

Q Well, if you only occupy one-half of energy and matter, who occupies the other half?

问: 如果你只占据了能量和物质的一半，那么谁占据了另一半呢？

A The other half is occupied by my opposition.

A 另一半被我的对手占据了。

Q Opposition? What do you mean?

问: 反对? 你是什么意思？

A The opposition is what you earthbound call God.

反对派就是你们俗称的上帝。

Q So you have the universe divided up with God. Is that your claim?

问: 所以你把宇宙和上帝分开了，这是你的主张吗？

A Not my claim, but the actual fact. Before this interview is finished you will understand why my claim is true. You will also understand why it has to be true, or there could be no world such as yours, no earthbound creatures such as you. I am no beast with a forked tongue and a spiked tail.

A 不是我的要求，而是实际的事实。在这次采访结束之前，你会明白为什么我的说法是正确的。你们也会明白为什么它必须是真实的，否则就不会有像你们这样的世界，没有像你们这样的地球生物。我不是那种长着分叉的舌头和尖尖的尾巴的野兽。

Q But you do control the minds of 98 out of every 100 people. You said so yourself. Who causes all the misery in this 98 percent Devil-controlled world, if you do not?

但是每100个人中就有98个人的思想是由你控制的。你自己说的。如果你不知道，是谁在这个98% 由魔鬼控制的世界里制造了所有的痛苦？

A I have not said that I do not cause all the misery of the world. On the other hand, I boast of it. It is my business to represent the negative side of everything, including the thoughts of you earthbound people. How else could I control people? My opposition controls positive thought. I control negative thought.

A 我没有说过我没有造成世界上所有的痛苦。另一方面，我以此为傲。我的工作就是代表一切事物的负面，包括你们这些地球人的思想。我还能怎么控制别人呢？我的反对者控制着积极的思想。我控制着消极的想法。

Q How do you gain control of the minds of people?

问: 你如何控制人们的思想？

A Oh, that is easy: I merely move in and occupy the unused space of the human brain. I sow the seeds of negative thought in the minds of people so I can occupy and control the space!

答: 哦，那很简单: 我只是搬进来，占据人类大脑未使用的空间。我在人们的头脑中播下消极思想的种子，这样我就可以占据和控制空间！

Q You must have many tricks and devices by which you gain and hold control of the human mind.

你一定有很多技巧和方法来获得和控制人类的思想。

A To be sure, I employ tricks and devices to control human thought. My devices are clever ones too.

可以肯定的是，我使用技巧和设备来控制人类的思想。我的设备也很聪明。

Q Go ahead and describe your clever tricks, Your Majesty.

请继续描述你的聪明把戏，陛下。

A One of my cleverest devices for mind control is fear. I plant the seed of fear in the minds of people, and as these seeds germinate and grow, through use, I control the space they occupy. The six most effective fears are the fear of poverty, criticism, ill health, loss of love, old age, and death.

恐惧是我最聪明的精神控制方法之一。我在人们的心中播下恐惧的种子，当这些种子发芽成长时，通过使用，我控制了他们所占据的空间。六种最有效的恐惧是对贫穷、批评、疾病、失去爱、衰老和死亡的恐惧。

Says the Devil: “One of my cleverest devices for mind control is fear . . . the fear of poverty, criticism, ill health, loss of love, old age, and death.”

魔鬼说: “我最聪明的精神控制方法之一就是恐惧... ... 对贫穷、批评、疾病、失去爱、衰老和死亡的恐惧。”

Q Which of these six fears serves you most often, Your Majesty?

问: 这六种恐惧中，哪一种是您最常见的，陛下？

A The first and the last—poverty and death! At one time or another during life I tighten my grip on all people through one or both of these. I plant these fears in the minds of people so deftly that they believe them to be their own creation. I accomplish this end by making people believe I am standing just beyond the entrance gate of the next life, waiting to claim them after death for eternal punishment. Of course I cannot punish anyone, except in that person’s own mind, through some form of fear—but fear of the thing which does not exist is just as useful to me as fear of that which does exist. All forms of fear extend the space I occupy in the human mind.

A 第一个也是最后一个ーー贫穷和死亡！在我一生中的某个时候，我通过这两种方式中的一种或两种方式加强了对所有人的控制。我如此巧妙地将这些恐惧植入人们的头脑，以至于他们相信这些恐惧是他们自己创造的。为了达到这个目的，我让人们相信我正站在来生的门口，等着在死后要求他们接受永恒的惩罚。当然，我不能通过某种形式的恐惧来惩罚任何人，除了那个人自己的心灵之外ーー但是对不存在的事物的恐惧对我来说就像对真实存在的事物的恐惧一样有用。所有形式的恐惧都扩展了我在人类心灵中所占据的空间。

Q Your Majesty, will you explain how you gained this control over human beings?

问: 陛下，您能否解释一下您是如何控制人类的？

A The story is too long to be told in a few words. It began over a million years ago, when the first man began to think. Up to that time I had control over all mankind, but enemies of mine discovered the power of positive thought, placed it in the minds of men, and then began a battle on my part to remain in control. So far, I have done quite well by myself, having lost only 2 percent of the people to the opposition.

A 这个故事太长了，不能用几个字来讲。它开始于一百多万年前，当时第一个人开始思考。到那时为止，我已经控制了全人类，但是我的敌人发现了积极思想的力量，把它植入了人类的头脑，然后开始了一场由我来控制的战斗。到目前为止，我自己做得很好，只有2% 的人被反对派夺去了生命。

Q I take it from your answer that men who think are your enemies. Is that right?

问: 我从你的回答中得知，那些认为你是敌人的人，是这样吗？

A It is not right, but it is correct.

A 这是不对的，但却是正确的。

Q Tell me something more about the world in which you live.

问: 告诉我更多关于你生活的世界的事情。

A I live wherever I choose. Time and space do not exist for me. I am a force best described to you as energy. My favorite physical dwelling place, as I have told you, is the minds of the earthbound. I control a part of the brain space of every human being. The amount of space I occupy in each individual’s mind depends upon how little and what sort of thinking that person does. As I have told you, I cannot entirely control any person who thinks.

A 我想住哪儿就住哪儿。时间和空间对我来说不存在。我是一种力量，对你来说最好的描述就是能量。我最喜欢的物理住所，正如我告诉过你们的，是地球人的思想。我控制着每个人大脑的一部分空间。我在每个人的头脑中占据的空间取决于这个人的思维空间有多少，以及这个人的思维方式如何。正如我已经告诉你的，我不能完全控制任何一个有思想的人。

Q You speak of your opposition. What do you mean by that?

问: 你说的是你的反对意见，这是什么意思？

A My opponent controls all the positive forces of the world, such as love, faith, hope, and optimism. My opponent also controls the positive factors of all natural law throughout the universe, the forces which keep the earth and the planets and all the stars balanced in their courses, but these forces are meek in comparison with those which operate in the human mind under my control. You see, I do not seek to control stars and planets. I prefer the control of human minds.

我的对手控制着世界上所有的积极力量，比如爱、信仰、希望和乐观。我的对手也控制着整个宇宙中所有自然法则的积极因素，这些力量使地球、行星和所有恒星在它们的运行过程中保持平衡，但是这些力量与那些在我控制下的人类头脑中运作的力量相比是温和的。你知道，我并不寻求控制恒星和行星。我更喜欢控制人类的思想。

Q Where did you acquire your power, and by what means do you add to it?

问: 你的能力是从哪里获得的，你是通过什么方式获得的？

A I add to my power by appropriating the mind-power of the earthbound, as they come through the gate at the time of death. Ninety-eight out of every 100 who come back to my plane from the earth plane are taken over by me and their mind-power is added to my being. I get all who come over with any form of fear. You see I am constantly at work, preparing the minds of people before death, so I can appropriate them when they come back to my plane.

我通过占有地上人的心灵力量来增加我的力量，因为他们在死亡之时通过了大门。每100个从地面回到我的飞机上的人中有98个被我接管，他们的心灵力量被加入到我的存在中。我知道所有带着任何形式的恐惧过来的人。你看，我一直在工作，让人们在死前做好心理准备，这样当他们回到我的飞机上时，我就可以占有他们。

Q Will you tell me how you go about your job of preparing human minds so you can control them?

问: 你能告诉我你是如何开展你的工作，准备人类的思想，以便你可以控制它们吗？

A I have countless ways of gaining control of human minds while they are still on the earth plane. My greatest weapon is poverty. I deliberately discourage people from accumulating material wealth because poverty discourages men from thinking and makes them easy prey for me. My next best friend is ill health. An unhealthy body discourages thinking. Then I have countless thousands of workers on earth who aid me in gaining control of human minds. I have these agents placed in every calling. They represent every race and creed, every religion.

A 我有无数种方法可以在人类还在地球上的时候控制他们的思想。我最大的武器就是贫穷。我故意阻止人们积累物质财富，因为贫穷使人们不敢思考，使他们很容易成为我的猎物。我的下一个最好的朋友是身体不好。不健康的身体不鼓励思考。然后我在地球上有无数的工人帮助我控制人类的思想。我在每个电话里都安排了这些探员。他们代表着每一个种族、信仰和宗教。

Q Who are your greatest enemies on earth, Your Majesty?

问: 陛下，你在这个世界上最大的敌人是谁？

A All who inspire people to think and act on their own initiative are my enemies. Such men as Socrates, Confucius, Voltaire, Emerson, Thomas Paine, and Abraham Lincoln. And you are not doing me any good either.

凡是激励人们主动思考和行动的人都是我的敌人。诸如苏格拉底、孔子、伏尔泰、爱默生、托马斯 · 潘恩和亚伯拉罕 · 林肯。你对我也没什么好处。

Q Is it true that you use men who have great wealth?

问: 你真的雇佣那些有钱人吗？

A As I have already told you, poverty is always my friend because it discourages independence of thought and encourages fear in the minds of men. Some wealthy men serve my cause while others do me great damage, depending upon how the wealth is used. The great Rockefeller fortune, for example, is one of my worst enemies.

A 正如我已经告诉过你的，贫穷永远是我的朋友，因为它阻碍思想的独立性，鼓励人们心中的恐惧。一些有钱人为我服务，而另一些人则根据财富的使用方式对我造成巨大的伤害。例如，洛克菲勒的巨额财富就是我最大的敌人之一。

Q That is interesting, Your Majesty; will you tell me why you fear the Rockefeller fortune more than others?

问: 这很有趣，陛下，你能告诉我为什么你比其他人更害怕洛克菲勒的财富吗？

A The Rockefeller money is being used to isolate and conquer diseases of the physical body, in all parts of the world. Disease has always been one of my most effective weapons. The fear of ill health is second only to the fear of poverty. The Rockefeller money is uncovering new secrets of nature in a hundred different directions, all of which are designed to help men take and keep possession of their own minds. It is encouraging new and better methods of feeding, clothing, and housing people. It is wiping out the slums in the large cities, the places where my favorite allies are found. It is financing campaigns for better government and helping to wipe out dishonesty in politics. It is helping to set higher standards in business practice and encouraging business men to conduct business by the Golden Rule; and that is not doing my cause any good.

A 洛克菲勒的钱被用来孤立和征服世界各地的肉体疾病。疾病一直是我最有效的武器之一。对疾病的恐惧仅次于对贫穷的恐惧。洛克菲勒的资金正在从上百个不同的方向揭示新的自然秘密，所有这些秘密都是为了帮助人们掌握和保持自己的思想。它鼓励新的和更好的方法喂养，衣服和住房的人。它正在清除大城市中的贫民窟，我最喜欢的盟友就是在这些地方找到的。它为更好的政府运动提供资金，并帮助铲除政治上的不诚实行为。它有助于提高商业实践的标准，并鼓励商人按照黄金法则经营业务; 这对我的事业没有任何好处。

Q What about these boys and girls who are said to be on the road to hell? Are you in control of them?

问: 那些据说正在通往地狱之路上的男孩和女孩呢？你能控制他们吗？

A Well, I can answer that question only with “yes and no.” I have corrupted the minds of the young by teaching them to drink and smoke, but they have me baffled through their tendency to think for themselves.

A 哦，我只能用“是”和“不是”来回答这个问题我教年轻人喝酒抽烟，使他们的思想堕落，但他们独立思考的倾向却让我感到困惑。

Hill ranges back and forth across the Devil’s field of battle. His earlier point about Rockefeller’s philanthropy is followed by an explanation of why young people are “on the road to hell.” I believe the author is challenging us to hold several ideas in mind at once as he lets the Devil do his dirty work with the hope of confusing us. Look for other examples throughout the book—you’ll find them!

希尔在魔鬼的战场上来回奔跑。在他早些时候关于洛克菲勒的慈善事业的观点之后，他解释了为什么年轻人“在通往地狱的路上”我相信作者是在挑战我们，让我们同时记住几个想法，因为他让魔鬼做他的肮脏的工作，希望迷惑我们。在整本书中寻找其他的例子ーー你会找到的！

Q You say you have corrupted the minds of the young people with liquor and cigarettes. I can understand how liquor might destroy the power of independent thought but do not see what cigarettes have to do with helping your cause.

问: 你说你用烟酒腐蚀了年轻人的思想。我能理解酒精如何摧毁独立思考的力量，但是我不明白香烟对你的事业有什么帮助。

A You may not know it, but cigarettes break down the power of persistence; they destroy the power of endurance; they destroy the ability to concentrate; they deaden and undermine the imaginative faculty, and help in other ways to keep people from using their minds most effectively.

你可能不知道，但是香烟打破了坚持的力量; 它们摧毁了耐力的力量; 它们摧毁了集中注意力的能力; 它们削弱和破坏了想象力的能力，并且在其他方面帮助阻止人们最有效地使用他们的思想。

Do you know I have millions of people, young and old, of both sexes, who smoke two packages of cigarettes a day? That means I have millions of people who are gradually destroying their power of resistance.

你知道吗，我有成千上万的人，无论男女老少，每天抽两包烟？这意味着我有数百万人正在逐渐摧毁他们的抵抗力量。

One day I shall add to their habit of cigarette smoking other thought-destroying habits, until I shall have gained control of their minds.

总有一天我会在他们吸烟的习惯上加上其他破坏思想的习惯，直到我能够控制他们的思想。

Habits come in pairs, triplets, and quadruplets. Any habit which weakens one’s will power invites a flock of its relatives to move in and take possession of the mind. The cigarette habit not only lowers the power of resistance and discourages persistence, but it invites looseness in other human relationships.

习惯是成对的、三胞胎的和四胞胎的。任何削弱一个人意志力的习惯都会招致一群它的亲戚进入并占有心灵。吸烟的习惯不仅降低了抵抗的力量，阻碍了坚持不懈的精神，而且还会导致其他人际关系的疏远。

Q I never thought that cigarettes were a tool of destruction, Your Majesty, but your explanation throws a different light on the subject. How many converts to the habit do you now claim?

我从来没有想过香烟是毁灭的工具，陛下，但是您的解释给这个问题带来了不同的解释。你现在声称有多少人改变了这个习惯？

A I am proud of my record. Millions are now victims, and the number is increasing daily. Soon I shall have most of the world indulging in the habit. In thousands of families I now have followers of the habit, including every member of the family. Very young boys and girls are beginning to take up the habit. They are learning how to smoke by observing their parents and older brothers and sisters.

A 我为我的记录感到骄傲。现在有数百万人成为受害者，而且这个数字每天都在增加。很快我就会让世界上大部分人都沉溺于这种习惯。在成千上万的家庭里，我现在有了这个习惯的追随者，包括家里的每一个成员。很小的男孩和女孩开始养成这个习惯。他们通过观察父母和哥哥姐姐来学习如何吸烟。

Q Which do you consider to be your greater tool for gaining control of human minds—cigarettes or liquor?

问: 你认为哪种工具是你控制人类思想的更好的工具? 香烟还是酒？

A Without hesitation I would say cigarettes. Once I get a young person to join my two-package-a-day club, I have no trouble in inducing that person to take on the habit of liquor, over-indulgence of sex, and all other related habits which destroy independence of thought and action.

A 我会毫不犹豫地说香烟。一旦我让一个年轻人加入我的一天两包的俱乐部，我就可以毫不费力地让他染上酗酒、过度纵欲以及所有其他相关的习惯，这些习惯会破坏他独立思考和行动的能力。

Remember, this was written in 1938—long before the addictive nature of tobacco was discovered. Here, as elsewhere, Napoleon Hill is far ahead of his time in some of his medical and sociological opinions.

记住，这是在1938年写的，远在烟草成瘾性被发现之前。这里，和其他地方一样，拿破仑 · 希尔在他的一些医学和社会学观点上远远领先于他的时代。

Q Your Majesty, when I began this interview I had you all wrong. I thought you were a fraud and a fake, but I see now that you are quite real and very powerful.

问: 陛下，当我开始这次采访时，我完全误解了您。我原以为你是个骗子，是个骗子，但是现在我看到你是真实的，而且非常强大。

A Your apology is accepted, but you need not have bothered. Millions of people have questioned my power, and I got most of them at the gate as they came over.

A 我们接受你的道歉，但你不必为此烦恼。数以百万计的人质疑我的力量，他们来的时候，我在大门口抓住了他们中的大多数。

I ask no person to believe in me. I prefer that people fear me. I am no beggar! I take what I want by cleverness and force. Begging people to believe is the business of my opposition— not mine.

我不要求任何人相信我。我宁愿人们害怕我。我不是乞丐！我用聪明和武力夺取我想要的东西。恳求人们相信是我的反对意见，而不是我的。

Q Your Majesty will please pardon my rudeness, but I would not be able to look myself in the face again if I did not tell you, here and now, that you are the damnedest fiend ever to be turned loose on innocent people.

女王陛下请原谅我的粗鲁，但是如果我不在此时此地告诉您，您是有史以来对无辜的人放任自流的最大恶魔，我将无法再面对自己。

I always had the wrong conception of you. I thought you were kind enough to let people alone while they were living, that you merely tortured their souls after death. Now I learn, from your own brazen confession, that you destroy their right to freedom of thought and cause them to go through a living hell on earth. What do you have to say to that?

我一直对你有错误的看法。我以为你很善良，让人们活着的时候，你只是在他们死后折磨他们的灵魂。现在我从你自己厚颜无耻的忏悔中得知，你破坏了他们思想自由的权利，使他们在人间经历一个活地狱。你有什么要说的吗？

A I get what I want by exercising self-control. It is not so good for my own business, but I suggest you emulate me instead of criticizing me. You call yourself a thinker, and you are. Otherwise you would never have forced this interview on me. But you will never be the sort of thinker that frightens me unless you gain and exercise greater control over your own emotions.

A 我通过锻炼自我控制来得到我想要的东西。这对我自己的事业不利，但我建议你学习我，而不是批评我。你称自己是一个思想家，你确实是。否则你永远不会强迫我接受这次采访。但是，除非你能更好地控制自己的情绪，否则你永远不会成为那种让我害怕的思考者。

Q Let us get away from personalities. I came here to learn more about you, not to discuss myself. Please go ahead and tell me of the many tricks you have devised for gaining control of the human mind. What is your most powerful weapon just now?

让我们远离个性。我来这里是为了更多地了解你，而不是讨论我自己。请继续，告诉我你为了控制人类思想而设计的许多技巧。你刚才最厉害的武器是什么？

A That is a difficult question to answer. I have so many devices for entering human minds and controlling them that it is difficult to say which are the most powerful. Right at the moment I am trying to bring about another world war. My friends here in Washington are helping me to involve America in the war. If I can start the world to killing on a wholesale basis, I shall be able to put into operation my favorite device for mind control. It is what you may call mass fear. I used this device to bring about the other World War in 1914. I used it to bring about the economic depression in 1929, and if my opposition had not double-crossed me I would now be in possession of every man, woman, and child in the world. You can see for yourself how near I came to world domination—the thing I have been struggling to attain for thousands of years.

A 这是一个很难回答的问题。我有这么多的设备进入人类的思想和控制他们，很难说哪一个是最强大的。此时此刻，我正试图引发另一场世界大战。我在华盛顿的朋友们正在帮助我把美国卷入战争。如果我可以让这个世界大规模地杀戮，我就可以把我最喜欢的精神控制装置投入使用。这就是所谓的大规模恐惧。我用这个装置在1914年引发了另一场世界大战。我利用它在1929年带来了经济萧条，如果我的反对没有出卖我，我现在拥有世界上的每一个男人，女人和孩子。你可以亲眼看到我是多么接近统治世界ーー这是我为之奋斗了几千年的事情。

Here the Devil claims to be working with both sides to instigate war, based on his sowing the seeds of fear throughout the world. This is the essence of what has come to be known in our time as terrorism—and the response to it. Through Hill’s work the Devil takes credit for not only both World Wars but also the Great Depression . . . it is easy to add the current economic collapse to his list of credits. Both war and economic collapse breed fear in people’s minds and are certainly the work of the Devil.

在这里，魔鬼宣称正与双方一起煽动战争，基于他在全世界播下恐惧的种子。这就是我们这个时代所谓的恐怖主义的本质ーー以及对恐怖主义的回应。通过希尔的作品，魔鬼不仅因为两次世界大战，还因为大萧条而获得赞誉... ... 很容易把目前的经济崩溃加入到他的信用列表中。战争和经济崩溃都在人们的心中滋生恐惧，这无疑是魔鬼的杰作。

Q Yes, I see your point. Who wouldn’t? You are a very ingenious manipulator of the minds of people. Is your devilish business carried on only through people of high position and great influence?

是的，我明白你的意思。谁不会呢？你是一个非常巧妙地操纵人们思想的人。你的魔鬼生意是不是只有通过身居高位、有很大影响力的人才能进行？

A Oh, no! I use the minds of people in all walks of life. As a matter of fact, I prefer the type of person who makes no pretense of thinking; I can manipulate that sort of person without difficulty. I could not control 98 percent of the people of the world if all people were skilled in thinking for themselves.

A 哦，不！我运用各行各业人们的思想。事实上，我更喜欢那种不假装思考的人; 我可以毫不费力地操纵那种人。如果所有人都有独立思考的能力，我就无法控制世界上98% 的人。

Q I am interested in the welfare of those people whom you claim to control. Therefore, I wish you to tell me all of the tricks by which you enter and control their minds. I want a complete confession from you, so begin with your cleverest trick.

问: 我对你声称控制的那些人的福利感兴趣。因此，我希望你能告诉我你进入并控制他们思想的所有技巧。我想从你那里得到一个完整的坦白，所以从你最聪明的把戏开始吧。

A This is suicide you are forcing on me, but I am helpless! So settle down and I will place in your hands the weapon by which millions of your fellow-earthbound will defend themselves against me.

这是你强加给我的自杀，但我无能为力！所以你们要安定下来，我要把你们手中的武器交给你们，你们地上的百万同胞就可以用这武器来抵御我。





Chapter Four

DRIFTING WITH THE DEVIL

第四章与魔鬼同游

Q TELL ME FIRST ABOUT YOUR MOST CLEVER TRICK—the one you use to ensnare the greatest number of people.

问: 首先告诉我你最聪明的把戏ーー你用来诱捕最多人的把戏。

A If you force me to give away this secret, it will mean my loss of millions of people now living and still greater numbers of millions as yet unborn. I beg of you, permit me to pass this one question unanswered.

A 如果你强迫我泄露这个秘密，那将意味着我失去数百万现在活着的人，以及更多尚未出生的数百万人。请允许我回答这个问题。

Q So His Majesty the Devil fears a mere humble earthbound creature! Is that right?

问: 所以，魔鬼陛下害怕的只是一个卑微的地下生物! 是这样吗？

A It is not right, but it is true. You have no right to rob me of my most necessary tool of trade. For millions of years I have dominated earthbound creatures through fear and ignorance. Now you come along and would destroy my use of these weapons by forcing me to tell how I use them. Do you not realize that you will break my grip on every person who heeds this confession you are forcing from me? Have you no mercy? Have you no sense of humor? Have you no sportsmanship?

A 这是不对的，但这是事实。你无权夺走我最需要的贸易工具。数百万年来，我通过恐惧和无知统治着地球上的生物。现在你出现了，要强迫我说出我是如何使用这些武器的，从而破坏我对它们的使用。你难道没有意识到你会打破我对每一个听从你强迫我认罪的人的控制吗？难道你没有怜悯之心吗？你没有幽默感吗？你没有运动员精神吗？

Q Stop stalling, and start confessing. Who are you to ask mercy of one whom you would destroy if you could? Who are you to talk of sportsmanship and a sense of humor? You, who by your own confession have set up a living hell on earth, where you punish innocent people through their fears and ignorance. As for minding my own business, that is just what I am doing when I force you to tell how you control people through their own minds. My business, if it can be called a business, is helping to unlock the doors of the self-made prisons in which men and women are confined because of the fears you have planted in their minds.

停止拖延，开始坦白。你有什么资格向一个如果你可以的话你会毁灭的人求饶？你凭什么谈论体育精神和幽默感？你，你自己承认在人间建立了一个活地狱，你通过无辜的人们的恐惧和无知来惩罚他们。至于我自己的事情，当我强迫你告诉别人你是如何通过他们自己的思想来控制别人的时候，这正是我在做的。我的工作，如果可以称之为工作的话，就是帮助打开那些白手起家的监狱的大门，在这些监狱里，由于你在他们心中种下的恐惧，男人和女人都被关在里面。

Mr. Earthbound has the power to force the Devil to answer his questions. His own knowledge of independent thought and lack of fear are his weapons to force this confession.

地缚先生有能力迫使魔鬼回答他的问题。他自己对独立思考的认识和缺乏恐惧是他迫使自己认罪的武器。

A My greatest weapon over human beings consists of two secret principles by which I gain control of their minds. I will speak first of the principle of habit, through which I silently enter the minds of people. By operating through this principle, I establish (I wish I could avoid using this word) the habit of drifting. When a person begins to drift on any subject, he is headed straight toward the gates of what you earthbound call hell.

我对人类最伟大的武器包括两个秘密的原则，通过这两个原则我可以控制他们的思想。首先，我要谈谈习惯的原则，通过这个原则，我可以静静地进入人们的思想。通过运用这个原则，我建立了(我希望我可以避免使用这个词)随波逐流的习惯。当一个人开始在任何问题上飘忽不定时，他就直接走向你们地球人所说的地狱之门。

Q Describe all the ways in which you induce people to drift. Define the word and tell us exactly what you mean by it.

描述你诱使人们随波逐流的所有方式。定义这个词并准确地告诉我们你的意思。

A I can best define the word “drift” by saying that people who think for themselves never drift, while those who do little or no thinking for themselves are drifters. A drifter is one who permits himself to be influenced and controlled by circumstances outside of his own mind. He would rather let me occupy his mind and do his thinking than go to the trouble of thinking for himself. A drifter is one who accepts whatever life throws in his way without making a protest or putting up a fight. He doesn’t know what he wants from life and spends all of his time getting just that. A drifter has lots of opinions, but they are not his own. Most of them are supplied by me.

A 我对“漂移”这个词的最好定义是: 独立思考的人永远不会漂移，而那些很少或根本没有独立思考的人就是“漂移者”。一个流浪汉是一个允许自己被他自己心灵之外的环境所影响和控制的人。他宁愿让我占据他的思想去做他的思考，也不愿自己费力去思考。一个流浪汉是一个能够接受生活中发生的任何事情而不去抗议或者反抗的人。他不知道自己想从生活中得到什么，他花了所有的时间去得到这些。一个流浪汉有很多意见，但这些意见不是他自己的。大部分都是我提供的。

A drifter is one who is too lazy mentally to use his own brain. That is the reason I can take control of people’s thinking and plant my own ideas in their minds.

一个流浪汉是一个在思想上太懒以至于不用自己的大脑的人。这就是为什么我可以控制人们的思想，并在他们的头脑中植入我自己的想法。

“Those who do little or no thinking for themselves are drifters. A drifter is one who permits himself to be influenced and controlled by circumstances outside of his own mind.”

“那些很少或根本不为自己考虑的人是流浪者。一个流浪汉是一个允许自己被自己思想之外的环境所影响和控制的人。”

Q I think I understand what a drifter is. Tell me the exact habits of people by which you induce them to drift through life. Start by telling me when and how you first gain control of a person’s mind.

问: 我想我知道什么是流浪汉。请告诉我你引导人们在生活中随波逐流的确切习惯。首先告诉我你什么时候以及如何第一次控制一个人的思想。

A My control over the mind of a human being is obtained while the person is young. Sometimes I lay the foundation for my control of a mind before the owner of it is born, by manipulating the minds of that person’s parents. Sometimes I go further back than this and prepare people for my control through what you earthbound call “physical heredity.” You see, therefore, I have two approaches to the mind of a person.

当一个人还年轻的时候，我就可以控制他的思想。有时候，我通过操纵一个人的父母的思想，为在他出生之前控制他的思想奠定基础。有时候我会回到比这更久远的时代，让人们准备好接受我的控制，通过你们地球上所谓的“身体遗传”你看，因此，我对一个人的思想有两种看法。

Q Yes. Go on and describe these two doors by which you enter and control the minds of human beings.

问: 是的。继续描述你进入并控制人类思想的这两扇门。

A As I have stated, I help to bring people into your world with weak brains by giving to them, before birth, as many as possible of the weaknesses of their ancestors. You call this principle “physical heredity.” After people are born I make use of what you earthbound call “environment” as a means of controlling them. This is where the principle of habit enters. The mind is nothing more than the sum total of one’s habits! One by one I enter the mind and establish habits, which lead finally to my absolute domination of the mind.

答: 正如我已经说过的，我帮助那些大脑薄弱的人进入你们的世界，在他们出生之前，尽可能多地告诉他们祖先的弱点。你把这个原理叫做“身体遗传”人们出生后，我利用你们地球上所谓的“环境”作为控制他们的手段。这就是习惯的原理。心灵不过是一个人习惯的总和！我一个接一个地进入头脑并建立起习惯，这最终导致我对头脑的绝对控制。

Q Tell me of the most common habits by which you control the minds of people.

问: 告诉我你控制别人思想的最常见的习惯。

A That is one of my cleverest tricks: I enter the minds of people through thoughts which they believe to be their own. Those most useful to me are fear, superstition, avarice, greed, lust, revenge, anger, vanity, and plain laziness. Through one or more of these I can enter any mind, at any age, but I get my best results when I take charge of a mind while it is young, before its owner has learned how to close any of these nine doors. Then I can set up habits which keep the doors ajar forever.

这是我最聪明的伎俩之一: 我通过人们认为是他们自己的思想进入他们的头脑。对我最有用的是恐惧、迷信、贪婪、贪婪、色欲、复仇、愤怒、虚荣和懒惰。通过其中的一个或多个，我可以进入任何思想，在任何年龄，但是当我掌控一个思想的时候，在它的主人还没有学会如何关上这九扇门之前，我就可以得到最好的结果。然后我就可以养成习惯，让门永远敞开着。

Q I am catching on to your methods. Now let us go back to the habit of drifting. Tell us all about that habit since you say it is your cleverest trick in controlling the minds of people.

问: 我正在学习你的方法。现在让我们回到漂流的习惯。告诉我们关于这个习惯的一切，因为你说这是你在控制别人思想方面最聪明的伎俩。

A As I said before, I start people drifting during their youth. I induce them to drift through school without knowing what occupation they wish to follow in life. Here I catch the majority of people. Habits are related. Drift in one direction and soon you will be drifting in all directions. I also use environmental habits to give me a definite grip on my victims.

A 正如我之前所说，我在人们年轻的时候就开始漂泊。我诱导他们在学校里漂泊，不知道他们想从事什么职业。在这里，我抓住了大多数人。习惯是相关的。朝一个方向漂移，很快你就会向四面八方漂移。我也利用环境习惯来帮助我抓住我的受害者。

Q I see. You make it your business to train children in the habit of drifting by inducing them to go through school without aim or purpose. Now tell me of some of your other tricks with which you cause people to become drifters.

我明白了。你把培养孩子漂泊的习惯作为你的工作，引导他们毫无目的地去上学。现在告诉我你其他一些使人们成为流浪者的技巧。

A Well, my second best trick in developing the habit of drifting is one that I put into operation with the aid of parents and public schoolteachers and religious instructors.

A 哦，我培养漂流习惯的第二个最好的方法是我在家长、公立学校老师和宗教教师的帮助下实施的方法。

I warn you not to force me to mention this trick. Do not disclose this trick. If you do so, you will be hated by my co-workers who help me use this trick. If you publish this confession in book form, your book will be barred from the public schools. It will be blacklisted by most of the religious leaders. It will be hidden from children by many parents. The newspapers will not dare to give reviews of your book. Millions of people will hate you for writing the book.

我警告你不要强迫我提这个把戏。不要透露这种伎俩。如果你这样做了，你将会被我的同事们所憎恨，他们帮助我使用这个技巧。如果你以书的形式出版这份忏悔书，你的书将被禁止进入公立学校。它将被大多数宗教领袖列入黑名单。许多父母都会对孩子隐瞒这一点。报纸不敢给你的书写评论。成千上万的人会因为你写了这本书而恨你。

In fact, no one will like you or your book except those who think, and you know how very few there are of this sort! My advice to you is to let me skip the description of my second best trick.

事实上，除了那些会思考的人，没有人会喜欢你或你的书，你知道这样的人是多么的少！我给你的建议是，让我跳过我的第二个最好的技巧的描述。

The author knew this opinion would be one of the most controversial aspects of his book. In fact, his wife was so concerned about how it would be received that she made him promise that he would not publish it. In fact, it is only now, well after her death, that the family has agreed to share it with the world. I would encourage you to follow Hill’s argument about the public education system and religious teachers and then decide for yourself.

作者知道这个观点将是他的书中最具争议的方面之一。事实上，他的妻子非常担心人们会怎么看待这本书，所以她让他保证不出版这本书。事实上，直到现在，在她去世很久之后，这个家庭才同意与全世界分享。我鼓励你们跟随希尔关于公共教育系统和宗教教师的观点，然后自己做决定。

Q So for my own good you wish to withhold the description of your second best trick. No one will like my book except those who think, eh? Very well, go ahead and answer.

所以为了我好，你希望不要描述你第二好的把戏。没有人会喜欢我的书，除了那些思考的人，嗯？很好，继续回答。

A You’ll regret this, Mr. Earthbound, but the joke is on you. By this mistake of yours you will divert attention from me to yourself. My co-workers, of whom there are millions, will forget about me and hate you for uncovering my methods.

A 你会为此后悔的，地缚先生，但这是在开你的玩笑。你犯了这个错误，会把注意力从我身上转移到你自己身上。我的同事，他们有数百万人，会忘记我，恨你揭露我的手段。

Q Never mind about me. Tell me all about this second best trick of yours with which you induce people to drift with you to hell.

问: 别管我。告诉我所有关于你的第二个最好的伎俩，你诱使人们与你漂移到地狱。

A My second best trick is not second at all. It is first! It is first because without it I never could gain control of the minds of the youths. Parents, schoolteachers, religious instructors, and many other adults unknowingly serve my purpose by helping me to destroy in children the habit of thinking for themselves. They go about their work in various ways, never suspecting what they are doing to the minds of children or the real cause of the children’s mistakes.

A 我第二好的魔术一点也不是第二好的。这是第一个！首先是因为没有它，我永远无法控制年轻人的思想。父母、学校老师、宗教导师和许多其他成年人在不知不觉中帮助我摧毁孩子们自己思考的习惯，从而达到我的目的。他们以各种各样的方式工作，从不怀疑他们对孩子们的思想做了什么，也不怀疑孩子们犯错误的真正原因。

Have you ever heard a parent finish a child’s sentence? Or seen a parent complete a child’s homework? Remember those science fairs at school where it was obvious the kids had a lot of outside “help” with their science projects? Mom and Dad may have “helped” a little too much, but deep down they know that their child appreciates the help and recognizes what great parents they are. Right? Actually, the child may be thinking, “Mom and Dad don’t think I can do it on my own . . . so why bother!” Eventually this parental “help” will destroy the child’s self-confidence. By allowing children to be truly in charge, parents will help their kids develop the habit of thinking for themselves!

你有没有听过父母为孩子说完一句话？或者看到父母完成孩子的家庭作业？还记得在学校的科学展览会上，很明显孩子们在科学项目上得到了很多外界的“帮助”吗？妈妈和爸爸可能有点“帮助”太多了，但在内心深处他们知道他们的孩子感激帮助，并认识到他们是多么伟大的父母。对吧？实际上，孩子可能会想，“爸爸妈妈认为我一个人做不了... ... 所以为什么要这么麻烦呢! ”最终，这种父母的“帮助”会摧毁孩子的自信。通过让孩子真正负责，父母将帮助他们养成独立思考的习惯！

Q I can hardly believe you, Your Majesty. I have always believed that children’s best friends were those closest to them, their parents, their school teachers, and their religious instructors. Where would children go for dependable guidance if not to those who have charge of them?

我简直不敢相信你，陛下。我一直相信孩子们最好的朋友就是他们最亲近的人，他们的父母，他们的老师，他们的宗教导师。如果不是向那些负责他们的人寻求可靠的指导，孩子们会去哪里呢？

A That is where my cleverness comes in. There is the exact explanation of how I control 98 percent of the people of the world. I take possession of people during their youth, before they come into possession of their own minds, by using those who are in charge of them. I especially need the help of those who give children their religious instruction, because it is here that I break down independent thought and start people on the habit of drifting, by confusing their minds with unprovable ideas concerning a world of which they know nothing. It is here also that I plant in the minds of children the greatest of all fears—the fear of hell!

A 这就是我聪明的地方。对于我如何控制世界上98% 的人，有一个确切的解释。我在人们年轻的时候，在他们掌握自己的思想之前，就利用那些掌管他们的人来占有他们。我特别需要那些给孩子们提供宗教教育的人的帮助，因为正是在这里，我打破了独立的思想，让人们养成了漂泊不定的习惯，把他们的思想和一个他们一无所知的世界的无法证明的想法混为一谈。也正是在这里，我在孩子们的心中种下了最大的恐惧ーー对地狱的恐惧！

Q I understand that it is easy for you to frighten children with threats of hell, but how do you continue to make them fear you and your hell after they grow up and learn to think for themselves?

问: 我知道你很容易用地狱的威胁来吓唬孩子，但是在他们长大并学会独立思考之后，你如何继续让他们害怕你和你的地狱呢？

A Children grow up, but they do not always learn to think for themselves! Once I capture the mind of a child, through fear, I weaken that child’s ability to reason and to think for himself, and that weakness goes with the child all through life.

一个孩子长大了，但他们并不总是学会独立思考！一旦我通过恐惧俘获了一个孩子的心灵，我就削弱了这个孩子的推理和独立思考的能力，而这种弱点会伴随这个孩子一生。

Q Is that not taking unfair advantage of a human being by contaminating his mind before he comes into full possession of it?

问: 在一个人完全拥有自己的思想之前，污染他的思想，这不是在不公平地占他的便宜吗？

A Everything is fair that I can use to further my ends. I have no foolish limitations of right and wrong. Might is right with me. I use every known human weakness to gain and keep control of the human mind.

一切都是公平的，我可以用它来达到我的目的。我对是非没有愚蠢的限制。强权与我同在。我利用每一个已知的人类弱点来获得并保持对人类思想的控制。

Q I understand your devilish nature! Now let us get back to further discussion of your methods of inducing people to drift to hell here on earth. From your confession I see that you take charge of children while their minds are young and pliable. Tell me more of how you use parents, teachers, and religious leaders to ensnare people into drifting.

我明白你的邪恶本性！现在让我们回到进一步讨论你诱导人们漂移到地球上地狱的方法。从你的忏悔中我可以看出，你在孩子们头脑还年轻柔软的时候就照顾他们。告诉我更多你是如何利用父母、老师和宗教领袖诱使人们漂泊的。

A One of my favorite tricks is to coordinate the efforts of parents and religious instructors so they work together in helping me to destroy the children’s power to think for themselves. I use many religious instructors to undermine the courage and power of independent thought of children, by teaching them to fear me; but I use parents to aid the religious leaders in this great work of mine.

我最喜欢的一个技巧是协调父母和宗教导师的努力，让他们一起帮助我摧毁孩子们独立思考的能力。我利用许多宗教导师来削弱孩子们独立思考的勇气和力量，教他们害怕我; 但是我利用父母来帮助宗教领袖完成我的伟大工作。

Q How do parents help religious leaders destroy their children’s power to think for themselves? I never heard of such a monstrosity!

问: 父母如何帮助宗教领袖摧毁孩子独立思考的能力？我从来没有听说过这样一个怪物！

A I accomplish this through a very clever trick. I cause the parents to teach their children to believe as the parents do in connection with religion, politics, marriage, and other important subjects. In this way, as you can see, when I gain control of the mind of a person I can easily perpetuate the control by causing that person to help me fasten it upon the minds of his offspring.

A 我通过一个非常聪明的技巧完成了这个任务。我促使父母教导他们的孩子相信，就像父母在宗教、政治、婚姻和其他重要问题上所做的那样。如你所见，通过这种方式，当我控制一个人的思想时，我可以很容易地通过让那个人帮助我把这种控制固定在他后代的思想上来延续这种控制。

Q In what other ways do you use parents to convert children into drifters?

问: 你还用其他什么方法让父母把孩子变成流浪者？

A I cause children to become drifters by following the example of their parents, most of whom I have already taken over and bound eternally to my cause. In some parts of the world I gain mastery over children’s minds and subdue their will power in exactly the same way that men break and subdue animals of lower intelligence. It makes no difference to me how a child’s will is subdued, as long as it fears something. I will enter its mind through that fear and limit the child’s power to think independently.

A 我效法他们的父母，使他们的孩子成为流浪者，我已经接管了他们中的大多数，并且永远与我的事业紧密相连。在世界上的一些地方，我获得了控制孩子们的思想和征服他们意志力的权力，就像人类征服和征服低智力的动物一样。对我来说，只要孩子害怕什么，他的意志是如何被压抑的，这没有什么区别。我会通过这种恐惧进入孩子的大脑，限制孩子独立思考的能力。

The Devil will enter a child’s mind through fear and then limit the child’s power to think independently. I can remember the many religious leaders I have known in the past and instantly divide them between fear-based instructors and faith-based instructors. In fact, I still get a chill from reliving the “fire and brimstone” of some of the fear-based sermons I heard as a child. In contrast, I remember the uplifted feeling of hope and courage from the faith-based sermons. Hill’s words of wisdom certainly ring true for me. Does fear then paralyze independent thought?

魔鬼会通过恐惧进入孩子的心灵，然后限制孩子独立思考的能力。我还记得我过去认识的许多宗教领袖，他们会立即把他们分为基于恐惧的教师和基于信仰的教师。事实上，当我回想起我小时候听到的一些恐惧布道的“火与硫磺”时，我仍然会感到一阵寒意。相比之下，我记得基于信仰的布道所带来的希望和勇气的升华感。希尔的至理名言对我来说当然是真理。恐惧会麻痹独立思考吗？

Q It seems that you go out of your way to keep people from thinking?

问: 看起来你竭尽全力阻止别人思考？

A Yes. Accurate thought is death to me. I cannot exist in the minds of those who think accurately. I do not mind people thinking as long as they think in terms of fear, discouragement, hopelessness, and destructiveness. When they begin to think in constructive terms of faith, courage, hope, and definiteness of purpose, they immediately become allies of my opposition and are therefore lost to me.

A 是的。准确的思想对我来说就是死亡。我无法存在于那些思维准确的人的头脑中。我不介意人们用恐惧、沮丧、绝望和破坏性的方式思考。当他们开始以建设性的方式思考信念、勇气、希望和明确的目标时，他们立即成为我反对派的盟友，因此对我来说就失去了意义。

Q I am beginning to understand how you gain control of the minds of children through the help of their parents and religious instructors, but I do not see how the schoolteachers help you in this damnable work.

问: 我开始明白你是如何通过孩子的父母和宗教导师的帮助来控制他们的思想的，但是我不明白学校老师是如何在这该死的工作中帮助你的。

A Schoolteachers help me gain control of the minds of children not so much by what they teach the children as because of what they do not teach them. The entire public school system is so administered that it helps my cause by teaching children almost everything except how to use their own minds and think independently. I live in fear that someday some courageous person will reverse the present system of school teaching and deal my cause a death blow by allowing the students to become the instructors, using those who now serve as teachers only as guides to help the children establish ways and means of developing their own minds from within. When that time comes, the schoolteachers will no longer belong to my staff.

教师帮助我控制孩子们的思想，与其说是因为他们教给孩子们什么，不如说是因为他们没有教给他们什么。整个公立学校系统的管理是如此严格，以至于除了教孩子们如何使用自己的思想和独立思考之外，几乎所有的事情都教给他们，这对我的事业是有帮助的。我生活在恐惧之中，害怕有一天某个勇敢的人会扭转现有的学校教育体系，让学生成为教师，利用那些现在只是作为指导的教师来帮助孩子们建立从内在发展自己思想的方式和方法，从而对我造成致命的打击。到那个时候，那些老师就不再属于我的员工了。

Here is the essence of Hill’s critique of public education, written in 1938. Do you agree with him? Think of young children during kindergarten and first grade. They are enthusiastic and volunteer for everything, raising their hands and excited to learn. Now fast-forward ten years, and think about those same children as high school students—the ones sitting in the back of the class, never making eye contact with adults, and absolutely never volunteering or asking a question. They have disengaged from the learning process. What happened to these children? Ten years of schooling. They perceive that to make an error will subject them to ridicule and scorn. So they cease to participate in order to protect themselves. They are taught that the solutions to all problems and conflicts lie not in their own hands and minds, but in the hands and mind of the teacher—the representative of the authorities. To act independently in the face of conflict brings swift rebuke and reprisal from the teacher. The children are thus discouraged from independent thought and indoctrinated with the concept that they are incapable of resolving their own problems. While there are many excellent teachers, Hill’s critique seems validated by the state of education today. If you agree with Hill, what do you think we can do about it? One thing we should do is to seek out those teachers and schools who encourage independent thought in their students and applaud them for their courage!

这是希尔1938年写的《公共教育批判》的精髓。你同意他的意见吗？想想幼儿园和一年级的孩子们。他们对任何事情都充满热情和志愿精神，举起双手，并且对学习充满激情。现在快进十年，把这些孩子想象成高中生——那些坐在教室后排，从不与大人有眼神交流，绝对从不主动提问的孩子。他们已经脱离了学习过程。这些孩子怎么了？十年教育。他们认为犯错误会使他们受到嘲笑和蔑视。所以他们为了保护自己而停止参与。他们被教导说，所有问题和冲突的解决办法不在于他们自己的手和头脑，而在于教师的手和头脑，即当局的代表。在冲突面前独立行动会迅速招致老师的谴责和报复。因此，儿童不愿独立思考，并被灌输这样的观念: 他们没有能力解决自己的问题。尽管有许多优秀的教师，但希尔的批评似乎得到了当今教育状况的验证。如果你同意希尔的意见，你认为我们能做些什么？我们应该做的一件事就是找出那些鼓励学生独立思考并为他们的勇气鼓掌的老师和学校！

Q I was under the impression that the purpose of all schooling was to help children to think.

问: 我的印象是，所有学校教育的目的都是帮助孩子们思考。

A That may be the purpose of schooling, but the system in most of the schools of the world does not carry out the purpose. School children are taught not to develop and use their own minds, but to adopt and use the thoughts of others. This sort of schooling destroys the capacity for independent thought, except in a few rare cases where children rely so definitely upon their own will power that they refuse to allow others to do their thinking. Accurate thought is the business of my opposition, not mine!

A 这可能是学校教育的目的，但是世界上大多数学校的教育制度并没有实现这个目的。学校教育孩子不要发展和使用自己的思想，而是采纳和使用他人的思想。这种学校教育摧毁了独立思考的能力，除了在极少数情况下，孩子们如此明确地依赖自己的意志力，以至于他们拒绝让其他人做他们的思考。准确的思想是我反对的事情，不是我的！

Q What relationship, if any, has your opposition with the homes, the churches, and the schools? Your reply to this question should be interesting.

问: 你与家庭、教堂和学校有什么关系，如果有的话？你对这个问题的回答应该很有趣。

A Here is where I make use of some more of my clever tricks. I cause it to appear that everything done by the parents, the schoolteachers, and the religious instructors is being done by my opposition.

A 这里是我利用我更多的聪明技巧的地方。我让它看起来像是父母、学校老师和宗教教师所做的一切都是我的反对。

This diverts attention from me while I manipulate the minds of the young. When religious instructors try to teach children the virtues of my opposition, they generally do so by frightening them with my name. That is all I ask of them. I kindle the flame of fear into proportions which destroy the child’s power to think accurately. In the public schools the teachers further my cause by keeping the children so busy cramming non-essential information into their minds they have no opportunity to think accurately or to analyze correctly the things their instructors teach them.

这转移了我的注意力，而我操纵着年轻人的思想。当宗教导师试图教导孩子们我反对派的优点时，他们通常会用我的名字吓唬他们。这就是我对他们的全部要求。我把恐惧的火焰点燃成比例，摧毁了孩子准确思考的能力。在公立学校里，老师们让孩子们忙着往脑子里灌输非必要的信息，以至于他们没有机会准确地思考或正确地分析教师教给他们的东西，从而进一步推动了我的事业。

Q Do you claim, for your cause, all those who are bound by the habit of drifting?

问: 你是否声称，为了你的事业，所有那些被漂泊习惯束缚的人？

A No. Drifting is only one of my tricks through which I take over the power of independent thought. Before a drifter becomes my permanent property, I must lead him on and ensnare him with another trick. I will tell you about this other trick after I finish describing my methods of converting people into drifters.

A 没有。随波逐流只是我的技巧之一，通过它我接管了独立思考的力量。在一个流浪汉成为我的永久财产之前，我必须用另一个诡计引诱他。在我描述完我把人们变成流浪者的方法之后，我会告诉你另一个技巧。

Q Do you mean you have a method by which you can cause people to drift so far away from self-determination that they can never save themselves?

问: 你的意思是你有一种方法，可以让人们远离自决，从而永远无法自救？

A Yes, a definite method: And it is so effective it never fails.

A 是的，一个明确的方法: 这个方法非常有效，从来不会失败。

Q Do I understand you to claim your method is so powerful your opposition cannot reclaim those whom you have permanently ensnared through drifting?

问: 我是否理解你声称你的方法是如此强大，以至于你的对手无法收回那些你通过漂移而永久陷入其中的人？

A I claim just that! Do you think I would control so many people if my opposition could prevent me? Nothing can stop me from controlling people except people themselves.
