A 我就是这么说的！如果我的反对可以阻止我，你认为我会控制这么多人吗？没有什么能阻止我控制别人，除了他们自己。

Nothing can stop me except the power of accurate thought. People who think accurately do not drift on any subject. They recognize the power of their own minds. Moreover, they take over that power and yield it to no person or influence.

没有什么能够阻止我，除了精确思考的力量。思维准确的人不会在任何问题上游离不定。他们认识到自己思想的力量。此外，他们接管了这种权力，并且没有把它交给任何人或影响力。

Q Go ahead and tell me more of the methods by which you cause people to drift to hell with you!

问: 继续，告诉我更多的方法，你使人们漂移到地狱与你！

A I cause people to drift on every subject through which I can control independent thought and action. Take the subject of health, for example. I cause most people to eat too much food and the wrong sort of food. This leads to indigestion and destroys the power of accurate thought. If the public schools and the churches taught children more about proper eating, they would do my cause irreparable damage.

A 我让人们在每一个我可以控制独立思考和行动的主题上游离。以健康为例。我导致大多数人吃了太多的食物和错误的食物种类。这会导致消化不良并破坏准确思维的能力。如果公立学校和教堂教给孩子们更多关于正确饮食的知识，他们会对我造成无法弥补的伤害。

Marriage: I cause men and women to drift into marriage without plan or purpose designed to convert the relationship into harmony. Here is one of my most effective methods of converting people into the habit of drifting. I cause married people to bicker and nag one another over money matters. I cause them to quarrel over the bringing up of their children. I engage them in unpleasant controversies over their intimate relationships and in disagreements over friends and social activities. I keep them so busy finding fault with one another that they never have time to do anything else long enough to break the habit of drifting.

婚姻: 我使得男人和女人在没有计划或目的的情况下走进婚姻，目的是将关系转化为和谐。这是我最有效的方法之一，可以让人们养成随波逐流的习惯。我导致已婚人士为了钱的问题争吵不休、唠叨不休。我使他们为了抚养孩子而争吵。我让他们陷入亲密关系的不愉快争论，以及朋友和社交活动的分歧中。我让他们忙于互相挑剔，以至于他们没有足够的时间去做其他任何事情来打破这种随波逐流的习惯。

Occupation: I teach people to become drifters by causing them to drift out of school into the first job they can find, with no definite aim or purpose except to make a living. Through this trick I keep millions of people in fear of poverty all their lives. Through this fear I lead them slowly but surely onward until they reach the point beyond which no individual ever has broken the drifting habit.

职业: 我教人们成为漂泊者，让他们离开学校，去找他们能找到的第一份工作，除了谋生之外，没有明确的目标或目的。通过这个把戏，我让数百万人一辈子都生活在对贫穷的恐惧之中。通过这种恐惧，我带领他们缓慢但坚定地前进，直到他们达到没有人能够打破这种漂泊的习惯的临界点。

Savings: I cause people to spend freely and to save sparingly or not at all, until I take complete control of them through their fear of poverty.

储蓄: 我让人们自由地消费，节俭地储蓄或根本不储蓄，直到我通过他们对贫穷的恐惧完全控制了他们。

Environment: I cause people to drift into inharmonious and unpleasant environments in the home, in their places of occupation, in their relationship with relatives and acquaintances, and to remain there until I claim them through the habit of drifting. Dominating Thoughts: I cause people to drift into the habit of thinking negative thoughts. This leads to negative acts and involves people in controversies and fills their minds with fears, thus paving the way for me to enter and control their minds. When I move in, I do so by appealing to people through negative thoughts which they believe to be their own. I plant the seeds of negative thought in the minds of people through the pulpit, the newspapers, the moving pictures, the radio, and all other popular methods of appeal to the mind. I cause people to allow me to do their thinking for them because they are too lazy and too indifferent to think for themselves.

环境: 我让人们在家里、在他们的职业场所、在他们与亲戚和熟人的关系中漂流到不和谐和不愉快的环境中，并且一直呆在那里，直到我通过漂流的习惯认领他们。主导思想: 我使人们陷入消极思想的习惯。这会导致消极的行为，使人们陷入争论，使他们的头脑充满恐惧，从而为我进入并控制他们的头脑铺平道路。当我搬进来的时候，我通过消极的想法吸引人们，他们认为这是他们自己的想法。我通过布道坛、报纸、电影、收音机以及所有其他吸引心灵的流行方式，在人们的头脑中播下了消极思想的种子。我让人们允许我为他们思考，因为他们太懒惰，太冷漠，不愿为自己思考。

Q I conclude from what you say that drifting and procrastination are the same. Is that true?

问: 我从你的话中得出结论，随波逐流和拖延是一样的，这是真的吗？

A Yes, that is correct. Any habit which causes one to procrastinate— to put off reaching a definite decision—leads to the habit of drifting.

A 是的，没错。任何导致拖延的习惯ーー推迟达成一个明确的决定ーー都会导致游离的习惯。

Says the Devil: “I cause people to allow me to do their thinking for them because they are too lazy and too indifferent to think for themselves.”

魔鬼说: “我让人们允许我为他们思考，因为他们太懒惰，太冷漠，不愿为自己思考。”

Laziness + Indifference = Procrastination = Drifting.

懒惰 + 冷漠 = 拖延 = 漂流。

This describes a true drifter as defined by Hill. Since I have been a true procrastinator for most of my life, this hits a little too close to home for me. I like to use the excuse that I work best under pressure—but that is all it is: an excuse for why I procrastinate. Can you think of examples in your own life when laziness and indifference led you off your path to success? When an opportunity slipped through your fingers because you were too slow to seize it in time?

这描述了一个真正的流浪汉希尔定义。由于我一生中的大部分时间都是一个真正的拖延者，这对我来说有点太贴切了。我喜欢用我在压力下工作效率最高的借口ーー但这就是我拖延的全部原因。当懒惰和冷漠使你偏离了通往成功的道路时，你能想到自己生活中的例子吗？当一个机会从你的手指间溜走，因为你太慢而没有及时抓住它？

Q Is man the only creature who drifts?

问: 人是唯一漂泊的生物吗？

A Yes. All other creatures move in response to definite laws of nature. Man alone defies nature’s laws and drifts when he wills.

A 是的。所有其他的生物都是根据明确的自然法则运动的。只有人类才能违背自然法则，随心所欲地漂泊。

Everything outside the minds of men is controlled by my opposition, by laws so definite that drifting is impossible. I control the minds of men solely because of their habit of drifting, which is only another way of saying that I control the minds of men only because they neglect or refuse to control and use their own minds.

人类思想之外的一切都受到我的对立面的控制，这种法律是如此明确，以至于漂泊是不可能的。我控制人们的思想仅仅是因为他们的漂泊习惯，这只是另一种说法，我控制人们的思想仅仅是因为他们忽视或拒绝控制和使用他们自己的思想。

Q This is getting to be pretty deep stuff for a mere human being. Let us get back to the discussion of something less abstract. Please tell me how this drifting habit affects people in the everyday walks of life and tell me in terms the average person can understand.

问: 对于一个普通人来说，这已经变得相当深奥了。让我们回到一些不那么抽象的讨论上来。请告诉我这种随波逐流的习惯如何影响日常生活中的人们，并用普通人能够理解的术语告诉我。

A I would prefer to keep this interview up among the stars!

A 我宁愿让这次采访在众星之间继续进行下去！

Q No doubt you would. That would save you from being exposed. But let us come back to earth. Tell me now what drifting is doing to us as a nation here in the United States.

问: 毫无疑问你会。这样你就不会暴露了。但是让我们回到现实吧。现在告诉我漂泊对我们美国这个国家有什么影响。

A Frankly, I may as well tell you that I hate the United States as only the Devil can hate.

A 坦率地说，我不妨告诉你，我恨美国就像只有魔鬼才能恨美国一样。

Q That is interesting. What is the cause of this hatred?

问: 这很有趣。这种仇恨的原因是什么？

A The cause was born on July 4, 1776, when fifty-six men signed a document which destroyed my chances of controlling the nation. You know that document as the Declaration of Independence. Had it not been for the influence of that damnable document, I would now have a dictator running the country and I would stop this right to free speech and independent thought that is threatening my rule on earth.

A 事业起源于1776年7月4日，当时有56个人签署了一份文件，这份文件破坏了我控制国家的机会。你知道这份文件叫做《美国独立宣言。如果不是那份该死的文件的影响，我现在就会有一个统治这个国家的独裁者，我会阻止这种威胁到我在地球上统治的言论自由和独立思想的权利。

Q Am I to understand from what you say that nations controlled by self-appointed dictators belong in your camp?

问: 我是否可以从你所说的话中理解，那些被自封的独裁者控制的国家属于你们的阵营？

A There are no self-appointed dictators. I appoint them all. Moreover, I manipulate them and direct them in their work. Nations run by my dictators know what they want and take it by force. Look what I have done through Mussolini in Italy! Look what I am doing through Hitler in Germany. Look what I am doing through Stalin in Russia. My dictators run those nations for me because the people have been subdued through the habit of drifting. My dictators do no drifting. That is why they rule for me the millions of people under their control.

A 没有自封的独裁者。我任命他们所有人。此外，我操纵他们，指导他们的工作。由我的独裁者统治的国家知道他们想要什么，并用武力夺取。看看我通过墨索里尼在意大利做了什么！看看我通过希特勒在德国做了什么。看看我通过斯大林在俄罗斯做了什么。我的独裁者为我管理这些国家，因为人民已经因为漂泊不定的习惯而屈服了。我的独裁者从不随波逐流。这就是为什么他们为我统治数百万在他们控制之下的人民。

Q What would happen if Mussolini, Stalin, and Hitler turned traitors and disavowed you and your rule?

问: 如果墨索里尼、斯大林和希特勒叛变，否认你和你的统治，会发生什么？

A That will not happen because I have them too well bribed. I am paying each of them with the sop of his own vanity, by making him believe he is acting on his own account. That is another trick of mine.

A 那不会发生，因为我收买了他们。我这样做是为了满足他们每个人的虚荣心，让他们相信他们是在为自己的利益而行动。这是我的另一个小把戏。

Q Let us come back to the United States and learn something of what you are doing to convert people into the habit of drifting.

问: 让我们回到美国，了解一下你们是如何让人们养成漂泊的习惯的。

A Right now I am paving the way for a dictatorship by sowing the seeds of fear and uncertainty in the minds of the people.

A 现在我正在为独裁铺平道路，在人民心中播下恐惧和不确定的种子。

Q Through whom are you carrying on your work?

问: 你通过谁继续你的工作？

A Mainly through the President. I am destroying his influence with the people by causing him to drift on the question of a working agreement between employers and their employees. If I can induce him to drift for another year, he will be so thoroughly discredited I can hand over the country to a dictator. If the President continues to drift, I will paralyze personal freedom in the United States just as I destroyed it in Spain, Italy, Germany, and England.

A 主要通过总统。我使他在雇主和雇员之间的工作协议问题上游离不定，这是在破坏他对人民的影响力。如果我能说服他再漂泊一年，他将名誉扫地，我可以把国家交给一个独裁者。如果总统继续漂泊不定，我将瘫痪美国的个人自由，就像我在西班牙、意大利、德国和英国摧毁个人自由一样。

In 1938 when Hill was writing this manuscript, the president was Franklin D. Roosevelt. Are the Devil’s comments applicable today? Do you think Hill might write the same words today as he wrote seventy years ago?

1938年，当希尔写这份手稿的时候，总统是富兰克林·德拉诺·罗斯福。魔鬼的评论适用于今天吗？你认为希尔今天会写出和七十年前一样的文字吗？

Q What you say leads me to the conclusion that drifting is a weakness which inevitably ends in failure, whether among individuals or nations. Is that your claim?

问: 你所说的让我得出这样的结论: 无论是在个人之间还是在国家之间，漂泊是一种弱点，它不可避免地以失败告终。这是你的要求吗？

A Drifting is the most common cause of failure in every walk of life. I can control anyone whom I can induce to form the habit of drifting on any subject. The reason for this is twofold. First, the drifter is just so much putty in my hands, to be molded into whatever pattern I choose, because drifting destroys the power of individual initiative. Second, the drifter cannot get help from my opposition, because the opposition is not attracted to anything so soft and useless.

在各行各业中，漂泊是导致失败的最常见原因。我可以控制任何人，只要我能引导他们养成在任何话题上游移不定的习惯。原因是双重的。首先，漂流者在我手中就像是一块油灰，可以被塑造成我选择的任何模式，因为漂流摧毁了个人主动性的力量。其次，流浪汉不能从我的对手那里得到帮助，因为对手不会被任何如此软弱和无用的东西吸引。

Q Is that why a few people are wealthy while the majority of people are poor?

问: 这就是为什么少数人富有而大多数人贫穷的原因吗？

A That is exactly the reason. Poverty, like physical illness, is a contagious disease. You find it always among the drifters, never among those who know what they want and are determined to get just that! It may mean something to you when I call your attention to the fact that the non-drifters, whom I do not control, and those who possess most of the wealth of the world, happen to be the same people.

A 这正是原因所在。贫穷，就像生理疾病一样，是一种接触传染病。你发现它总是在流浪者中间，而不是在那些知道自己想要什么并决心得到它的人中间！当我提请你们注意这样一个事实时，它可能对你们意味着什么: 那些我无法控制的不流浪者，和那些拥有世界上大部分财富的人，恰好是同一批人。

Q I have always understood that money was the root of all evil, that the poor and the meek would inherit heaven, while the wealthy would pass into your hands. What have you to say of that claim?

我一直明白，金钱是一切罪恶的根源，穷人和温顺的人会继承天堂，而富人会转到你的手中。你对这种说法有什么看法？

A Men who know how to get the material things of life generally know how to keep out of the hands of the Devil as well. The ability to acquire things is contagious. Drifters acquire nothing except that which no one else wants. If more people had definite aims and stronger desires for material and spiritual riches, I would have fewer victims.

一个知道如何获得物质生活的人通常也知道如何远离魔鬼的手。获得东西的能力是会传染的。流浪者除了别人不想要的东西，什么也得不到。如果更多的人对物质和精神财富有明确的目标和更强烈的欲望，我会有更少的受害者。

The actual verse of the Bible talks about the “love of money,” not money itself:
“For the love of money is the root of all kinds of evil.”
1 Timothy 6:10

圣经的实际经文谈到“爱钱财” ，而不是钱财本身: “因为爱钱财是万恶之源。”提摩太前书6:10

Q I assume, from what you say, that you do not claim fellowship with the industrial leaders. Evidently they are not friends of yours.

问: 从你说的话来看，我认为你并没有要求与工业领袖们建立友谊。显然他们不是你的朋友。

A Friends of mine? I’ll tell you what sort of friends of mine they are. They have belted the entire country with good roads, thus bringing into close communion the people of both city and country. They have converted ores into steel, with which they have built the skeletons of great skyscrapers. They have harnessed electrical power and converted it into a thousand uses, all designed to give man time to think. They have provided through the automobile personal transportation to the humblest citizen, thus giving to everyone the freedom of travel. They have provided every home with instantaneous news of what is happening in all parts of the world through the aid of the radio.

我的朋友？我来告诉你他们是什么样的朋友。他们在全国铺设了良好的道路，使城市和乡村的人民紧密相连。他们把矿石变成钢铁，用钢铁建造了摩天大楼的骨架。他们利用电力并将其转化为一千种用途，所有这些设计都是为了给人们时间去思考。他们通过汽车为最卑微的公民提供私人交通工具，从而给予每个人旅行的自由。通过无线电的帮助，他们向每个家庭提供了世界各地正在发生的事情的即时新闻。

. . . and now television, smart phone, satellite, and Internet!

现在是电视、智能手机、卫星和互联网！

They have reared libraries in every city, town, and hamlet and have filled them with books giving to all who read a complete outline of the most useful knowledge mankind has gathered from his experiences. They have given the humblest citizen the right to express his own opinion on any subject, anytime, anywhere, without fear of molestation, and they have seen to it that every citizen may help make his own laws, levy his own taxes, and manage his own country through the ballot. These are but some of the things the industrial leaders have done to give every citizen the privilege of becoming a non-drifter. Do you think these men have helped my cause?

他们在每个城市、城镇和村庄都建立了图书馆，并且在里面放满了书籍，给所有读过这些书的人提供了人类从自己的经历中获得的最有用的知识的完整大纲。他们赋予最卑微的公民在任何时间、任何地点对任何问题表达自己意见的权利，而不必担心受到干扰，他们还确保每个公民都可以帮助制定自己的法律，征收自己的税款，并通过投票管理自己的国家。这些仅仅是工业领袖们为了给予每个公民成为非流浪者的特权所做的一些事情。你认为这些人对我的事业有帮助吗？

Q Who are some of the present-day non-drifters over whom you have no control?

问: 现在有哪些人是你无法控制的“不流浪者” ？

A I have control over no non-drifter, present or past. I control the weak, not those who think for themselves.

我控制不了任何非漂泊者，不管是现在的还是过去的。我控制的是弱者，而不是那些为自己着想的人。

Q Go ahead and describe a typical drifter. Give your description point by point so I can recognize a drifter when I see him.

请描述一个典型的流浪汉。给出你的描述点，这样我可以认出一个流浪汉，当我看到他。

A The first thing you will notice about a drifter is his total lack of a major purpose in life.

你注意到的第一件事就是一个流浪汉完全没有人生的主要目标。

He will be conspicuous by his lack of self-confidence.

他会因缺乏自信而引人注目。

He will never accomplish anything requiring thought and effort.

他永远不会完成任何需要思考和努力的事情。

He spends all he earns and more too, if he can get credit.

如果他能得到信贷，他会花光他所有的收入，还会花得更多。

He will be sick or ailing from some real or imaginary cause, and calling to high heaven if he suffers the least physical pain.

他会因为某些真实或虚构的原因而生病或生病，如果他遭受的肉体痛苦最少，他就会呼唤上天堂。

He will have little or no imagination.

他几乎没有想象力。

He will lack enthusiasm and initiative to begin anything he is not forced to undertake, and he will plainly express his weakness by taking the line of least resistance whenever he can do so.

他会缺乏热情和主动性去开始做任何他没有被迫去做的事情，而且只要他能做到，他就会毫不犹豫地选择阻力最小的路线来表达自己的弱点。

He will be ill-tempered and lacking in control over his emotions.

他脾气暴躁，无法控制自己的情绪。

His personality will be without magnetism and it will not attract other people.

他的个性没有吸引力，也不会吸引其他人。

He will have opinions on everything but accurate knowledge of nothing.

他对什么事情都有意见，但对什么事情都没有准确的了解。

He may be jack of all trades but good at none.

他可能是个多面手，但是什么都不擅长。

He will neglect to cooperate with those around him, even those on whom he must depend for food and shelter.

他会忽略与周围的人合作，即使是那些他必须依靠的食物和住所。

He will make the same mistake over and over again, never profiting by failure.

他会一次又一次地犯同样的错误，从不从失败中获利。

He will be narrow-minded and intolerant on all subjects, ready to crucify those who may disagree with him.

他对任何事物都心胸狭窄、不宽容，准备把那些不同意他的人钉在十字架上。

He will expect everything of others but be willing to give little or nothing in return.

他对别人的一切都抱有期望，但却愿意付出很少甚至没有回报。

He may begin many things but he will complete nothing.

他可以开始做很多事情，但他不会完成任何事情。

He will be loud in his condemnation of his government, but he will never tell you definitely how it can be improved.

他会大声谴责他的政府，但他永远不会明确告诉你政府如何改进。

He will never reach decisions on anything if he can avoid it, and if he is forced to decide he will reverse himself at the first opportunity.

如果他能够避免，他将永远不会在任何事情上做出决定，如果他被迫做出决定，他将在第一时间改变自己的决定。

He will eat too much and exercise too little.

他会吃得太多，运动得太少。

He will take a drink of liquor if someone else will pay for it.

如果别人付钱，他就会喝酒。

He will gamble if he can do it “on the cuff.”

如果他能“即兴”赌一把，他就会赌一把

He will criticize others who are succeeding in their chosen calling.

他会批评那些在他们所选择的职业上取得成功的人。

In brief, the drifter will work harder to get out of thinking than most others work in earning a good living.

简而言之，流浪汉会比其他人更努力地工作，以摆脱思考，从而获得更好的生活。

He will tell a lie rather than admit his ignorance on any subject.

他宁愿说谎也不愿承认自己在任何问题上的无知。

If he works for others, he will criticize them to their backs and flatter them to their faces.

如果他为别人工作，他会当着别人的面批评他们，奉承他们。

Q You have given me a graphic description of the drifter. Please now describe the non-drifter so that I may recognize him on sight.

问: 你给了我一个关于流浪汉的生动描述。现在请你描述一下那个不是流浪汉的人，以便我一见到他就能认出来。

A The first sign of a non-drifter is this: He is always engaged in doing something definite, through some well-organized plan which is definite. He has a major goal in life toward which he is always working, and many minor goals, all of which lead toward his central scheme.

A 非流浪汉的第一个特征是: 他总是通过一些组织良好的明确计划，从事一些明确的事情。他有一个人生的主要目标，他总是朝着这个目标努力，还有许多次要的目标，所有这些都指向他的中心计划。

The tone of his voice, the quickness of his step, the sparkle in his eyes, the quickness of his decisions clearly mark him as a person who knows exactly what he wants and is determined to get it, no matter how long it may take or what price he must pay.

他的语气，他的步伐敏捷，他的眼神，他的决定敏捷，清楚地标志着他是一个人谁知道他到底想要什么，并决心得到它，不管多久可能需要或他必须付出什么代价。

If you ask him questions, he gives you direct answers and never falls back on evasions or resorts to subterfuge.

如果你问他问题，他会直截了当地回答你，从不回避或借口托词。

He extends many favors to others, but accepts favors sparingly or not at all.

他给予别人很多恩惠，但是要么有节制地接受恩惠，要么根本不接受。

He will be found up front whether he is playing a game or fighting a war.

不管他是在玩游戏还是在打仗，他都会被发现。

If he does not know the answers he will say so frankly.

如果他不知道答案，他就会坦率地说出来。

He has a good memory; never offers an alibi for his shortcomings.

他记性好，从不为自己的缺点找借口。

He never blames others for his mistakes no matter if they deserve the blame.

他从不为自己的错误责备别人，不管他们是否应该受到责备。

He used to be known as a go-getter, but in modern times he is called a go-giver. You will find him running the biggest business in town, living on the best street, driving the best automobile, and making his presence felt wherever he happens to be.

他过去被认为是一个积极进取的人，但在现代他被称为一个进取的人。你会发现他经营着城里最大的生意，住在最好的街道上，开着最好的汽车，无论他在哪里，都能感受到他的存在。

He is an inspiration to all who come into contact with his mind.

他是所有与他心灵接触的人的灵感来源。

The major distinguishing feature of the non-drifter is this: He has a mind of his own and uses it for all purposes.

非流浪汉的主要特点是: 他有自己的思想，并将其用于各种目的。

The non-drifter “has a mind of his own and uses it for all purposes.”

非流浪汉“有自己的想法，并将其用于各种目的。”

Can you think of someone you know who fits this description? Is that person a non-drifter?

你能想到一个你认识的人符合这种描述吗? 那个人不是流浪汉吗？

Q Is the non-drifter born with some mental, physical, or spiritual advantage not available to the drifter?

非流浪者是否天生具有某些精神、身体或精神上的优势，而流浪者却没有？

A No. The major difference between the drifter and the non-drifter is something equally available to both. It is simply the prerogative right of each to use his own mind and think for himself.

A 没有。流浪者和非流浪者之间的主要区别在于，他们都可以使用某些东西。每个人都有使用自己的思想并为自己思考的特权。

Q What brief message would you send to the typical drifter if you wished to cure him of this evil habit?

问: 如果你想治愈这种恶习，你会给典型的流浪汉发什么样的简短信息呢？

A I would admonish him to wake up and give!

A 我会告诫他醒来并给予！

Q Give what?

给什么？

A Some form of service useful to as many people as possible.

一些对尽可能多的人有用的服务形式。

Q So the non-drifter is supposed to give, is he?

那么非漂流者应该给予，是吗？

A Yes, if he expects to get! And he must give before he gets!

A 是的，如果他想得到的话! 而且他必须在得到之前付出！

Q Some people doubt that you exist.

有些人怀疑你的存在。

A I wouldn’t worry about that if I were you. Those who are ready to be converted from the habit of drifting will recognize the authenticity of this interview by its soundness of counsel. The others are not worth the trouble it would take to convert them.

A 如果我是你，我不会担心这个。那些准备改变这种漂泊不定的习惯的人，会从这次访谈的忠告的正确性中认识到它的真实性。其他人不值得我们费这么大劲去改变他们的信仰。

Q Why do you not try to stop me from publishing this confession I am wringing from you?

问: 为什么你不试着阻止我发表我从你那里得到的这份自白？

A Because that would be the surest of all ways to guarantee you will publish it. I have a better plan than trying to suppress publication of my confession. I will urge you to go ahead with the publication, then sit back and watch you suffer when some of my faithful drifters begin to make things hot for you. I will not need to deny your story. My followers will do that for me—see if they don’t.

A 因为这是保证你会发表它的最可靠的方法。我有一个更好的计划，而不是试图阻止我的忏悔被发表。我会敦促你继续出版，然后坐下来看着你受苦，当我的一些忠实的漂泊者开始让事情对你热。我不需要否认你的故事。我的追随者会为我这样做ーー看看他们是否会这样做。

Knowing that indeed this book was not published for more than seventy years after Hill wrote these words, I am intrigued and anxious to learn what else he will reveal! There are plenty of fireworks still ahead . . .

知道这本书确实在希尔写下这些话之后的七十多年才出版，我很好奇，急切地想知道他还会揭示些什么！前方还有很多焰火。





Chapter Five

THE CONFESSION CONTINUES

第五章忏悔继续

Q IF THIS CONFESSION OF YOURS STOPPED right here your statement would be sound, but fortunately for millions of your victims who will gain their release because of your confession, this interview will continue until you have supplied me with the weapon by which you will eventually be restrained from domination of people through their fears and superstitions. Remember, Your Majesty, your confession has just begun. After I wring from you a description of the methods by which you control people, I will force you also to give the formula by which your control can be broken at will.

问: 如果你的供词在这里停止，你的陈述将是合理的，但幸运的是，对于数百万因为你的供词而获得释放的受害者来说，这次采访将继续下去，直到你为我提供了武器，你最终将不会因为人们的恐惧和迷信而被控制。记住，陛下，你的忏悔才刚刚开始。在我向你描述了你控制人们的方法之后，我会强迫你也给出一个公式，通过这个公式你可以随意地打破你的控制。

It is true I shall not remain here long enough to defeat you, but the published word I leave behind me will be deathless because it will consist of truth! You fear the opposition of no individual because you know it will be short, but you do fear truth. You fear truth and nothing else, for the reason it is slowly but definitely giving human beings freedom from all manner of fear. Without the weapon of fear you would be helpless and entirely unable to control any human being! Is that true or false?

的确，我不会在这里停留足够长的时间来打败你们，但是我留在身后的公开的话语将是不死的，因为它将包含真理！你害怕没有个人的反对，因为你知道反对是短暂的，但你确实害怕真理。你只害怕真理，因为它缓慢而明确地给予人类免于各种恐惧的自由。没有恐惧的武器，你将是无助的，完全无法控制任何人！这是真的还是假的？

“It is true I shall not remain here long enough to defeat you, but the published word I leave behind me will be deathless because it will consist of truth!”

“的确，我在这里的时间不会长到足以打败你们，但我留在身后的公开言论将是不朽的，因为它将包含真理! ”

Indeed, Napoleon Hill passed away in 1970, and this work being published in 2011 becomes deathless.

事实上，拿破仑 · 希尔于1970年去世，这部著作于2011年出版，成为不朽之作。

A I have no alternative but to admit that what you say is true.

A 我别无选择，只能承认你说的是真的。

Q Now that we understand each other, let us go ahead with your confession. But before we continue, I may as well take time out to do a little boasting on my own account, now that you have had your fling at it. I will confine myself to one question, the answer to which will give me all the satisfaction I want. Is it not true that you control only the minds of those who have allowed the drifting habit to be fixed upon them?

既然我们已经了解了彼此，让我们继续你的忏悔吧。但是在我们继续之前，既然你已经试过了，我不妨花点时间为我自己吹嘘一下。我只想问一个问题，这个问题的答案将使我得到我想要的一切满足。你只能控制那些允许漂泊习惯固定在他们头脑上的人，这难道不是真的吗？

A Yes, that is true. I have already admitted this truth in a dozen or more different ways. Why do you tantalize me by repeating the question?

A 是的，这是真的。我已经用十几种或更多不同的方式承认了这个事实。你为什么重复这个问题来逗弄我？

Q There is power in repetition. I am forcing you to repeat the highlights of your confession in as many different ways as possible so your victims may check this interview and determine its soundness by their own experiences with you. That is one of my little tricks. Do you approve of my method?

重复有力量。我强迫你以尽可能多的方式重复你供词的要点，这样你的受害者就可以检查这次采访，并根据他们自己与你的经历来判断这次采访是否合理。这是我的一个小把戏。你赞成我的方法吗？

A You couldn’t be setting a trap for me for the purpose of doing some more boasting, could you?

A 你不会是为了更多的吹嘘而给我设下圈套吧？

Q I am asking the questions and you are doing the answering! Go ahead now and confess why you are powerless to stop me from forcing this confession from you. I want your confession for aid and comfort to victims of yours whom I intend to release from your control the moment they read your confession.

问: 我在问问题，你在回答！现在就承认吧，为什么你无力阻止我强迫你认罪。我需要你的供词来帮助和安慰你的受害者，我打算在他们读到你的供词时，从你的控制中释放他们。

A I am powerless to influence or control you because you have found the secret approach to my kingdom. You know that I exist only in the minds of people who have fears. You know that I control only the drifters who neglect to use their own minds. You know that my hell is here on earth and not in the world that comes after death. And you know also that drifters supply all the fire I use in my hell. You know that I am a principle or form of energy which expresses the negative side of matter and energy, and that I am not a person with a forked tongue and a spiked tail. You have become my master because you have mastered all your fears. Lastly, you know that you can release all of my earthbound victims whom you contact, and this definite knowledge is the blow with which you will deal me the greatest damage.

我无力影响或控制你们，因为你们已经找到了通往我王国的秘密途径。你知道我只存在于那些有恐惧的人的头脑中。你知道我只控制那些不用脑子的流浪汉。你知道我的地狱在人间，而不在死后的世界。你也知道我在地狱里用的火都是流浪者提供的。你知道，我是一种原则或能量的形式，它表达了物质和能量的消极面，我不是一个有着分叉的舌头和尖尖的尾巴的人。你已经成为我的主人，因为你已经掌握了你所有的恐惧。最后，你们知道你们可以释放所有你们接触过的地球上的受害者，而这确切的知识就是你们对我造成最大伤害的打击。

I cannot control you because you have discovered your own mind and you have taken charge of it. There now, Mr. Earthbound, that confession should feed your vanity to the bursting point.

我不能控制你，因为你已经发现了你自己的思想，你已经掌控了它。好了，地缚先生，这样的坦白会使你的虚荣心爆发出来。

Says the Devil: “I cannot control you because you have discovered your own mind and you have taken charge of it. This definite knowledge is the blow with which you will deal me the greatest damage.”

魔鬼说: “我不能控制你，因为你已经发现了你自己的思想，你已经掌控了它。这个明确的知识是你对我造成最大伤害的一击。”

Q That last dart was unnecessary. Knowledge of the sort I have used to master you does not contaminate itself with vulgar indulgence in vanity. Truth is the one, and only, thing in the world that can stand ridicule. Now let us continue with your confession. What is wrong with the principle of flattery? You use it, do you not?

最后那支飞镖是不必要的。我曾经掌握过你的那些知识，它们不会因为贪图虚荣而玷污了自己。真理是这个世界上唯一可以忍受嘲笑的东西。现在让我们继续你的忏悔。阿谀奉承的原则有什么错？你用它，不是吗？

A Do I use it? Man alive! Flattery is one of my most useful weapons. With this deadly instrument I slay the big ones and the little ones.

A 我使用它吗？好家伙！奉承是我最有用的武器之一。用这个致命的工具，我杀死了大的和小的。

Q Your admission interests me. Go ahead now and tell me how you make use of flattery.

我对你的承认很感兴趣。来吧，告诉我你是如何使用奉承的。

A I make use of it in so many ways it is difficult to know where to begin. I warn you, before I answer in detail, that publishing my answers will bring down an avalanche of ridicule on your head for bringing up the question.

A 我在很多方面利用它，很难知道从哪里开始。在我详细回答之前，我要警告你，公布我的答案会使你因为提出这个问题而受到铺天盖地的嘲笑。

Q I’ll take the responsibility. Proceed.

我会负起责任，继续。

A Well, I may as well here admit that you have stumbled onto the major secret of how I convert people to the habit of drifting!

答: 好吧，我也可以在这里承认你已经无意中发现了我如何让人们养成漂泊的习惯的主要秘密！

Q That is a startling admission. Go ahead with your confession, and stick strictly to this subject of flattery. No more side remarks and no more facetiousness for the present. Tell me all about your use of flattery in gaining control over people.

问: 这是一个令人吃惊的承认。继续你的忏悔吧，严格遵守这个奉承的话题。目前不再有旁门左道，也不再滑稽可笑。告诉我你是如何运用奉承来控制别人的。

A Flattery is a bait of incomparable value to all who wish to gain control over others. It has powerful pulling qualities because it operates through two of the most common human weaknesses: vanity and egotism. There is a certain amount of vanity and egotism in everyone. In some people these qualities are so pronounced they literally serve as a rope by which one may be bound. The best of all ropes is flattery.

对于所有希望控制他人的人来说，奉承是一种具有无可比拟价值的诱饵。它具有强大的吸引力，因为它通过两个最常见的人类弱点来运作: 虚荣心和自我中心。每个人都有一定程度的虚荣心和自我中心。对有些人来说，这些品质是如此显著，以至于他们实际上就像一根绳子，一个人可以被绳子束缚。奉承是最好的解决办法。

Flattery is the chief bait through which men seduce women. Sometimes—in fact, frequently—women use the same bait to gain control of men, especially men who cannot be mastered through sex appeal. I teach its use to both men and women. Flattery is the chief bait with which my agents weave their way into the confidence of people from whom they procure information needed to carry on warfare.

奉承是男人勾引女人的主要诱饵。事实上，有时候女人也会使用同样的诱饵来控制男人，尤其是那些不能通过性吸引力来控制的男人。我教男人和女人使用它。奉承话是我的特工们用来骗取人们信任的主要诱饵，他们从这些人那里获得进行战争所需的情报。

Wherever anyone stops to feed his vanity on flattery, I move in and begin to build another drifter. Non-drifters are not easily flattered. I inspire people to use flattery in every human relationship where its use is possible because those who are influenced by it become easy victims of the drifting habit.

凡有人停下来用奉承来满足他的虚荣心的地方，我就进去，开始造另一个流浪汉。非漂泊者不容易被奉承。我鼓励人们在每一段人际关系中使用阿谀奉承，因为那些受其影响的人很容易成为这种流动习惯的受害者。

Says the Devil: “Flattery is the chief bait through which men seduce women.”

魔鬼说: “奉承是男人勾引女人的主要诱饵。”

Q Can you control anyone who is amenable to flattery?

问: 你能控制任何一个容易被奉承的人吗？

A Very easily. As I have already told you, flattery is of major importance in alluring people into the habit of drifting.

A 非常容易。正如我已经告诉过你的那样，奉承话在诱使人们养成随波逐流的习惯方面非常重要。

Q At what age are people most susceptible to flattery?

什么年龄的人最容易受到奉承的影响？

A Age has nothing to do with one’s susceptibility to flattery. People respond to it, in one way or another, from the time they become conscious of their own existence until they die.

一个时代与一个人是否容易受到奉承无关。人们会以这样或那样的方式回应它，从他们意识到自己的存在直到他们死去。

Q Through what motive can women be most easily flattered?

问: 女人最容易被奉承的动机是什么？

A Their vanity. Tell a woman she is pretty or that she wears clothes well.

A 他们的虚荣心。告诉一个女人她很漂亮或者她穿衣服很好看。

Q What motive is most effective in harpooning men?

用鱼叉射击男人最有效的动机是什么？

A Egotism, with a capital E! Tell a man he has a strong Herculean body or that he is a great business tycoon, and he will purr like a cat and smile like an opossum! After that you know what happens.

一个自我中心，大写的 e! 告诉一个人他有一个强壮的赫拉克勒斯式的身体或者他是一个伟大的商业大亨，他会像猫一样咕噜咕噜地叫，像负鼠一样微笑！之后你就知道会发生什么了。

Q Are all men like that?

所有的男人都是这样的吗？

A Oh, no. Two out of every hundred have their egotism so thoroughly under control that even an expert flatterer couldn’t get under their skins with a double-edged butcher knife.

A 哦，不。每一百个人中就有两个人完全掌控了自己的自我中心，即使是一个专业的奉承者也无法用双刃屠刀刺穿他们的皮肤。

Q How does a cunning woman apply her art of flattery in attracting men?

一个狡猾的女人如何运用她的奉承艺术来吸引男人？

A Great heavens, man, do I have to draw a picture of her method for you? Have you no imagination?

天哪，伙计，难道要我为你描绘她的方法吗? 你没有想象力吗？

Q Oh, yes, I have imagination enough, Your Majesty, but I am thinking of the poor dupes of the world who need to understand the exact technique with which they may be flattered into the habit of drifting. Go on and tell us how a woman can harpoon rich and presumably smart men.

哦，是的，我有足够的想象力，陛下，但是我想到了世界上那些可怜的笨蛋们，他们需要了解一些精确的技巧，这些技巧可以使他们养成漂泊的习惯。继续，告诉我们一个女人如何可以捕获富有的，可能是聪明的男人。

A This is a devilish trick to play on women, but since you demand the information I am helpless to withhold it. Women influence men through a technique consisting, first, of ability to inject soft, cooing baby tones into their voices, and, second, by closing their eyes into a half-closed position which registers hypnotism in connection with the flattery of men.

这是对女人开的一个邪恶的玩笑，但是既然你要求我提供信息，我也无能为力。女人通过一种技巧来影响男人，首先，她们有能力在声音中注入柔和的婴儿音调，其次，她们把眼睛闭成半闭的姿势，这种姿势与男人的奉承有关。

I am sure there are a few women agitated by this; in fact, I was at first. Roll your eyes, and keep going . . . there is truth here!

我敢肯定有一些女人对此感到不安，事实上，我一开始就是这样。转动你的眼睛，继续前进... ... 这里有真理！

Q Is that all there is to the business of flattery?

问: 阿谀奉承就是这么回事吗？

A No, that is only the technique. Then comes the motive a woman uses as a lure. The type of woman you perhaps have in mind never sells a man herself or anything she can give him. Instead she sells him his own egotism!

A 不，那只是技巧而已。然后是女人用来做诱饵的动机。你心目中的那种女人从来不会卖给男人她自己或者她能给他的任何东西。相反，她向他兜售他自己的自负！

Q Is that all that women use when they wish to flatter men?

问: 这就是女人为了讨好男人所用的方法吗？

A That is the most effective thing they use. It works when sex appeal fails!

A 那是他们使用的最有效的东西。当性吸引力失败的时候，它就起作用了！

Q So I am to believe that big, strong, smart men can be wound up and manipulated through flattery, just as if they were so much putty? Is that possible?

问: 所以我要相信，高大、强壮、聪明的男人可以通过奉承受伤和被操纵，就像他们是如此任性一样？这可能吗？

A Is it possible? It is happening every minute of the day. Moreover, unless they are non-drifters, the bigger they come, the harder they fall when the expert flatterer moves in on them.

A 这可能吗？它每时每刻都在发生。此外，除非他们不是流浪者，否则他们越高大，当拍马屁的专家靠近他们时，他们摔得越重。

Q Tell me of some of your other tricks with which you cause people to drift in life.

问: 告诉我你其他一些让人们在生活中随波逐流的小把戏。

A One of my most effective devices is failure! The majority of people begin to drift as soon as they meet with opposition, and not one out of ten thousand will keep on trying after failing two or three times.

我最有效的方法之一就是失败！大多数人一遇到阻力就开始游离不定，万分之一的人在失败两三次之后也不会继续尝试。

Q So it is your business to induce people to fail whenever you can. Is that correct?

问: 所以你的工作就是尽可能地诱导人们失败，对吗？

A You have it right. Failure breaks down one’s morale, destroys self-confidence, subdues enthusiasm, dulls imagination, and drives away definiteness of purpose.

A 你说得对。失败打击人的士气，摧毁自信，抑制热情，使想象力变得迟钝，并且使人失去明确的目标。

Without these qualities no one can permanently succeed in any undertaking. The world has produced thousands of inventors with ability superior to that of the late Thomas A. Edison. But these men have never been heard of, while the name of Edison will go marching on because Edison converted failure into a stepping stone to achievement while the others used it as an alibi for not producing results.

没有这些品质，任何人都不可能在任何事业上取得永久的成功。世界上已经产生了成千上万的发明家，他们的能力超过了爱迪生。但是，这些人从来没有听说过，而爱迪生的名字将继续前进，因为爱迪生把失败变成了成就的垫脚石，而其他人用它作为不产生结果的托辞。

Q Is the capacity to surmount failure without being discouraged one of Henry Ford’s chief assets?

问: 克服失败的能力是不是亨利 · 福特的主要资产之一？

A Yes, and this same quality is the chief asset of every man who attains outstanding success in any calling.

A 是的，同样的品质是每一个在任何行业中取得杰出成就的人的主要资产。

The “capacity to surmount failure without being discouraged”
is “the chief asset of every man who attains outstanding success in any calling.”

“毫不气馁地克服失败的能力”是“在任何职业中获得杰出成功的人的首要资产”

In the book Three Feet from Gold my co-author and I interviewed more than thirty-five of today’s top leaders, not about their successes but about their toughest moments and how they persevered to achieve great success. For example, Julie Krone, the first woman ever inducted into the Thoroughbred Hall of Fame, with 3,704 victories under her reins, described her struggles at the beginning of her career as a jockey. Many of the horse owners simply would not hire a woman jockey. She said her motto of perseverance was, “Keep showing up!” She said, “I discovered if I showed up every day and did my best, eventually they’d put me on a horse just to get rid of me.” The rest is history. Julie was named as one of the toughest athletes of all time by USA Today.

在《距离金子三英尺》一书中，我和我的合著者采访了超过35位当今的最高领导人，不是关于他们的成功，而是关于他们最艰难的时刻，以及他们如何坚持不懈地取得巨大成功。例如，第一位入选纯种马名人堂的女性朱莉 · 克朗(Julie Krone)以3704次胜利入选，她描述了自己职业生涯开始时的挣扎，当时她是一名骑师。许多马主根本不会雇佣一个女骑师。她说她坚持不懈的座右铭是“坚持出现! ”她说，“我发现，如果我每天都出现，并尽我最大的努力，最终他们会把我放在马上，只是为了摆脱我。”剩下的就是历史了。朱莉被《今日美国》评为有史以来最强悍的运动员之一。

Q That statement covers lots of territory, Your Majesty. Do you not wish to modify it or tone it down a bit for the sake of accuracy?

问: 这句话涵盖了很多领土，陛下。为了准确起见，你不希望修改它或者降低它的音调吗？

A No modification is necessary because the claim is none too broad. Search accurately into the lives of men and women who achieve enduring success and you will find, without exception, that their success has been in exact proportion to the extent that they surmounted failure.

没有修改是必要的，因为要求不是太宽泛。准确地研究那些取得持久成功的男人和女人的生活，你会毫无例外地发现，他们的成功与他们战胜失败的程度成正比。

The life of every successful person loudly acclaims that which every true philosopher knows: “Every failure brings with it the seed of an equivalent success.”

每个成功人士的一生都在大声赞扬每个真正的哲学家都知道的一句话: “每次失败都会带来同等成功的种子。”

But the seed will not germinate and grow under the influence of a drifter. It springs to life only when it is in the hands of one who recognizes that most failures are only temporary defeat, and who never, under any circumstances, accepts defeat as an excuse for drifting.

但是种子在流浪汉的影响下不会发芽和生长。只有当它掌握在一个认识到大多数失败只是暂时的失败，并且在任何情况下都不接受失败作为随波逐流的借口的人手中时，它才会活过来。

Q If I understand you correctly, you claim there is virtue in failure. That does not seem reasonable. Why do you try to induce people to fail if there is virtue in failure?

问: 如果我理解正确的话，你声称失败中有美德。这似乎不太合理。如果失败中有美德，你为什么要诱导人们失败呢？

A There is no inconsistency in my claims. The appearance of inconsistency is due to your lack of understanding. Failure is a virtue only when it does not lead one to quit trying and begin drifting. I induce as many people as I can to fail as often as possible for the reason that not one out of ten thousand will keep on trying after failing two or three times. I am not concerned about the few who convert failures into stepping stones because they belong to my opposition anyway. They are the non-drifters and therefore they are beyond my reach.

A 我的主张没有前后矛盾之处。前后不一致的现象是由于你缺乏理解。只有当失败不会导致一个人放弃尝试并开始漂流时，它才是一种美德。我诱导尽可能多的人失败，因为万分之一的人在失败两三次之后不会继续尝试。我并不关心那些把失败变成垫脚石的少数人，因为他们属于我的反对派。他们是非流浪者，因此他们超出了我的范围。

Q Your explanation clears up the matter. Now go ahead and tell me of some of your other tricks with which you allure people into drifting.

问: 你的解释澄清了问题。现在继续，告诉我一些你的其他技巧，与你诱惑人们漂移。

“Edison converted failure into a stepping stone to achievement while the others used it as an alibi for not producing results.”

“爱迪生把失败变成了成功的垫脚石，而其他人则把它当成了没有结果的托辞。”

How are you dealing with failure in your life?

你是如何面对生活中的失败的？

A One of my most effective tricks is known to you as propaganda. This is the instrument of greatest value to me in setting people to murdering one another under the guise of war.

我最有效的伎俩之一就是你们所知道的宣传。这是我最有价值的工具，可以让人们在战争的幌子下互相残杀。

The cleverness of this trick consists mainly of the subtlety with which I use it.

这个小把戏的巧妙之处主要在于我使用它的微妙之处。

I mix propaganda with the news of the world. I have it taught in public and private schools. I see that it finds its way into the pulpit. I color moving pictures with it. I see that it enters every home where there is a radio. I inject it into billboard, newspaper, and radio advertising. I spread it in every place of business where people work. I use it to fill the divorce courts and I make it serve to destroy business and industry.

我把宣传和世界新闻混在一起。我在公立和私立学校教授这门课程。我看到它进入了讲坛。我用它给活动的图片上色。我看到它进入每个有收音机的家庭。我把它注入到广告牌、报纸和广播广告中。我把它传播到每一个人们工作的地方。我用它来填满离婚法庭，我用它来摧毁商业和工业。

It is my chief instrument for starting runs on banks. My propagandists cover the world so thoroughly that I can start epidemics of disease, turn loose the dogs of war, or throw business into a panic at will.

它是我启动银行挤兑的主要工具。我的宣传工作覆盖了整个世界，以至于我可以随心所欲地引发疾病流行，释放战争之犬，或者让企业陷入恐慌。

Q If you can do all that you claim with propaganda, it is little wonder that we have wars and business depressions. Give me a simple description of what you mean by the term “propaganda.” Just what is it and how does it work? I wish to know particularly how you cause people to drift through the use of this devilish device.

问: 如果你可以通过宣传做到你所说的一切，那么战争和商业萧条也就不足为奇了。请简单描述一下你所说的“宣传”是什么意思它到底是什么，它是如何工作的？我特别想知道你是如何通过使用这个邪恶的装置使人们产生漂移的。

A Propaganda is any device, plan, or method by which people can be influenced without knowing that they are being influenced, or the source of the influence.

宣传是任何一种手段、计划或方法，通过这种手段、计划或方法，人们可以在不知道自己受到影响的情况下受到影响，或者不知道影响的来源。

Propaganda is used in business for the purpose of discouraging competition. Employers use it to gain advantage over their employees. The employees retaliate by using it to gain advantage over their employers. In fact, it is used so universally and through such a smooth and beautiful streamlined technique that it looks harmless even when it is detected.

在商业中进行宣传是为了阻止竞争。雇主利用它来获得对雇员的优势。雇员们利用这一点来报复他们的雇主。事实上，它是如此普遍的使用，并通过这样一个平滑和美丽的流线型技术，它看起来无害，即使它被检测到。

Q I suppose some of your boys are now engaged in preparing the minds of the American people to drift into some form of dictatorship. Tell me how they work.

问: 我想你们的一些人现在正在准备让美国人民的思想进入某种形式的独裁统治。告诉我它们是怎么工作的。

A Yes! Millions of my boys are preparing Americans to become Hitlerized. My best boys are working through politics and labor organization. We intend to take over the country with ballots instead of bullets. Americans are so sensitive they would never stand the shock of seeing their form of government changed with the aid of machine guns and tank cars. So our propaganda boys are serving them a diet they will swallow, by stirring up strife between employers and employees and turning the government against business and industry. When propaganda has done its work thoroughly, one of my boys will move in as dictator and the Nine Old Men on your Supreme Court with their silly notions of the Constitution will move out! Everyone will be given a job or fed from the government treasury. When men’s bellies are filled, they drift freely with one who does the filling. Hungry men get out from under control.

A 是的！我的数百万儿子正在为美国人成为希特勒做准备。我最好的孩子们在政界和劳工组织工作。我们打算用选票而不是子弹来接管这个国家。美国人是如此敏感，以至于他们永远不会承受看到他们的政府形式在机关枪和坦克车的帮助下发生改变所带来的震惊。因此，我们的宣传小子们正在为他们提供他们能接受的饮食，煽动雇主和雇员之间的冲突，让政府反对企业和工业。当宣传工作完成后，我的一个孩子将以独裁者的身份入住，你们最高法院的九个老人将带着他们愚蠢的宪法观念离开！每个人都将得到一份工作，或者从政府财政部获得粮食。当人们的肚子被填满时，他们就可以随心所欲地和填饱肚子的人在一起。饥饿的人们摆脱了控制。

In 1938, one of the Devil’s tools for “Hitlerizing” America was “turning the government against business and industry” and feeding the populace from the government treasury. Is that still the case today? Is the Devil succeeding? Were Napoleon Hill to interview the Devil today, the Devil might well gloat over the so-called “entitlement” programs now in place or proposed and crow over the government’s increasing involvement in independent businesses, such as the automotive and financial industries.

1938年，魔鬼用来“希特勒化”美国的工具之一就是“让政府反对商业和工业” ，并从政府财政中为民众提供食物。现在还是这样吗？魔鬼成功了吗？如果拿破仑 · 希尔(Napoleon Hill)今天采访魔鬼，魔鬼很可能会幸灾乐祸地看着所谓的“权利”计划，或者对政府越来越多地参与独立企业(如汽车业和金融业)的提议沾沾自喜。

Q I have often wondered who invented the clever trick which you call propaganda. From what you tell me of its source and nature I understand why it is so deadly. Only one as clever as Your Majesty could have invented such a device with which to dull the reason, dethrone the will, and lure men into drifting.

问: 我经常想知道是谁发明了这个聪明的把戏，你们称之为宣传。从你告诉我它的来源和性质，我明白了它为什么如此致命。只有像陛下这样聪明的人才能发明出这样的装置，用来蒙蔽理智，推翻意志，引诱人们漂流。

Why do you not use your powerful propaganda to gain control of your victims instead of subduing them through fear and annihilating them through warfare?

你为什么不用你强大的宣传来控制你的受害者，而不是通过恐惧征服他们，通过战争消灭他们？

A What is fear of the Devil except propaganda? You have not observed my technique very carefully or you would have seen that I am the world’s greatest propagandist! I never attain an end by direct, open means which I can achieve through subterfuge and subtlety.What do you suppose I am using, when I plant negative ideas in the minds of men and gain control of them through what they believe to be their own ideas? What would you call that except the cleverest of all forms of propaganda?

A 除了宣传，对魔鬼的恐惧还有什么？你没有仔细观察我的技巧，否则你会看到我是世界上最伟大的宣传家！我从来没有通过直接、公开的方式达到目的，而这种方式是我可以通过诡计和微妙的手段来达到的。当我把消极的想法植入人们的头脑，并通过他们认为是他们自己的想法来控制他们的时候，你认为我在使用什么？除了所有形式的宣传中最聪明的一种，你还能称之为什么呢？

Q Surely you are not going to tell me that you destroy people through their own help without their realizing what you are doing?

问: 你肯定不会告诉我，你通过人们自己的帮助来摧毁他们，而他们却没有意识到你在做什么？

A That is exactly what I wish you to understand. Moreover, I will show you exactly how the trick is performed.

A 这正是我希望你能理解的。此外，我将向您展示这个技巧是如何实施的。

Q Now we are getting somewhere. Exactly how do you convert human beings into propagandists and lure them into self-imprisonment? Give me the story with all its lurid details. This is the most important part of your confession and I am consumed with eagerness to gain control of your secret. I can hardly blame you for stalling about answering my question because you know so well that your answer will snatch millions of innocent victims from your control. You also know that your answer will protect other countless millions of yet unborn people from being victimized by you. It is little wonder you are hedging about answering.

现在我们有了一些进展。你究竟是如何将人类转变成宣传者并诱使他们自我监禁的呢？告诉我这个故事所有耸人听闻的细节。这是你忏悔中最重要的部分，我渴望控制你的秘密。我不能责怪你迟迟不回答我的问题，因为你知道你的回答会使数百万无辜的受害者脱离你的控制。你也知道，你的答案将保护其他无数尚未出生的人免受你的伤害。难怪你避而不答。

A Your deductions are correct. This part of my confession will do me more damage than all the remainder of it.

A 你的推理是正确的。我这一部分的坦白比其余部分对我造成的伤害更大。

Q Stating your headache in a better way, this part of your confession will save more millions of people from your control than all the remainder of it.

问: 用一种更好的方式来说明你的头痛，你的这部分忏悔会比其他所有的忏悔节省更多的人。

A All I can say is that you have me in a hell of a situation!

A 我所能说的就是，你让我陷入了一个糟糕的境地！

Q Now you shall know how the millions of your victims feel. Let’s have it.

现在你应该知道数以百万计的受害者的感受了。说吧。

A I make my first entry into an individual’s mind by bribing him.

A 我第一次进入一个人的思想是通过贿赂他。

Q What do you use as a bribe?

你用什么作为贿赂？

A I use many things, all of them pleasant things the individual covets. I use the same sort of bribes that individuals use when they bribe one another. That is, I use for bribes the things people most want. My best bribes are these:

我用了很多东西，都是个人垂涎的好东西。我使用的贿赂方式与个人行贿时使用的方式是一样的。也就是说，我用人们最想要的东西来行贿。我最好的行贿方式是:

• Love

•爱

• The thirst for sex expression

•对性表达的渴望

• Covetousness for money

•对金钱的贪婪

• The obsessive desire to gain something for nothing—gambling

•不劳而获的强迫性欲望ーー赌博

• Vanity in women, egotism in men

•女性的虚荣心，男性的自我中心

In today’s environment, clearly both women and men can fall victim to both vanity and egotism.

在今天的环境下，很明显，女人和男人都会成为虚荣和自我主义的牺牲品。

• Desire to be the master of others

•渴望成为他人的主人

• Desire for intoxicants and narcotics

‧对麻醉品和毒品的欲望

• Desire for self-expression through words and deeds

•通过言行表达自我的愿望

• Desire to imitate others

•模仿他人的欲望

• Desire for perpetuation of life after death

•希望死后永生的愿望

• Desire to be a hero or heroine

•渴望成为男主角或女主角

• Desire for physical food

•对实体食物的渴望

Q That is an imposing list of bribes, Your Majesty. Do you use others?

陛下，这可是一大笔贿赂，你用别人的钱吗？

A Yes, plenty of them, but these are my favorites. Through some combination of them I can enter the mind of any human being at will at any age from birth until death.

A 是的，很多，但这些是我最喜欢的。通过它们的组合，我可以随意进入任何人的思想，从出生到死亡，任何年龄。

Q You mean that these bribes are the keys with which you can silently unlock the door to any mind you choose?

问: 你的意思是这些贿赂是钥匙，你可以用它悄无声息地打开任何你选择的心灵之门？

A That is exactly what I mean and I can do it too.

A 这正是我的意思，我也能做到。

Q What happens when you enter the mind of a person who is not yet in the habit of drifting, but belongs in the 98 percent class as a potential drifter?

问: 当你进入一个还没有漂泊习惯，但是属于98% 的潜在漂泊者的心灵时，会发生什么？

A I go to work immediately to occupy as much of that person’s mind as I can master. If the individual’s greatest weakness is the desire for money, I begin to dangle coins before him, figuratively speaking. I intensify his desire and induce him to go after money. Then when he gets near it I snatch it away from him.

A 我立刻开始工作，尽可能多地占据那个人的思想。如果一个人最大的弱点是对金钱的渴望，我开始在他面前晃动硬币，比喻性地说。我强化了他的欲望，诱使他去追求金钱。然后当他靠近它的时候，我从他手里抢走了它。

This is an old trick of mine. After the trick has been repeated a few times, the poor fellow gives in and quits. Then I take over a little more space in his mind and fill it with the fear of poverty. That is one of my best mind-fillers.

这是我的一个老把戏。这个把戏重复了几次之后，这个可怜的家伙屈服了，放弃了。然后我在他的脑海中占据了更多的空间，并用对贫穷的恐惧填满了这个空间。这是我最好的心灵填充剂之一。

Q Yes, I admit your method is very clever, but what happens if the victim fools you and gets his hands on a lot of money? You don’t fill his mind with fear of poverty then, do you?

问: 是的，我承认你的方法非常聪明，但是如果受害者愚弄了你并且得到了一大笔钱会发生什么呢？那么你不会让他满脑子都是对贫穷的恐惧吧？

A No, I don’t. I take over the space by filling it with something which serves my purpose just as well. If my victim converts his desire for money into large sums, I start over-feeding him with the things he can buy with it. For example, I cause him to stuff himself with rich foods. This slows down his thinking capacity, endangers his heart, and starts him on the road to drifting.

A 不，我不知道。我接管了这个空间，用一些符合我目的的东西来填充它。如果我的受害者将他对金钱的渴望转化为大量的金钱，我就开始过度喂养他用这些钱可以买到的东西。例如，我让他吃了很多油腻的食物。这减缓了他的思考能力，危及了他的心灵，使他开始漂泊。

Then I pester him with intestinal poisoning through the surplus food he eats. That also slows down his thinking and gives him a nasty disposition.

然后我通过他吃剩下的食物让他肠道中毒。这也减缓了他的思考，给了他一个讨厌的脾气。

Q What if the victim is not a glutton? What other follies can you induce him to pick up that lead to drifting?

问: 如果受害者不是贪食者怎么办？你还能说服他接受哪些其他的愚蠢行为导致他漂泊不定呢？

A If the victim is a male I can usually snare him through his sex appetite. Over-indulgence in sex starts more men to drifting toward failure than all other causes combined.

如果受害者是男性，我通常可以通过他的性欲诱惑他。过度放纵的性生活比其他所有原因加起来还要让更多的男人开始走向失败。

Q So food and sex are two of your sure-fire baits! Is that correct?

问: 所以食物和性是你的两个必杀诱饵，对吗？

A Yes. With these two lures I can take over a majority of my victims, and then there is the desire for money.

A 是的。通过这两种诱饵，我可以控制大部分受害者，然后就是对金钱的渴望。

Q I am beginning to think that wealth is more dangerous than poverty, if your story is to be believed.

问: 如果你的故事可信的话，我开始认为财富比贫穷更危险。

A That altogether depends upon who has the wealth and how it was acquired.

这完全取决于谁拥有财富以及财富是如何获得的。

Q What has the manner in which money is acquired to do with its being a blessing or a curse?

问: 获得金钱的方式与它是祝福还是诅咒有什么关系？

A Everything. If you don’t believe me, take a look at those who acquire a large amount of money quickly, without time to get wisdom along with it, and observe how they use it.

A 一切。如果你不相信我，那就看看那些没有时间去获取智慧，却能很快获得大量金钱的人，然后观察他们是如何使用这些钱的。

Why, do you suppose, rich men’s sons seldom equal the achievements of their fathers? I’ll tell you why. It is because they have been deprived of the self-discipline which comes from being forced to work.

你认为，为什么富人的儿子很少能与他们父亲的成就相比呢？我来告诉你为什么。这是因为他们被剥夺了被迫工作而产生的自律。

Look into the records of moving picture stars or athletes who suddenly find themselves in possession of big money and hero worship and praise from the public. Observe how quickly I move in and take them over in many cases, mainly through sex, gambling, food, and liquor. With these I catch and control the biggest and the best of people as soon as they get their hands on big money.

看看电影明星或运动员的记录，他们突然发现自己拥有大量的金钱和英雄崇拜和公众的赞扬。观察我是如何迅速地进入并且在许多情况下接管他们，主要是通过性、赌博、食物和酒精。有了这些，我就能抓住并控制那些最大、最优秀的人，只要他们一拿到大钱。

Think of the countless athletes who have become mega-celebrities only to crash and burn from their fast money and fame . . . and then think of the millions of young people who looked up to them! Think of lottery winners who end up losing all their money within just a few years after they win the lottery . . . could it be from drifting . . . a fall-out from gambling? Could these cycles be orchestrated by the Devil?

想想那些无数的运动员，他们已经成为了超级名人，但是却因为他们的暴利和名声而毁于一旦... ... 然后想想那些数以百万计的年轻人，他们都很尊敬他们！想想彩票中奖者，他们在赢得彩票后的几年内就失去了他们所有的钱... 会不会是因为漂移... 赌博引起的失败？这些循环会不会是魔鬼策划的呢？

Q What about those who acquire money slowly, by rendering some form of useful service? Are they easily snared too?

问: 那些通过提供某种形式的有用服务慢慢获得金钱的人呢? 他们也很容易陷入困境吗？

A Oh, I get them all right, but I generally have to change my bait. Some of them want one thing and others want something else.

A 哦，我知道他们的意思，但通常我必须改变我的诱饵。他们中的一些人想要一样东西，另一些人想要别的东西。

Where my purpose is best served I see to it that they get what they want most, but I manage to wrap in the package something they don’t want. The thing I give them is the definite thing that makes them drifters. Do you see how I work?

在我的目的达到最好的地方，我会确保他们得到他们最想要的东西，但是我会设法把他们不想要的东西包起来。我给他们的东西是使他们成为漂泊者的明确的东西。你知道我是怎么工作的吗？

Q And very clever work it is. You lure people on through their natural desires, but you slip your deadly poison into the object of those desires wherever you can.

问: 这是一个非常聪明的工作。你通过人们的自然欲望来诱惑他们，但是你把你致命的毒药注入到那些欲望的对象中，无论你在哪里。

A Now you are catching on. You see, I play both ends against the middle, so to speak.

A 现在你明白了。你看，可以这么说，我是两头对着中间。

Q From all you say I infer that you cannot induce a non-drifter to help you gain control of his mind by baiting him with your bribes. Is that correct?

从你所说的一切，我推断你不能通过贿赂诱使一个非流浪汉来帮助你控制他的思想。是这样吗？

A That is exactly correct. I can—and I do—interest non-drifters in my bribes, because I use for the purpose of bribery the things all people naturally desire, but the non-drifter resembles a fish that steals the bait from your hook but refuses to take the hook.

A 完全正确。我可以——而且我确实对“无漂者”感兴趣，因为我的目的是贿赂所有人自然想要的东西，但“无漂者”就像一条鱼，从你的鱼钩上偷了鱼饵却拒绝上钩。

The non-drifter takes from life whatever he wants, but he takes it on his own terms. The drifter takes whatever he can get, but he takes what he gets on my terms.

非流浪汉从生活中得到他想要的一切，但是他用自己的方式得到它。那个流浪汉能得到什么就拿什么，但他得到什么就按我的条件拿。

Stating the matter in another way, the non-drifter borrows money from a legitimate banker, if he wants it, and pays a legitimate rate of interest. The drifter goes to the pawn shop, hocks his watch, and pays a suicidal rate of interest for his loan.

换句话说，非流浪汉向合法的银行家借钱，如果他想要的话，并支付合法的利率。这个流浪汉去了当铺，用手表抵押了他的贷款，并支付了一个自杀性的利率。

Q So I draw from your claims the conclusion that your hand is mixed up somehow in all of people’s troubles and miseries, even though your presence may not be visible?

问: 那么，我从你的说法中得出结论，你的手不知怎么地卷入了人们所有的麻烦和苦难，即使你的存在可能看不见？

A My unwilling workers are often my best workers. You see, my unwilling workers are those whom I cannot control with some combination of bribes, people whom I have to master by fear or through some form of misfortune. They do not wish to serve me, but they cannot avoid it because they are eternally bound to me by the habit of drifting.

A 我不情愿的工人常常是我最好的工人。你看，我不情愿的工人是那些我不能用贿赂来控制的人，是那些我必须用恐惧或某种形式的不幸来控制的人。他们不愿意为我服务，但他们不能逃避，因为他们总是因为漂泊的习惯而永远与我联系在一起。

Q Now I am beginning to better understand your technique. You bribe your victims through their natural desires and lead them astray while you induce them to become drifters if they respond to your lure. If they refuse to respond, you plant the seed of fear in their minds or trap them through some form of misfortune, and hog-tie them while they are down. Is that your method?

现在我开始更好地理解你的技巧了。你通过受害者的自然欲望贿赂他们，引导他们误入歧途，如果他们对你的诱惑做出反应，你就诱使他们成为流浪者。如果他们拒绝回应，你就在他们的头脑中播下恐惧的种子，或者通过某种形式的不幸困住他们，在他们低落的时候把他们绑起来。这就是你的方法吗？

A That is exactly the way I work. Clever, don’t you think?

A 那正是我工作的方式. 聪明，你不觉得吗？

Q Which do you prefer to serve as your propagandists—the young or the old?

问: 你更喜欢哪一个角色作为你的宣传者? 年轻人还是老年人？

A The young, of course! They can be influenced by most bribes more easily than people of mature judgment. Moreover, they have longer to remain in my service.

A 当然是年轻人！他们比有成熟判断力的人更容易受到大多数贿赂的影响。此外，他们还有更长的时间为我服务。

Q Your Majesty has given me a clear description of drifting. Tell me what must be done to insure against the habit of drifting. I want a complete formula that anyone can use.

女王陛下已经向我清楚地描述了漂泊。告诉我必须采取什么措施来防止漂泊的习惯。我想要一个完整的公式，任何人都可以使用。

A Protection against drifting lies within easy reach of every human being who has a normal body and a sound mind. The self-defense can be applied through these simple methods:

防止漂泊的保护措施是每个身体正常、心智健全的人都可以轻易得到的。自卫可以通过以下简单方法实施:

1. Do your own thinking on all occasions. The fact that human beings are given complete control over nothing save the power to think their own thoughts is laden with significance.

1.在任何场合都要有自己的想法。事实上，除了思考自己的思想之外，人类完全可以控制任何事物，这一事实充满了意义。

2. Decide definitely what you want from life; then create a plan for attaining it and be willing to sacrifice everything else, if necessary, rather than accept permanent defeat.

图2。明确地决定你想从生活中得到什么; 然后制定一个实现它的计划，如果必要的话，愿意牺牲一切，而不是接受永久的失败。

3. Analyze temporary defeat, no matter of what nature or cause, and extract from it the seed of an equivalent advantage.

图3。分析暂时的失败，不管是什么性质或原因，并从中提取相应优势的种子。

4. Be willing to render useful service equivalent to the value of all material things you demand of life, and render the service first.

图4。愿意提供相当于你生活中所需要的一切物质价值的有用服务，并且首先提供服务。

5. Recognize that your brain is a receiving set that can be attuned to receive communications from the universal storehouse of Infinite Intelligence, to help you transmute your desires into their physical equivalent.

5.认识到你的大脑是一个接收装置，可以调谐接收来自宇宙无限智慧仓库的通信，帮助你将你的欲望转化为它们的物理等价物。

6. Recognize that your greatest asset is time, the only thing except the power of thought which you own outright, and the one thing which can be shaped into whatever material things you want. Budget your time so none of it is wasted.

图6。认识到你最大的财富是时间，除了你完全拥有的思想的力量以外，唯一可以被塑造成你想要的任何物质的东西。安排好你的时间，这样就不会浪费时间。

7. Recognize the truth that fear generally is a filler with which the Devil occupies the unused portion of your mind. It is only a state of mind which you can control by filling the space it occupies with faith in your ability to make life provide you with whatever you demand of it.

图7。认识到恐惧通常是魔鬼占据你心灵未使用部分的填充物这一事实。它只是一种你可以控制的精神状态，只要你相信自己有能力让生活为你提供任何你想要的东西。

8. When you pray, do not beg! Demand what you want and insist upon getting exactly that, with no substitutes.

8. 当你祈祷的时候，不要乞求! 要求你想要的，并且坚持要得到你想要的，没有替代品。

9. Recognize that life is a cruel taskmaster and that either you master it or it masters you. There is no half-way or compromising point. Never accept from life anything you do not want. If that which you do not want is temporarily forced upon you, you can refuse, in your own mind, to accept it and it will make way for the thing you do want.

图9。认识到生活是一个残酷的工头，你要么主宰它，要么被它主宰。没有折衷或妥协的地方。不要从生活中接受任何你不想要的东西。如果你不想要的东西暂时强加在你身上，你可以在你自己的心里拒绝接受它，它将为你想要的东西让路。

10. Lastly, remember that your dominating thoughts attract, through a definite law of nature, by the shortest and most convenient route, their physical counterpart. Be careful what your thoughts dwell upon.

图10。最后，请记住，你的主导思想通过一个明确的自然法则，以最短和最方便的路线，吸引他们的物理对应物。要小心你的思想停留在什么上。

Q That list looks imposing. Give me a simple formula, combining all the ten points. If you had to combine all ten in one, what would it be?

问: 那个名单看起来很壮观。给我一个简单的公式，把所有的十点都结合起来。如果你必须把所有的十个放在一起，你会选择什么？

A Be definite in everything you do and never leave unfinished thoughts in the mind. Form the habit of reaching definite decisions on all subjects.

对你做的每件事都要明确，不要把未完成的想法留在头脑里。养成在所有问题上做出明确决定的习惯。

Q Can the habit of drifting be broken, or does it become permanent once it has been formed?

问: 漂泊的习惯能够被打破吗? 或者一旦形成就会变成永久的习惯吗？

A The habit can be broken if the victim has enough will power, providing it is done in time. There is a point beyond which the habit can never be broken. Beyond that point the victim is mine. He resembles a fly that has been caught in a spider’s web. He may struggle, but he cannot get out. Each move he makes entangles him more securely. The web in which I entangle my victims permanently is a law of nature not yet isolated by, or understood by, men of science.

如果受害者有足够的意志力，这个习惯可以被打破，前提是及时完成。有一个临界点，超过这个临界点，习惯就永远无法改变。除此之外，受害者是我的。他就像一只被蜘蛛网缠住的苍蝇。他可能挣扎，但他出不去。他的每一个动作都让他更安全地被困住。我将受害者永久纠缠在一张网中，这是一条自然法则，科学家们尚未孤立或理解它。





Chapter Six

HYPNOTIC RHYTHM

第六章催眠的节奏

Q WHAT IS THIS MYSTERIOUS LAW through which you take permanent control of people’s bodies even before you take over their souls? The whole world will want to know more about this law and how it operates.

问: 在你接管别人的灵魂之前，你就通过这个神秘的法则来永久控制他们的身体，这个法则是什么？全世界都想知道更多关于这项法律的信息，以及它是如何运作的。

A It will be hard to describe the law so you will understand it, but you may call it “hypnotic rhythm.” It is the same law through which people can be hypnotized.

A 很难描述这个规律，所以你会理解它，但你可以称之为“催眠的节奏”这是同样的法律，人们可以通过催眠。

Q So you have the power to use the laws of nature as a web in which you bind your victims in eternal control. Is that your claim?

问: 所以你有能力利用自然法则作为一张网，把你的受害者绑在永恒的控制中。这是你的要求吗？

A That is not only my claim. It is the truth! I take over their minds and bodies even before they die whenever I can lure them or frighten them into hypnotic rhythm.

A 这不仅是我的要求。这是事实！在他们死之前，只要我能引诱或恐吓他们进入催眠状态，我就会控制他们的思想和身体。

Q What is hypnotic rhythm? How do you use it to gain permanent mastery over human beings?

什么是催眠节奏? 你如何使用它来获得对人类的永久掌控？

A I will have to go back into time and space and give you a brief elementary description of how nature uses hypnotic rhythm. Otherwise you will not be able to understand my description of how I use this universal law to control human beings.

答: 我将不得不回到时间和空间，给你一个简短的关于大自然如何使用催眠节奏的基本描述。否则你将无法理解我对于如何使用这个宇宙法则来控制人类的描述。

Q Go ahead, but keep your story confined to simple illustrations which come within the range of my own experience and knowledge of natural laws.

问: 继续，但是你的故事应该限制在简单的插图中，这些插图应该在我自己的经验和自然法则的知识范围内。

A Very well, I shall do my best. You, of course, know that nature maintains a perfect balance between all the elements and all the energy in the universe. You can see that the stars and the planets move with perfect precision, each one keeping its own place in time and space. You can see that the seasons of the year come and go with perfect regularity. You can see that an oak tree grows from an acorn and a pine grows from the seed of its ancestor. An acorn never produces a pine and a pine seed never produces an oak.

A 很好，我将尽力而为。当然，你知道大自然在宇宙中的所有元素和所有能量之间保持着完美的平衡。你可以看到，恒星和行星的运动非常精确，每个恒星和行星在时间和空间上都有自己的位置。你可以看到一年中的季节有规律地来来去去。你可以看到橡树是从橡实长出来的，而松树是从它祖先的种子长出来的。橡子生不出松树，松子生不出橡树。

These are simple things which anyone can understand; what one cannot see is the universal law through which nature maintains perfect balance throughout the myriad of universes.

这些都是任何人都能理解的简单事物; 但是人们看不到的是宇宙法则，通过这个法则，自然在无数的宇宙中保持着完美的平衡。

You earthbound caught a fragmentary glimpse of this great universal law when Newton discovered that it holds your earth in its position and causes all material objects to be attracted toward the center of the earth. He called the law gravitation.

当牛顿发现它使你的地球保持在它的位置，并且使所有的物质物体被吸引到地球的中心时，你在地球上捕捉到这个伟大的宇宙定律的一个零碎的一瞥。他称之为万有引力定律。

But he did not go far enough in his study of the law. If he had, he would have discovered that the same law which holds your earth in position and helps nature to maintain a perfect balance over the four dimensions—in which all matter and energy are contained—is the web in which I entangle and control the minds of human beings.

但他对法律的研究还不够深入。如果他这样做了，他就会发现，同样的法则，让你的地球保持位置，帮助自然在四个维度上保持完美的平衡---- 所有的物质和能量都包含在其中---- 是我纠缠和控制人类思想的网络。

Q Tell me more of this astounding law of hypnotic rhythm.

问: 告诉我更多关于这个令人震惊的催眠律的信息。

A As I have already stated, there is a universal form of energy with which nature keeps a perfect balance between all matter and energy. She makes specialized use of this universal building material by breaking it up into different wavelengths. The breaking-up process is carried on through habit.

正如我已经说过的，存在着一种普遍的能量形式，大自然借助这种能量在所有物质和能量之间保持着完美的平衡。她通过将这种通用的建筑材料分解成不同的波长，对其进行了专门的使用。分手的过程是通过习惯进行的。

You will better understand what I am trying to convey if I compare it with the method by which one learns to play music. At first the notes are memorized in the mind. Then they are related to one another through melody and rhythm. By repetition the melody and rhythm become fixed in the mind. Observe how relentlessly the musician must repeat a tune before he masters it. Through repetition the musical notes blend and then you have music.

如果我把我想要表达的东西和一个人学习演奏音乐的方法进行比较，你会更好地理解我想要表达的东西。起初，这些音符在脑海中被记住了。然后它们通过旋律和节奏相互联系。通过重复，旋律和节奏变得固定在头脑中。观察一下这个音乐家在掌握一首曲子之前是如何不屈不挠地重复它的。通过重复音符的混合，你就有了音乐。

Any impulse of thought that the mind repeats over and over through habit forms an organized rhythm. Undesirable habits can be broken. They must be broken before they assume the proportions of rhythm. Are you following me?

任何思想的冲动都会通过习惯一遍又一遍地重复，形成一种有组织的节奏。不良习惯是可以改掉的。在它们达到节奏的比例之前，必须先打破它们。你在跟踪我吗？

Q Yes.

问: 是的。

A Well, to continue, rhythm is the last stage of habit! Any thought or physical movement which is repeated over and over through the principle of habit finally reaches the proportion of rhythm.

A 好，继续，节奏是习惯的最后阶段！任何通过习惯原则反复重复的思想或身体运动最终达到节奏的比例。

Then the habit cannot be broken because nature takes it over and makes it permanent. It is something like a whirlpool in water. An object may keep floating indefinitely unless it is caught in a whirlpool. Then it is carried round and round but it cannot escape. The energy with which people think may be compared with water in a river.

那么习惯就不能被打破，因为大自然接管了它并使它永久化。它有点像水中的漩涡。一个物体可以无限期地漂浮，除非它被卷入漩涡。然后它被带来带去，但它无法逃脱。人们思考的能量可以与河流中的水相比。

Q So this is the way in which you take control of the minds of people, is it?

问: 这就是你控制人们思想的方式，是吗？

A Yes. All I have to do to gain control over any mind is to induce its owner to drift.

答: 是的。我所要做的就是引导它的主人漂移，从而控制任何思想。

Q Am I to understand that the habit of drifting is the major danger through which people lose their prerogative or privilege of thinking their own thoughts and shaping their own earthly destinations?

问: 我是否理解漂泊的习惯是主要的危险，人们因此失去了思考自己的想法和塑造自己的世俗目的地的特权或特权？

A That and much more. Drifting is also the habit through which I take over their souls after they give up their physical bodies.

A 那个，还有更多。漂泊也是一种习惯，在他们放弃肉体之后，我通过这种习惯接管了他们的灵魂。

Q Then the only way a human being can be saved from eternal annihilation is by maintaining control over his own mind while he is on this earth. Is that true?

那么人类能够从永恒的毁灭中被拯救出来的唯一方法就是当他在这个地球上的时候保持对他自己思想的控制。是真的吗？

A You have stated the truth perfectly! Those who control and use their own minds escape my web. I get all the others as naturally as the sun sets in the west.

A 你已经完全说出了真相！那些控制和使用自己思想的人逃离了我的网。其他的我都能像太阳在西边落下一样自然地得到。

Says the Devil: “Those who control and use their own minds escape my web.”

魔鬼说: “那些控制和使用他们自己思想的人逃脱了我的网。”

Q Is that all there is to the business of being saved from eternal annihilation? Doesn’t what you call your opposition have anything to do with saving people?

问: 从永恒的毁灭中被拯救出来，这就是全部吗？难道你所说的反对和拯救人类没有任何关系吗？

A I can see that you do think very deeply. My opposition— the power you earthbound call God—has everything to do with the salvation of people from eternal annihilation, and for that reason it is my opposition who provides every human being with the privilege of using his own mind.

A 我看得出你的确思考得很深刻。我的反对者——你们俗称为上帝的力量——与人类免遭永恒毁灭的救赎有着千丝万缕的联系，正是因为这个原因，我的反对者赋予了每个人使用自己思想的特权。

If you use that power by maintaining control over your own mind, you become a part of it when you give up your physical body. If you neglect to use it, then I have the privilege of taking advantage of the neglect through the law of hypnotic rhythm.

如果你通过控制自己的思想来使用这种力量，当你放弃你的肉体时，你就成为了它的一部分。如果你忽视了使用它，那么我就有特权通过催眠律法利用这种忽视。

Q How much of a person do you take over when you gain control of him?

问: 当你控制一个人的时候，你会控制他多少？

A Everything that is left after he ceases to control and use his own mind.

他停止控制和使用自己的思想后所剩下的一切。

Q In other words, when you gain control of a person you take over all there is of his individuality up to the time that he quits using his own mind? Is that correct?

换句话说，当你控制了一个人，你就控制了他的一切，直到他用自己的思想放弃的时候，他的个性还是存在的？是这样吗？

A That is how I operate.

A 这就是我的工作方式。

Q What do you do with people whom you control before death? Of what good are they to you while they live?

问: 你会怎么处理那些在你死之前被你控制的人？他们活着对你有什么好处？

A I use them, or what is left of than after I take charge, as propagandists to help me prepare the minds of others to drift.

我利用他们，或者说我掌权后剩下的东西，作为宣传工具，帮助我让别人的思想随波逐流。

Q You not only fool people into destroying their power to control their own minds, but you use them to help you trap others?

问: 你不仅愚弄人们摧毁他们的力量来控制自己的思想，而且还利用他们来帮助你困住别人？

A Yes, I let no opportunity get away from me.

A 是的，我没有让任何机会从我身边溜走。

Q Let us come back to the subject of hypnotic rhythm. Tell me more of how this law works. Show me how you use individuals to help you gain control over others. I want to know something of the most effective way you use hypnotic rhythm.

让我们回到催眠节律这个话题。告诉我更多这个法律是如何运作的。告诉我你是如何利用别人来帮助你控制别人的。我想知道使用安眠药的最有效的方法。

A Oh, that is easy! The thing I like best is to fill the minds of people with fear. Once I fill one’s mind with fear I have little trouble causing him to drift until I have entangled him in the web of hypnotic rhythm.

A 哦，那很简单！我最喜欢的事情就是用恐惧填满人们的心灵。一旦我用恐惧填满一个人的心灵，我很容易让他漂移，直到我把他困在催眠的节奏网中。

Q What human fear best serves your purpose?

问: 什么样的人类恐惧最符合你的目的？

A The fear of death.

A 对死亡的恐惧。

Q Why is the fear of death your favorite weapon?

为什么对死亡的恐惧是你最喜欢的武器？

A Because no one knows, and by the very nature of the laws of the universe, no one can prove definitely what happens after death. This uncertainty frightens people out of their wits.

答: 因为没有人知道，而且根据宇宙法则的本质，没有人能够确切地证明死后发生了什么。这种不确定性把人们吓得魂不附体。

People who give over their minds to fear—any sort of fear— neglect to use their minds and begin to drift. Eventually they drift into the whirlpool of hypnotic rhythm from which they may never escape.

那些放弃自己的思想去恐惧ーー任何形式的恐惧ーー的人忽视了运用自己的思想并开始漂泊。最终，他们进入了催眠节奏的漩涡，他们可能永远无法逃脱。

Q Then you do not mind what religious leaders think or say of you when they speak of death?

问: 那么你不介意宗教领袖在谈到死亡时对你的看法或说法吗？

A Not as long as they say something! If the churches should stop talking about me, my cause would receive a severe setback. Every attack made against me fixes the fear of me in the minds of all who are influenced by it. You see, opposition is the thing that keeps some people from drifting! Providing they do not yield to it.

A 只要他们说点什么就不会！如果教会不再谈论我，我的事业就会受到严重的挫折。对我的每一次攻击都会使所有受其影响的人心中对我的恐惧得到缓解。你看，对立是阻止一些人漂流的东西！只要他们不屈服于它。

Q Since you claim the churches help instead of hindering your cause, tell me what would give you cause to worry?

问: 既然你声称教会帮助而不是阻碍你的事业，告诉我你有什么理由担心？

A My only worry is that someday a real thinker may appear on earth.

A 我唯一担心的是，有一天地球上会出现一位真正的思想家。

Q What would happen if a thinker did appear?

问: 如果一个思想家真的出现了，会发生什么？

A You ask me what would happen? I’ll tell you what would happen. People would learn the greatest of all truths—that the time they spend in fearing something would, if reversed, give them all they want in the material world and save them from me after death. Isn’t that worth thinking about?

A 你问我会发生什么？我来告诉你会发生什么。人们会学到所有真理中最伟大的一条ーー他们花在害怕某件事上的时间，如果反过来，会给他们在物质世界里想要的一切，并在我死后把他们从我手中拯救出来。这难道不值得思考吗？

Says the Devil: “The time they [people] spend in fearing something would, if reversed, give them all they want in the material world and save them from me after death.”

魔鬼说: “他们(人们)花在害怕某事上的时间，如果反过来，会给他们在物质世界想要的一切，并在死后从我手中拯救他们。”

Q What is keeping such a thinker from appearing in the world?

问: 是什么阻止这样一位思想家出现在世界上？

A Fear of criticism! It may interest you to know that the fear of criticism is the only effective weapon I have with which to whip you. If you were not afraid to publish this confession after you wring it from me, I would lose my earthly kingdom.

害怕批评！你可能有兴趣知道，对批评的恐惧是我用来鞭打你的唯一有效武器。如果你在从我这里得到这份忏悔之后，还敢公开这份忏悔，我就会失去我的世俗王国。

Q And if I did surprise you and publish it, how long would it be until you lost your kingdom?

问: 如果我真的让你大吃一惊并且发表了它，那么多久你就会失去你的王国？

A Just long enough for one generation of children to grow into understanding. You cannot take the adults from me. I have them too securely sewed up. But if you published this confession, it would be sufficient to keep me from gaining control of the yet unborn and those who have not yet reached the age of reason. You wouldn’t dare publish what I have told you about the religious leaders. They would crucify you!

只够一代孩子长大成人的时间。你不能把大人们从我身边带走。我把它们缝得太牢了。但是，如果你公布了这个供词，那就足以使我无法控制尚未出生的人和那些尚未达到理智年龄的人。你不敢公开我告诉你的关于宗教领袖的事情。他们会把你钉死在十字架上！

Q I thought the savage practice of crucifixion went out of style two thousand years ago.

问: 我认为野蛮的钉十字架的行为在两千年前就已经过时了。

A I don’t mean crucifixion on a cross. I mean social and financial crucifixion. Your income would be shut off. You would become a social outcast. Religious leaders and their followers alike would treat you with scorn.

A 我不是说钉死在十字架上。我的意思是社会和金融的十字架。你的收入将被切断。你会成为社会的弃儿。宗教领袖和他们的追随者都会对你嗤之以鼻。

Q Suppose I should choose to throw in my lot with the select few who make a pretense of using their own minds rather than fear the masses who do not—the masses of whom you claim 98 percent?

问: 假如我选择把自己的命运交给那些假装使用自己思想的少数人，而不是害怕那些不使用自己思想的大众ーー那些你声称占98% 的大众？

A If you have courage enough to do this, you will crimp my style.

A 如果你有足够的勇气做这件事，你就会破坏我的风格。

A chill ran down my spine when I first read this . . . since circumstances did indeed prevent this manuscript, written in 1938, from being published until now, well after Hill’s death in 1970. Was the delayed publication of the work truly caused by his wife’s “fear of criticism” and concern over the reaction of religious leaders and public school advocates . . . or was it due to the work of the Devil himself? And now, the family and the Foundation have decided it is time to share the manuscript with the world. Shall we heed Hill’s wisdom, discover our “other selves,” and take control of our own minds, reclaiming our destiny?

当我第一次读到这篇文章的时候，我的脊背一阵寒意... ... 因为确实是环境阻止了这篇写于1938年的手稿的出版，直到现在，也就是在1970年希尔去世之后。推迟出版这部作品真的是因为他的妻子“害怕批评”和担心宗教领袖和公立学校倡导者的反应... ... 还是因为魔鬼自己的工作？现在，这个家庭和基金会决定是时候与世界分享这份手稿了。我们是否应该留意希尔的智慧，发现我们的“其他自我” ，控制我们自己的思想，重新掌握我们的命运？

Q Why do you lay claim to no scientist? Don’t you like scientists?

问: 你为什么声称没有科学家? 你不喜欢科学家吗？

A Oh yes, I like all people well enough, but true scientists are out of my reach.

A 哦，是的，我非常喜欢所有的人，但是真正的科学家是我力所不及的。

Q Why?

问: 为什么？

A Because they think for themselves and spend their time studying natural laws. They deal with cause and effect. They deal with facts wherever they find them. But do not make the mistake of believing scientists have no religion. They have a very definite religion.

A 因为他们独立思考，花时间研究自然法则。他们处理因果关系。无论他们在哪里发现事实，他们都会处理。但不要错误地认为科学家没有宗教信仰。他们有一个非常明确的宗教信仰。

Q What is their religion?

问: 他们的宗教是什么？

A The religion of truth! The religion of natural law! If the world ever produces an accurate thinker with ability to fathom the deeply buried secret of life and death, you can be sure that science will be responsible for the catastrophe.

A 真理的宗教！自然法则的宗教！如果这个世界曾经产生过一个精确的思想家，他有能力领悟深埋在地下的生与死的秘密，你可以肯定，科学将为这场灾难负责。

Q Catastrophe to whom?

谁的灾难？

A To me, of course!

A 当然是给我的！

Q Let’s get back to the subject of hypnotic rhythm. I want to know more about it. Is it something like the principle through which people can hypnotize one another?

让我们回到催眠节奏的话题。我想知道更多。它是否类似于人们可以相互催眠的原则？

A It is precisely the same thing. I have already told you so. Why do you repeat your questions?

A 完全是一回事。我已经告诉过你了。你为什么要重复你的问题呢？

Q That is an old worldly custom of mine, Your Majesty. For your enlightenment I will tell you I am forcing you to repeat many of your statements for the sake of emphasis. I am also trying to see if I can catch you in a lie! Don’t dodge the issue. Get back to hypnotic rhythm and tell me all you know about it. Am I a victim of it?

这是我的一个古老的世俗习惯，陛下。为了启迪你们，我将告诉你们，为了强调，我强迫你们重复许多你们的陈述。我也在试着看看我能不能抓住你的谎言！不要回避这个问题。回到催眠的节奏，告诉我你所知道的一切。我是它的受害者吗？

A Not now, but you barely missed falling into my web. You drifted toward the whirlpool of hypnotic rhythm, until you discovered how to force me into making this confession. Then I lost control of you!

A 不是现在，但你差点掉进我的网里。你飘向催眠律动的漩涡，直到你发现如何迫使我做出这样的忏悔。然后我失去了对你的控制！

Q How interesting. You are not trying to recapture me through flattery, are you?

问: 真有意思。你不是想通过拍马屁再次抓住我吧？

A That would be the best bribe I could offer you. It is the bribe I used on you effectively before you got the upper hand of me.

A 那将是我能给你的最好的贿赂。这是我在你占上风之前有效地用在你身上的贿赂。

Q With what did you flatter me?

问: 你用什么恭维我？

A With many things, chief among them sex and the desire for self-expression.

A 有很多事情，其中最主要的是性和自我表达的欲望。

Q What effect did your bribes have on me?

问: 你的贿赂对我有什么影响？

A They caused you to neglect your major purpose in life and started you to drifting.

它们使你忽视了你生活的主要目标，让你开始漂泊不定。

Q Was that all you did to me through your bribes?

问: 这就是你通过贿赂对我所做的一切吗？

A That was plenty.

A 那已经足够了。

Q But I am back on the track and out of your reach now, am I not?

问: 但是我现在回到了赛道上，而且已经超出了你的能力范围，对吗？

A Yes, you are temporarily out of my reach because you are not drifting.

A 是的，你暂时超出了我的能力范围，因为你没有漂流。

Q What broke your spell over me and released me from the habit of drifting?

问: 是什么打破了你对我的魔咒，让我摆脱了漂泊的习惯？

A My answer may humiliate you. Do you want to hear it?

A 我的回答可能会让你丢脸。你想听吗？

Q Go ahead and give it to me, Your Majesty. I wish to learn how much truth I can stand.

来吧，把它给我吧，陛下。我想知道我能承受多少真理。

A When you found a great love in the woman of your choice, I lost my grip on you.

当你在你选择的女人身上找到一份伟大的爱情时，我失去了对你的控制。

Q So you are going to accuse me of hiding behind a woman’s skirts, are you?

问: 所以你要指责我躲在一个女人的裙子后面，是吗？

A No, not hiding. I wouldn’t put it that way. I would say you have learned how to give yourself a solid background with the embellishment of a woman’s mind.

A 不，不是躲起来。我不会这么说。我想说，你已经学会了如何用女人的思想来为自己打造一个坚实的背景。

Q The woman’s skirt has nothing to do with it then?

问: 那女人的裙子和这件事没有关系吗？

A No, but her brain does. When you and your wife began to combine your two brains, through your habit of “Master Minding” every day, you stumbled upon the secret power with which you forced me into this confession.

A 不，但是她的大脑知道。当你和你的妻子开始结合你们两个的头脑，通过你们每天的习惯“思考大师” ，你们偶然发现了你们用来强迫我认罪的神秘力量。

Q Is that the truth, or are you trying to flatter me again?

问: 这是真的吗，还是你又在奉承我？

A I could flatter you if I had you alone, but I cannot flatter you while you have the use of your wife’s mind.

A 如果只有你一个人的话，我可以奉承你，但是如果你有你妻子的心思，我就不能奉承你了。

Q I am beginning to catch on to something important. I am beginning to understand what was meant by the writer of that passage in the Bible which says substantially, “When two or more meet together and ask for anything in My name, it shall be granted.” It is true, then, that two minds are better than one.

我开始明白一些重要的事情。我开始明白《圣经》中那段经文的作者的意思了，这段经文实质上说: “当两个或两个以上的人相遇，并以我的名求任何事，这事必得应许。”那么，两个心灵胜过一个心灵，这是事实。

A It is not only true, it is necessary before anyone can continuously contact the great storehouse of Infinite Intelligence wherein is stored all that is, all that ever was, and all that can ever be.

答: 这不仅是真的，而且在任何人能够不断地接触存储着一切现在、过去和未来的无限智慧的巨大仓库之前，这是必要的。

Q Is there such a storehouse?

问: 有这样的仓库吗？

A If there had not been, you would not—could not—now be humiliating me with this silly forced confession.

A 如果没有，你现在就不会ーー也不可能ーー用这种愚蠢的逼供来羞辱我了。

Q Isn’t it dangerous to give this sort of information to the world?

问: 把这种信息公之于众是不是很危险？

A Sure, it is dangerous to me. If I were you, I would not give it out.

A 当然，它对我来说很危险。如果我是你，我就不会把它给别人。

Q Let us get back, now, to the technique through which you fasten on your victims the habit of drifting. What is the very first step a drifter must take to break the habit?

现在让我们回到技巧上来，通过这个技巧，你把漂流的习惯强加在你的受害者身上。一个流浪汉打破这个习惯的第一步是什么？

A A burning desire to break it! You of course know that no one can be hypnotized by another person without his willingness to be hypnotized. The willingness may assume the form of indifference toward life generally, lack of ambition, fear, lack of definiteness of purpose, and many other forms. Nature does not need one’s consent in order to place him under the spell of hypnotic rhythm. It needs only to find him off guard, through any form of neglect to use his own mind.
